Rulings on Intercourse After Menstrual Cessation
Expansion of rulings on post-menses intercourse with three scenarios

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three scenarios of menses cessation and determine the permissibility of intercourse in each, applying the Hanafi principles of prayer time and precaution.

Core Idea
Intercourse after menses depends not only on ghusl but on prayer time and habit—precaution rules when uncertainty remains.

In this lesson, we delve into the detailed Hanafi rulings on when a husband may approach his wife after her menstruation stops. The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies that permissibility hinges on the timing of the cessation relative to prayer times and, in certain cases, on the woman's habitual cycle. We will trace the reasoning behind these distinctions and examine an internal Hanafi disagreement regarding the third, more cautious scenario.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three cessation scenarios
From the passage, extract the three cases: (1) cessation at the beginning or middle of a prayer time, (2) cessation at the end of a prayer time, and (3) cessation for less than ten days, less than her habit, but above three days.
Each scenario carries a different ruling regarding when intercourse becomes permissible.
2
Understand the prayer time condition
The passage stresses that the 'least prayer time' refers to the end of the time. If cessation occurs at the beginning, the entire time must pass; if at the end, she must have enough time for ghusl and the opening takbir before time expires.
This is because a prayer becomes a debt (dayn) on her once the time exits, and she must have had the opportunity to pray.
3
Analyze the third scenario and the precaution principle
The third scenario requires waiting until her habitual period passes, even if she performs ghusl. The reason is that blood may return, which is common in such cases. The principle of precaution (ihtiyat) dictates avoidance.
The wording 'he does not approach her' (la yaqrabha) in al-Hidayah implies prohibition.
4
Resolve the intra-Hanafi dispute
Some Hanafi sources (al-Nihayah, al-Kafi) state 'karahah' (dislike) for this case. The passage reconciles this: if karahah means prohibition (tahrimi), there is no conflict; if it means tanzihi, it contradicts al-Hidayah. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is prohibition.
The dispute illustrates how different wording can affect the ruling, and the author favours the prohibition view.

لا يوجب تأخر حق الزوج بعد القطع بارتفاع المانع ا هـ . فقوله وتطهرن بمعنى طهرن إلى آخره جواب سؤال تقديره أن هذا الحمل يرده قوله تعالى «فإذا تطهرن فإنه لم يقرأ إلا بالتشديد واعلم أن المراد بأدنى وقت وقت صلاة ناقصة كصلاة الضحى والعيد فإنه لا يجوز وطؤها حتى تغتسل أو يمضي عليها وقت صلاة الظهر ا هـ . وإنما عبر بعضهم بالأدنى ولم يقل مضي وقت صلاة نفياً لما قد. أن مضي الوقت كله والدم منقطع شرط للحل وليس زمان قدر الغسل والتحريمة وخرج الوقت حل وإلا فلا. وأما الثالث وهو ما إذا كان الانقطاع لما دون العشرة لأقل من العادة فوق الثلاث لم يقربها حتى تمضي عادتها وإن اغتسلت لأن العود في العادات غالب فكان الاحتياط في الاجتناب . كذا في الهداية . وصيغة لم يقربها وكذا التعليل بالاحتياط في الاجتناب يقتضي حرمة الوطء، وقد صرح به في غاية البيان، والمنصوص عليه في النهاية والكافي للنسفي كراهة الوطء فإن أريد بالكراهة التحريم فلا منافاة بين العبارتين وإلا فالمنافاة بينهما .ظاهرة وفي النهاية تأخير الغسل إلى آخر الوقت المستحب مستحب فيما إذا انقطع لتمام عادتها، وفيما إذا انقطع لأقلها واجب. وفي المبسوط : إذا انقطع لأقل من عشرة تنتظر إلى آخر الوقت المستحب دون المكروه.
يبعد أن «تفعل» يجيء بمعنى «فعل من غير أن يدل على صنيع قوله : (وفي المبسوط إذا انقطع الخ) ظاهره أنه لا فرق بين انقطاعه لأقل من عادتها أو لتمامها . ثم قوله تنتظر» ظاهره الوجوب ولا . يحمل على أقل العادة ليوافق ما في النهاية وما في معراج الدراية أيضاً حيث قال: قال الهندواني : تأخر الاغتسال في هذه الحالة بطريق الاستحباب وفيما دون عادتها بطريق الوجوب اهـ.
نص عليه محمد في الأصل قال : إذا انقطع في وقت العشاء تؤخر إلى وقت يمكنها أن تغتسل فيه وتصلي قبل انتصاف الليل وما بعد نصف الليل مكروه ا هـ . وفي فتح القدير: إن حكم الثالث خلاف إنهاء الحرمة بالغسل الثابت بقراءة التشديد فهو مخرج منه بالإجماع ا هـ . ويعارضه ما نقله في الغاية عن ابن تيمية أنه ذكر الإجماع على أنها تغتسل وتصلي ولا يحرم وطؤها كما في شرح منظومة ابن وهبان ولعله توهم من قول بعض الحنفية بالكراهة أنها كراهة تنزيه فنقل الإجماع على عدم الحرمة وإلا فلا يصح نقل الإجماع مع خلاف الحنفية كما لا يخفى.
The one whose temporary prohibition has ended by carrying that [reading] upon what is less than the majority, and this upon it. And 'yutahhirna' means 'taharna' because it comes in the pattern of 'takabbara' and 'ta'azzama' in His attributes, preserving the reality of 'yathurna' with tashdid. And all, though contrary to the apparent, but this is closer because it does not cause delay of the husband's right after certainty of removal of the impediment. His statement 'and they become pure' meaning 'they became pure' to the end is an answer to an implicit question: that this interpretation is rejected by His statement 'fa-idha tatahaharna' which is only recited with tashdid. And know that the intended by 'the least time of prayer' is its least that occurs last, i.e., that she appears in a time from it to its exit equal to performing ghusl and the tahrima, not more general than this. Or that she becomes pure at its beginning and this amount passes, because this does not render her legally pure, as I have seen some who err in this. Do you not see their reasoning that that prayer becomes a debt in her liability, and that by the exit of time. For that reason, more than one did not mention the word 'the least' and the expression of al-Kafi: 'or the prayer becomes a debt in her liability by the passing of the least time of prayer equal to ghusl and tahrima, by it stopping at the end of time' as in Fath al-Qadir. And what he said is correct, for I have also seen one who errs in this, and it is supported by what is in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: that if the cessation is at the beginning of time, it is not permissible to approach her except after ghusl or by the passing of all the time. And if it stops during a deficient prayer like duha or 'id prayer, it is not permissible to have intercourse with her until she performs ghusl or the time of zuhr prayer passes. And some expressed it as 'the least' and did not say 'passing of time of prayer' to negate what might occur, that passing of all time while blood is cut is a condition for permissibility—it is not so. Therefore, many commentators mistakenly thought that this is applied to when the cessation is at the end of time. The conclusion: if the cessation is at the beginning or middle of time, the exit of time is necessary for permissibility; if it is at the end, then if there remains from it a time equal to ghusl and tahrima and time exits, it is permissible; otherwise not. As for the third, which is when the cessation is for less than ten days, less than her habit but above three, he does not approach her until her habit passes even if she has performed ghusl, because return is frequent in habits, so precaution is in avoidance. This is in al-Hidayah. The wording 'he does not approach her' and similarly the reasoning by precaution in avoidance implies prohibition of intercourse, and it was explicitly stated in Ghayat al-Bayan. But what is prescribed in al-Nihayah and al-Kafi of al-Nasafi is dislike of intercourse. If by dislike is meant prohibition, there is no contradiction between the two expressions; otherwise the contradiction is apparent. In al-Nihayah: delaying ghusl to the end of the recommended time is recommended if cessation is at the end of her habit, and if cessation is less than her habit, it is obligatory. In al-Mabsut: if cessation is for less than ten, she waits until the end of the recommended time, not the disliked time. It is unlikely that 'yaf'alu' comes in the meaning of 'fa'ala' without indicating an action. His statement: (In al-Mabsut, if it stops, etc.) apparently no difference between stopping less than her habit or at its end. Then his statement 'she waits' apparently indicates obligation. And it is not carried upon less than her habit to agree with what is in al-Nihayah and what is in Mir'aj al-Dirayah also where he said: al-Hinduwani said: delaying ghusl in this case is by way of recommendation, and in less than her habit by way of obligation. Muhammad stated in al-Asl: if it stops at the time of 'isha, she delays until a time in which she can perform ghusl and pray before midnight, and after midnight is disliked. In Fath al-Qadir: the ruling of the third case is opposed to the ending of prohibition by ghusl established by the reading with tashdid, so it is excluded from it by consensus. And this is contradicted by what was transmitted in al-Ghayah from Ibn Taymiyyah that he mentioned consensus that she performs ghusl and prays and her intercourse is not prohibited, as in Sharh Manzumah Ibn Wahban. Perhaps he misunderstood from the statement of some Hanafis of dislike that it is a dislike of tanzih, so he transmitted consensus on non-prohibition; otherwise, transmission of consensus with Hanafi opposition is not valid, as is not hidden.
Source pages p. 353

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion of the ruling on when a woman becomes permissible for intercourse after her menstruation ceases. It begins by addressing a textual issue: the word 'yutahhirna' in the Quran (2:222) can be read with tashdid (emphasis) or takhfif. The author argues that reading with takhfif in the context of His attributes is more consistent, but the common reading is with tashdid. The main point is that the least prayer time referred to is the end of the prayer time, not the beginning. If the bleeding stops at the beginning or middle of a prayer time, intercourse is not permissible until the entire time passes, because the prayer becomes a debt on her. If it stops at the end and there remains enough time for ghusl and the opening takbir, then she must perform ghusl and pray before time ends; intercourse is then permissible. If not enough time remains, she must wait until the next prayer time. The third case is when bleeding stops for less than ten days but less than her habit and more than three. Here, out of precaution, she should not be approached until her habit passes, even if she performs ghusl. There is a difference of opinion among Hanafi scholars whether this is prohibition or disliked. The passage clarifies that depending on the cessation scenario, delaying ghusl may be obligatory or recommended. The text also includes a note from Muhammad al-Shaybani about a specific case with 'isha prayer time, and a discussion of a claimed consensus that intercourse is not prohibited in the third case, which is contradicted by Hanafi positions.

Key Terms
أدنى وقت الصلاة (adna waqt al-salat): The least prayer time specifically referring to the end of the prayer time, not the beginning.
التحريمة (al-tahrima): The opening takbir of the prayer, used as a measure for the duration needed after menses cessation.
الاحتياط (al-ihtiyat): Precaution; in this context, avoiding intercourse in the third case due to likelihood of return of blood.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the third case (cessation for less than ten days, less than her habit, above three), when does intercourse become permissible?
A) Immediately after ghusl
B) After her habitual menses period passes
C) At the end of the prayer time
D) After tayammum

Key Takeaway
Intercourse after menses is not simply permitted by ghusl; it depends on prayer time and, in uncertain cases, on the woman's habitual cycle, with the principle of precaution prohibiting approach until the habit passes.

Tayammum and Permissibility of Intercourse After Menses
Intra-Hanafi dispute on tayammum and intercourse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on whether tayammum without prayer permits intercourse and identify the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Tayammum alone does not permit intercourse; prayer confirms purity.

This lesson examines a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute: a woman who becomes pure from menses, performs tayammum due to lack of water, then finds water before praying. The core question is whether her husband may approach her before she prays. We will explore the arguments of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani, and see why the relied-upon view prohibits approach.

Guided Path
1
State the Issue
Identify the scenario: a woman purifies from menses, does tayammum (no water), then finds water before praying. Is intercourse permissible without prayer?
The key factor is that tayammum precedes prayer.
2
Identify the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
List the positions: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf prohibit approach; Muhammad permits it. Note the basis for each.
Muhammad analogizes tayammum to ghusl for precautionary matters.
3
Analyze the Proofs
Understand the dalil: Muhammad argues tayammum removes the state of menses like ghusl, so the prohibition of intercourse lifts. The majority counter that tayammum before prayer is not confirmed; precaution dictates avoidance.
Reference al-Mabsut's reasoning that Muhammad's analogy is limited to precautionary matters like cutting the right of return.
4
Determine the Tarjih
The most correct view (al-sahih) is prohibition according to all three imams, because Muhammad's permission is based on a precautionary analogy that does not extend to intercourse.
The author sides with the majority; Qadi al-Isbijabi's claim of consensus is rejected.
5
Apply to Mufta Bihi
The operative ruling (mufta bihi): tayammum without prayer does not make intercourse permissible. The husband must wait until she prays.
This is the position for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي التنجيس: مسافرة طهرت من الحيض فتيممت ثم وجدت ماء جاز للزوج أن يقربها لكن لا تقرأ القرآن لأنها لما تيممت خرجت من الحيض. فلما وجدت الماء فإنما وجب عليها الغسل فصارت كالجنب ا هـ . وظاهره أن التيمم من غير صلاة يخرجها من الحيض فيجوز قربانها وليس كذلك فقد قال في المبسوط : ولم يذكر يعني الحاكم الشهيد في الكافي ما إذا تيممت ولم تصل، فقيل هو على الاختلاف عندهما ليس للزوج أن يقربها، وعند محمد له ذلك، والأصح أنه ليس له أن يقربها عندهم جميعاً لأن محمداً إنما جعل التيمم كالاغتسال فيما هو مبني على الاحتياط وهو قطع الرجعة والاحتياط في الوطء تركه فلم نجعل التيمم فيه قبل تأكده بالصلاة كالاغتسال كما لا يفعله في الحل للأزواج ا هـ . فالحاصل أن التيمم لا يوجب حل وطئها وانقطاع الرجعة وحلها للأزواج إلا بالصلاة على الصحيح من المذهب لكن قال القاضي الاسبيجابي في شرح مختصر الطحاوي: وأجمعوا أنه يقربها زوجها وإن لم تصل ولا تتزوج بزوج آخر ما لم تصل وفي انقطاع الرجعة الخلاف وفي الخلاصة : إذا انقطع دم المرأة دون عادتها المعروفة في حيض أو نفاس اغتسلت حين تخاف فوت الصلاة وصلت واجتنب زوجها قربانها احتياطاً حتى تأتي على عادتها لكن تصوم رمضان احتياطاً، ولو كانت الثالثة هذه الحيضة هي من العدة انقطعت الرجعة احتياطاً ولا تتزوج بزوج آخر احتياطاً، فإن
فتح القدير، لكن نقل في النهر عن النهاية ما يخالف نقل المؤلف عنها حيث قال : وفي النهاية : وتأخير الغسل إلى الوقت المستحب فيما إذا انقطع لتمام عادتها أو لأقلها واجب اهـ. وهذا يوافق ظاهر كلام المبسوط لكن رأيت عبارة النهاية كما نقله المؤلف عنها والظاهر أن «أل» من المستحب في كلام النهر زائدة من النساخ وبدونها تتوافق العبارتان قوله : (بخلاف الانقطاع للعشرة) أي فإن فيه يكون زمن الغسل من الطهر فيما إذا انقطع لعشرة . (فائدة) : حكي أن خلف بن أيوب أرسل ابنه من بلخ إلى بغداد للتعلم فأنفق عليه خمسين ألف فلما درهم، رجع قال له : ما تعلمت؟ قال : هذه المسألة أن زمان الغسل من الظهر في حق صاحبة العشرة ومن الحيض فيما دونها . قال خلف والله ما ضيعت سفرك. كذا في الكفاية اهـ. زاده على الشرعة قوله : ( وهكذا جواب صومها إذا طهرت الخ) أي إذا طهرت قبل الفجر لأقل من عشرة
In al-Tanjees: A traveling woman became pure from menses and performed tayammum, then found water. It is permissible for her husband to approach her, but she should not recite Quran because when she performed tayammum she exited from menses. When she found water, ghusl became obligatory on her, so she became like a junub. Its apparent meaning is that tayammum without prayer removes her from menses, thus her intercourse is permissible, but it is not so. For it is said in al-Mabsut: The Hakim al-Shahid did not mention in al-Kafi the case where she performed tayammum and did not pray. It is said that there is a difference: according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Abu Hanifa), the husband should not approach her; according to Muhammad, he may. The most correct is that he should not approach her according to all of them, because Muhammad only considered tayammum like ghusl in matters based on precaution, like cutting off the right of return (raj'a), but precaution in intercourse is to avoid it. So we do not consider tayammum before it is confirmed by prayer like ghusl, just as it is not done in permissibility for husbands. The conclusion: tayammum does not cause permissibility of intercourse, cessation of the right of return, or permissibility for other husbands except with prayer, according to the correct view of the school. But Qadi al-Isbijabi said in Sharh Mukhtasar al-Tahawi: They all agreed that her husband may approach her even if she did not pray, but she may not marry another man until she prays, and there is difference regarding cessation of the right of return. In al-Khulasah: If the woman's blood stops before her known habit in menstruation or lochia, she performs ghusl when she fears missing prayer and prays, and her husband avoids approaching her out of precaution until her habit passes, but she may fast Ramadan out of precaution. And if this menstruation is part of the 'iddah, the right of return is cut off out of precaution, and she may not marry another out of precaution. Then from Fath al-Qadir, but it is transmitted in al-Nahr from al-Nihayah something contradicting the author's transmission from it: In al-Nihayah, delaying ghusl to the recommended time is obligatory when cessation is at the end of her habit or for less than hers. This agrees with the apparent statement of al-Mabsut, but I saw the expression of al-Nihayah as transmitted by the author. It appears that the 'al' of 'al-mustahabb' in the speech of al-Nahr is an addition from the copyists, and without it the two expressions agree. His statement: (Contrary to cessation for ten days) i.e., in it the time of ghusl is from purity when cessation is for ten. (Benefit): It is narrated that Khalf ibn Ayyub sent his son from Balkh to Baghdad to learn, spending fifty thousand dirhams. When he returned, he said: What did you learn? He said: This issue that the time of ghusl from zuhr for the woman of ten days, and from menstruation for less than it. Khalf said: By Allah, you did not waste your journey. This is in al-Kifayah. He added to al-Shir'ah: His statement: (Similarly the answer of her fast when she becomes pure) i.e., if she becomes pure before dawn for less than ten.
Source pages p. 354

Commentary
This passage addresses a nuanced issue: a woman who becomes pure from menses but performs tayammum due to lack of water, then finds water before praying. According to a text in al-Tanjees, her husband may approach her even without prayer, but the author refutes this. Citing al-Mabsut, there is a dispute: according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, the husband may not approach, while Muhammad permits it. The correct view (al-sahih) is that none of them permit approach without prayer. Muhammad's analogy of tayammum to ghusl is limited to matters of precaution like cutting off the right of return (raj'a), but for intercourse, precaution dictates avoidance. Thus, tayammum alone does not make her permissible for intercourse; she must also pray. However, Qadi al-Isbijabi claims consensus that the husband may approach even without prayer, but this is contradicted by Hanafi differences. The passage then returns to earlier rulings about cessation and ghusl timing, including a beneficial anecdote about Khalf ibn Ayyub, emphasizing that for a woman whose habit is ten days, the time for ghusl is from zuhr, while for less than ten, it is from menstruation (i.e., she must wait until her habit passes).

Key Terms
التيمم (al-tayammum): Dry ablution with earth as a substitute for ghusl or wudu when water is unavailable or harmful.
الرجعة (al-raj'a): The right of a husband to take back his wife during her 'iddah (waiting period) after a revocable divorce.
الجنب (al-junub): A person in a state of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the most correct Hanafi view, what is the ruling on a woman who performed tayammum after menses but did not pray?
A) It is permissible for her husband to approach her immediately
B) It is permissible only if she intends to pray later
C) It is not permissible for her husband to approach her until she prays
D) It is disliked but not haram

Key Takeaway
Tayammum after menses does not permit intercourse until the woman prays; the mufta bihi is prohibition without prayer.

Tayammum and Intercourse After Menses: The Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute with talil, dalil, and tarjih.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi mufta bihi on intercourse after tayammum without prayer and explain the talil behind the ruling.

Core Idea
Tayammum without prayer does not permit intercourse; caution (ihtiyat) demands avoidance until ghusl.

When a woman's menstruation stops, the general prohibition on intercourse is lifted only after she performs ghusl (full body wash). But what if she performs tayammum due to lack of water, without having prayed? In this lesson, we examine the intra-Hanafi dispute on this issue, tracing the reasoning from al-Asl, al-Mabsut, and later works. You will learn why the Hanafi school ultimately holds that tayammum alone is insufficient for intercourse, and how the principle of caution (ihtiyat) governs this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
The central question: does tayammum (without subsequent prayer) remove the prohibition of intercourse after menstruation? The passage presents two views.
The dispute is between Muhammad al-Shaybani (who permits) and Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf (who forbid) according to some reports.
2
Extract the Hanafi position from the primary sources
Muhammad's statement in al-Asl implies that ghusl is required for prayer and for lifting the prohibition. The tashdid reading of Quran 2:222 (يَطَّهَّرْنَ) supports this.
The dalil is the Quranic verse with tashdid, indicating purification through ghusl.
3
Analyze the counter-claim of consensus
Ibn Taymiyya and al-Qadi al-Ispijabi claim ijma' that intercourse is permissible even without prayer. The author refutes this by showing Hanafi disagreement.
The Hanafi position is that such a consensus is invalid because Hanafis differ.
4
Understand the talil from al-Mabsut
Muhammad's analogy of tayammum to ghusl is limited to cautionary matters (e.g., cutting off the right of return in divorce). For intercourse, caution requires avoidance, so tayammum is not equivalent.
This is a key argument: ihtiyat (caution) overrides the analogy.
5
Apply the ruling to practical scenarios
The mufta bihi: a woman who performs tayammum without prayer may not be approached by her husband until she performs ghusl (or prays if possible). She also cannot remarry until she prays.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa according to the most correct view.

نص عليه محمد في الأصل قال : إذا انقطع في وقت العشاء تؤخر إلى وقت يمكنها أن تغتسل فيه وتصلي قبل انتصاف الليل وما بعد نصف الليل مكروه ا هـ . وفي فتح القدير: إن حكم الثالث خلاف إنهاء الحرمة بالغسل الثابت بقراءة التشديد فهو مخرج منه بالإجماع ا هـ . ويعارضه ما نقله في الغاية عن ابن تيمية أنه ذكر الإجماع على أنها تغتسل وتصلي ولا يحرم وطؤها كما في شرح منظومة ابن وهبان ولعله توهم من قول بعض الحنفية بالكراهة أنها كراهة تنزيه فنقل الإجماع على عدم الحرمة وإلا فلا يصح نقل الإجماع مع خلاف الحنفية كما لا يخفى. وفي التنجيس: مسافرة طهرت من الحيض فتيممت ثم وجدت ماء جاز للزوج أن يقربها لكن لا تقرأ القرآن لأنها لما تيممت خرجت من الحيض. فلما وجدت الماء فإنما وجب عليها الغسل فصارت كالجنب ا هـ . وظاهره أن التيمم من غير صلاة يخرجها من الحيض فيجوز قربانها وليس كذلك فقد قال في المبسوط : ولم يذكر يعني الحاكم الشهيد في الكافي ما إذا تيممت ولم تصل، فقيل هو على الاختلاف عندهما ليس للزوج أن يقربها، وعند محمد له ذلك، والأصح أنه ليس له أن يقربها عندهم جميعاً لأن محمداً إنما جعل التيمم كالاغتسال فيما هو مبني على الاحتياط وهو قطع الرجعة والاحتياط في الوطء تركه فلم نجعل التيمم فيه قبل تأكده بالصلاة كالاغتسال كما لا يفعله في الحل للأزواج ا هـ . فالحاصل أن التيمم لا يوجب حل وطئها وانقطاع الرجعة وحلها للأزواج إلا بالصلاة على الصحيح من المذهب لكن قال القاضي الاسبيجابي في شرح مختصر الطحاوي: وأجمعوا أنه يقربها زوجها وإن لم تصل ولا تتزوج بزوج آخر ما لم تصل وفي انقطاع الرجعة الخلاف وفي الخلاصة : إذا انقطع دم المرأة دون عادتها المعروفة في حيض أو نفاس اغتسلت حين تخاف فوت الصلاة وصلت واجتنب زوجها قربانها احتياطاً حتى تأتي على عادتها لكن تصوم رمضان احتياطاً، ولو كانت الثالثة هذه الحيضة هي من العدة انقطعت الرجعة احتياطاً ولا تتزوج بزوج آخر احتياطاً، فإن تزوجها رجل إن لم يعاودها الدم ،جاز، وإن عاودها إن كان في العشرة ولم يزد على العشرة فسد نكاح الثاني، وكذا صاحب الاستبراء يجتنبها احتياطاً ا.هـ.
Muhammad stated in al-Asl: If it (the blood) stops at the time of Isha, she delays until a time when she can perform ghusl and pray before midnight, and after midnight is disliked. End. And in Fath al-Qadir: The ruling of the third is a difference, that the removal of prohibition (of intercourse) by ghusl is established by the reading with tashdid, so it is excluded from it by consensus. End. And opposing it is what was transmitted in al-Ghaya from Ibn Taymiyya that he mentioned consensus that she performs ghusl and prays, and her intercourse is not prohibited, as in Sharh Manzuma of Ibn Wahban. And perhaps he was deluded by the statement of some Hanafis of karaha that it is a tanzih karaha, so he transmitted consensus on non-prohibition; otherwise it is not correct to transmit consensus with Hanafi opposition, as is not hidden. And in al-Tanjis: A traveler purified from menses and made tayammum, then found water: it is permissible for the husband to approach her, but she does not recite Quran because when she made tayammum she left menses. But when she found water, ghusl became obligatory upon her, so she became like a junub. End. And its apparent meaning is that tayammum without prayer takes her out of menses, so approaching her is permissible, but it is not so. For it is said in al-Mabsut: He (the author al-Hakim al-Shahid) did not mention in al-Kafi the case if she made tayammum and did not pray. So it is said: according to the disagreement, according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad?) the husband may not approach her, and according to Muhammad he may. And the most correct is that he may not approach her according to all of them, because Muhammad made tayammum like ghusl only in that which is based on caution, which is cutting off the right of return (in divorce), and caution in intercourse is to avoid it. So we do not make tayammum before its confirmation by prayer like ghusl, just as it does not make her permissible for husbands. End. The summary is that tayammum does not make permissible her intercourse, nor does it break the right of return (in divorce), nor does it make her permissible for husbands, except with prayer, according to the correct position of the school. But al-Qadi al-Asbijabi said in Sharh Mukhtasar al-Tahawi: And they (the scholars) are agreed that her husband may approach her even if she does not pray, but she may not marry another husband as long as she has not prayed, and regarding the cutting off of the right of return there is disagreement. And in al-Khulasa: If the blood of a woman stops before her known habit in menses or lochia, she performs ghusl when she fears missing prayer, and prays, and her husband avoids approaching her as a precaution until her habit is completed. But she fasts Ramadan as a precaution. And if that menses was the third of the waiting period, the right of return is cut off as a precaution, and she does not marry another husband as a precaution. If a man marries her, and the blood does not return to her, it is permissible. If it returns, and it is within ten days and does not exceed ten, then the marriage of the second is invalid. Similarly, the one who is observing istibra avoids her as a precaution. End.
Source pages p. 354

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion of the rulings when a woman's menstruation stops before her usual habit. The author begins by quoting Muhammad al-Shaybani from al-Asl: if the blood stops at Isha time, she should delay ghusl until she can pray before midnight; after midnight is makruh. Then from Fath al-Qadir: the ruling that prohibition of intercourse is removed by ghusl is established by the tashdid reading of the Qur'an (يَطْهُرْنَ). The author notes an opposing claim by Ibn Taymiyya of consensus that she must do ghusl and pray but intercourse is not forbidden. The author argues this is likely a misunderstanding of the Hanafi position of karaha tanzih, otherwise consensus would not be valid given Hanafi opposition. Next, from al-Tanjis: a traveler who becomes pure, makes tayammum, then finds water: her husband may approach her, but she cannot read Quran. The author critiques this, showing from al-Mabsut that tayammum without prayer does not permit intercourse according to the most correct opinion (al-ashah). The dispute is between 'the two' (possibly Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) who say not permissible, and Muhammad (alone) who says permissible, but the relied-upon view is that he cannot approach her. The reason: Muhammad's analogy of tayammum to ghusl only applies in matters of caution (like cutting off the right of return in divorce), but in intercourse caution demands avoidance. The final summary: tayammum does not permit intercourse, cut off the right of return, or allow remarriage except with prayer. However, al-Qadi al-Ispijabi transmits a consensus that the husband may approach her even without prayer, but she cannot marry another without prayer. Then al-Khulasa synthesizes: when blood stops early, she performs ghusl and prays, but the husband avoids her out of precaution; she fasts Ramadan as precaution; the right of return is cut off precautionarily; she cannot remarry precautionarily; if she remarries and blood does not return, it's valid; if it returns within ten days, the second marriage is invalid. The passage demonstrates the interplay between legal rulings and caution (ihtiyat) in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
التيمم (al-tayammum): Dry ritual purification with clean earth when water is unavailable or harmful.
الاغتسال (al-ightisal): Full body washing with water for purification from major impurity (janaba, hayd, nifas).
الاحتياط (al-ihtiyat): The principle of caution; choosing the more restrictive ruling to ensure one does not fall into sin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the most correct Hanafi position, what is the ruling if a woman's menses stops and she performs tayammum but does not pray due to lack of water?
A) Her husband may approach her immediately.
B) Her husband may not approach her until she performs ghusl with water.
C) She must repeat the tayammum after finding water.
D) She is considered pure and may remarry.

Key Takeaway
Intercourse after menses requires ghusl (or at least prayer with tayammum); tayammum without prayer is insufficient, and the Hanafi school relies on caution (ihtiyat) in this matter.

Time of Ghusl After Menstruation and Its Effect on Fasting
Determining whether the time of ghusl is counted from hayd or tahara, and its impact on fasting validity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that the time of ghusl is counted from hayd for habits less than ten days and from tahara for a ten-day habit to determine the validity of a woman's fast after her menstrual bleeding stops, and distinguish the requirements for prayer versus fasting regarding the takbira.

Core Idea
Time of ghusl is from hayd if habit <10 days, from tahara if habit =10 days; fasting needs only time for ghusl, but prayer also needs time for takbira.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq, the author clarifies a crucial principle from the mashayikh: the time required for ghusl after menstruation is measured differently depending on whether the woman's habitual cycle is less than ten days or exactly ten days. This distinction directly affects whether a fast or prayer is valid when purity occurs close to Fajr. We will work through the rule, its proof from the Quran, and its application to fasting versus prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
First, identify what is being ruled upon: the time of ghusl after menstrual bleeding stops. The ruling determines whether the woman is considered pure from that moment or only after she performs ghusl.
This is a pre-condition for the validity of ibadat like fasting and prayer.
2
State the mashayikh's principle
The mashayikh rule: 'Zaman al-ghusl min al-tahr fi haqq sahibat al-ashara, wa min al-hayd fi ma dunaha.' That is, the time of ghusl is counted from tahara (the moment bleeding stops) for a woman whose habit is exactly ten days, and from hayd (the onset of bleeding) for those whose habit is less than ten days.
This principle applies to rulings like marital relations, idda, and remarriage, but not necessarily to all rulings.
3
Apply to fasting
For fasting: if a woman becomes pure before Fajr and enough time remains in the night to perform ghusl (i.e., the time from the moment of purity or from the start of hayd depending on habit), her fast the next day is valid. The correct view is that takbira (opening takbir of prayer) is not considered for fasting; only the possibility of ghusl matters.
If her habit is less than ten days, the time for ghusl is counted from the beginning of her hayd, so if she becomes pure too close to Fajr, she may not have 'enough time' even if she could theoretically ghusl quickly.
4
Contrast with prayer
For prayer: if she becomes pure in the first half of the night, she must have enough time for both ghusl and takbira to make Isha obligatory. If in the second half, only takbira time is needed. This is because prayer requires entry into the prayer time while purified.
The passage notes a potential objection from al-Nahr that prayer and fasting differ; fasting can be intended after dawn as long as she was pure at dawn, but prayer requires actual performance within its time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال في فتح القدير : ومفهوم التقييد أنه إذا زاد لا يفسد ومراده إذا كان العود بعد انقضاء العادة، أما قبلها فيفسد وإن زاد لأن الزيادة توجب الرد إلى العادة والفرض أنه عاودها فيها، فظهر أن النكاح قبل انقضاء الحيضة. واعلم أن مدة الاغتسال معتبرة من الحيض في الانقطاع لأقل من العشرة وإن كان تمام عادتها بخلاف الانقطاع للعشرة حتى لو طهرت في الأولى والباقي قدر الغسل والتحريمة فعليها قضاء تلك الصلاة، ولو طهرت في الثانية يشترط أن يكون الباقي قدر التحريمة فقط . وفي المجتبى : والصحيح أنه يعتبر مع الغسل لبس الثياب، وهكذا جواب صومها إذا طهرت قبل الفجر لكن الأصح أن لا تعتبر التحريمة في حق الصوم ثم قال قال مشايخنا: زمان الغسل من الطهر في حق صاحبة العشرة ومن الحيض فيما دونها. ولكن ما قالوا في حق القربان وانقطاع الرجعة وجواز التزوج بزوج آخر لا في حق جميع الأحكام، ألا ترى أنها إذا طهرت عقب غيبوبة الشفق ثم اغتسلت عند الفجر الكاذب ثم رأت الدم في الليلة السادسة عشر بعد زوال الشفق فهو طهر تام وإن لم يتم خمسة عشر من وقت الاغتسال ا هـ . وقوله يعتبر في الصوم التحريمة ظاهره الاكتفاء بمضي زمان الغسل. أن لا الأصح الغد، وفي السراج الوهاج ولو انقطع دمها في بعض ليالي رمضان، فإن وجدت في الليل مقدار ما تغتسل ويبقى ساعة من الليل فإنه يجب عليها قضاء العشاء ويجوز صومها من الغد، وإن بقي من الليل أقل من ذلك لا يجب عليها قضاء العشاء ولا يجوز صومها من الغد. ومن التوشيح : : إن كانت أيامها دون العشرة لا يجزئها صوم هذا اليوم إذا لم يبق من الوقت قدر الاغتسال والتحريمة لأنه لا يحكم بطهارتها إلا بهذا، وإن بقي مقدار الغسل والتحريمة فإنه يجزئها صومها لأن العشاء صارت ديناً عليها وأنه من حكم الطهارات فحكم بطهارتها ضرورة وهذا هو الحق فيما يظهر. وفي الكافي للحاكم ولو كانت نصرانية تحت مسلم فانقطع عنها الدم فيما دون العشرة وسع الزوج أن يطأها ووسعها أن تتزوّج لأنه لا اغتسال عليها الخطاب وهي مخرجة من حمل قراءة التشديد على ما دون الأكثر كما لا يخفى، فإن أسلمت بعد الانقطاع لا تتغير الأحكام لأنا حكمنا بخروجها من الحيض بنفس الانقطاع فلا يعود بالإسلام بخلاف ما إذا عاودها الدم فرؤية الدم مؤثرة في إثبات الحيض به ابتداء، اهـ. لعدم والباقي قدر الغسل والتحريمة جاز لها صوم اليوم وعليها قضاء العشاء وإلا فلا. قوله: (وهذا هو الحق فيما يظهر) قال في النهر فيه نظر ولم يبين وجهه، ولعل وجهه ظهور الفرق بين الصوم والصلاة فإن الصلاة لا تجب ما لم تدرك جزءاً من الوقت يسع التحريمة بخلاف الصوم فإنه يصح فيه إنشاء النية بعد الفجر وهي حين طلوع الفجر كانت طاهرة فتصح نيتها ويسقط عنها بلا لزوم قضاء
It is said in Fath al-Qadir: And the implication of the restriction is that if it increases, it does not invalidate. And his meaning is if the return (of blood) is after the completion of the habit. As for before it, it invalidates even if it increases, because the increase necessitates return to the habit, and the assumption is that it returned during it. Thus it becomes clear that the marriage before the completion of the menstrual period (is invalid). And know that the duration of ghusl is considered from the menses in the case of cessation before ten days even if it completes her habit, contrary to cessation at ten days. So if she becomes pure in the first (of two periods?) and the remaining is the extent of ghusl and takbira, then she must make up that prayer. And if she becomes pure in the second, it is required that the remaining be only the extent of takbira. And in al-Mujtaba: And the correct is that along with ghusl, wearing clothes is considered. And similarly is the answer regarding her fast if she becomes pure before dawn, but the correct is that takbira is not considered with respect to fasting. Then he said: Our mashayikh said: The time of ghusl is from tahara for the one whose habit is ten days, and from menses for those less than that. But they said this with respect to approaching and cutting off the right of return and permissibility of marriage to another husband, not with respect to all rulings. Do you not see that if she becomes pure immediately after the disappearance of twilight, then she performs ghusl at false dawn, then sees blood on the sixteenth night after the disappearance of twilight, it is a complete tahara even if fifteen days have not passed from the time of ghusl. End. And his statement: 'Takbira is considered in fasting' apparently means being satisfied with the passage of the time of ghusl. That ... the correct is ... tomorrow. And in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: If her blood stops during some nights of Ramadan, if she finds in the night an amount to perform ghusl and an hour of the night remains, then she must make up Isha and her fast of the next day is permissible. If less than that remains of the night, she does not have to make up Isha and her fast of the next day is not permissible. And from al-Tawshih: If her days are less than ten, her fast of that day is not valid if there does not remain of time the extent of ghusl and takbira, because she is not considered pure except by that. If there remains the extent of ghusl and takbira, then her fast is valid because Isha becomes a debt upon her and it is from the rulings of purifications, so she is judged pure necessarily, and this is the truth as it appears. And in al-Kafi by al-Hakim: And if a Christian woman under a Muslim husband has her blood stop before ten days, it is permissible for the husband to have intercourse with her and permissible for her to marry (another) because there is no ghusl upon her – the address (of the verse) is taken to apply to less than the majority, as is not hidden. If she converts to Islam after the cessation, the rulings do not change, because we ruled that she came out of menses by the cessation itself. So it does not return with Islam. But if the blood returns, then seeing blood is effective in establishing menses anew. End. Due to the non-existence... and the remaining is the extent of ghusl and takbira, her fast of that day is permissible and she must make up Isha, otherwise not. His statement: 'This is the truth as it appears' – it is said in al-Nahr: There is a consideration in it, and he did not explain his reason. Perhaps the reason is the apparent difference between fasting and prayer: prayer is not obligatory unless a part of time sufficient for takbira is reached, unlike fasting, because the intention can be made after dawn, and she was pure at the time of dawn, so her intention is valid and (the fast) is incumbent upon her without the necessity of making up.
Source pages p. 355

Commentary
This passage continues from the previous lesson, focusing on the timing of ghusl after menstruation and its effects on fasting. The author from Fath al-Qadir explains that if blood returns after the habit ends, it does not invalidate a marriage concluded in the meantime; but if it returns before the habit ends, it invalidates it. Then a key rule: the duration of ghusl is counted from the menses (hayd) when the bleeding stops before ten days, but from tahara when it stops exactly at ten days for a woman with a ten-day habit. This affects whether she must make up a prayer: if she becomes pure in the first half of the night with enough time for ghusl and takbira, she must pray Isha; if in the second half, only takbira is needed. For fasting, the correct view is that takbira is not required; the mere passage of time for ghusl suffices. The mashayikh rule: the time of ghusl is from tahara for the ten-day habit woman, from hayd for others. But this applies only to rulings of intercourse, cutting off idda rights, and remarriage, not to all rulings. An example: if she becomes pure at twilight, does ghusl at false dawn, then sees blood on the 16th night after twilight, that is a complete tahara even if 15 days haven't passed from ghusl. Then from al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: if her blood stops during Ramadan night, she must have enough time for ghusl and an hour left to make Isha valid; then she can fast the next day. From al-Tawshih: if her habit is less than ten days, her fast is not valid unless there is enough time for ghusl and takbira before Fajr; if so, fast is valid and she owes Isha. The author notes that al-Nahr objects to this equivalence between prayer and fasting: prayer requires a part of time after tahara, but fasting can be intended after Fajr as long as she was pure at dawn. Finally, a separate ruling for a Christian woman under a Muslim husband: when her menses stops before ten days, husband may approach her, and she may remarry, because there is no obligation of ghusl for her (the Quranic address is for Muslims). Converting to Islam after the cessation does not change the ruling that she was already pure, but if blood returns, it establishes a new menses.

Key Terms
التحريمة (al-tahrima): The opening takbir of prayer; used here as a measure of time sufficient to begin prayer.
الطهر (al-tahr): State of purity after menstruation or postpartum bleeding ceases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi mashayikh, when is the time of ghusl considered from al-tahr (purity) rather than from hayd (menstruation)?
A) For a woman whose habit is less than ten days.
B) For a woman whose habit is exactly ten days.
C) For all women regardless of habit.
D) Only for Christian women.

Key Takeaway
The time of ghusl for a menstruating woman is determined by her habit: from hayd for cycles less than ten days, from tahara for exactly ten days, and this directly impacts the validity of subsequent fasting and prayer.

Ruling on Marriage Validity When Blood Returns After Purity
Explains marriage validity when blood returns after apparent purity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marriage validity when a woman experiences a return of blood after apparent purity and identify the conditions that affect its validity.

Core Idea
Marriage is invalid if blood returns within the habitual period, but valid if it returns after the habit.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in Hanafi fiqh: a woman whose menstrual blood stops, leading to an apparent purity, then resumes. The ruling on a marriage contracted during that interval depends on whether the return occurs within or after her habitual menstrual period. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying the rules of iddah and remarriage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key actors and actions
Recognize the woman (who had blood stop) and the man who marries her. The key event is the return of blood after apparent purity.
The passage also mentions 'sahib al-istibra'' (the one observing istibra') as a precautionary case.
2
State the general rule and its condition
The rule: if blood does not return, marriage is valid. If it returns within ten days and does not exceed ten, the marriage is invalid. Note the condition 'within the ten days (maximum hayd) and not exceeding ten'.
This is the baseline Hanafi position.
3
Analyze the exception from Fath al-Qadir
The commentator clarifies: if the return occurs after the woman's habitual period ends, the marriage is NOT invalid even if blood exceeds. However, if it returns before the habit ends, the marriage is invalid even if the bleeding exceeds the habit. This is because an increase in blood after the habit is deemed istihadah, while return before the habit confirms ongoing hayd.
The key is the habit (adah), not just the ten-day maximum.
4
Apply to a scenario
Consider a woman with a habit of 6 days. Her blood stops on day 6, she marries on day 7, then blood returns on day 8: marriage is invalid because return occurred within the habit? Actually, the habit is 6 days, so day 7 is after habit. But the passage says 'if return is after habit, even if it exceeds, marriage is not invalid'. Here return on day 8 is after habit, so marriage is valid. However, if return on day 5 (within habit), marriage is invalid even if total bleeding becomes 8 days.
Always check the habit first.

تزوجها رجل إن لم يعاودها الدم، جاز، وإن عاودها إن كان في العشرة ولم يزد على العشرة فسد نكاح الثاني، وكذا صاحب الاستبراء يجتنبها احتياطاً ا.هـ. قال في فتح القدير : ومفهوم التقييد أنه إذا زاد لا يفسد ومراده إذا كان العود بعد انقضاء العادة، أما قبلها فيفسد وإن زاد لأن الزيادة توجب الرد إلى العادة والفرض أنه عاودها فيها، فظهر أن النكاح قبل انقضاء الحيضة. واعلم أن مدة الاغتسال معتبرة من الحيض في الانقطاع لأقل من العشرة وإن كان تمام عادتها بخلاف الانقطاع للعشرة حتى لو طهرت في الأولى والباقي قدر الغسل والتحريمة فعليها قضاء تلك الصلاة، ولو طهرت في الثانية يشترط أن يكون الباقي قدر التحريمة فقط . وفي المجتبى : والصحيح أنه يعتبر مع الغسل لبس الثياب، وهكذا جواب صومها إذا طهرت قبل الفجر لكن الأصح أن لا تعتبر التحريمة في حق الصوم ثم قال قال مشايخنا: زمان الغسل من الطهر في حق صاحبة العشرة ومن الحيض فيما دونها. ولكن ما قالوا في حق القربان وانقطاع الرجعة وجواز التزوج بزوج آخر لا في حق جميع الأحكام، ألا ترى أنها إذا طهرت عقب غيبوبة الشفق ثم اغتسلت عند الفجر الكاذب ثم رأت الدم في الليلة السادسة عشر بعد زوال الشفق فهو طهر تام وإن لم يتم خمسة عشر من وقت الاغتسال ا هـ . وقوله يعتبر في الصوم التحريمة ظاهره الاكتفاء بمضي زمان الغسل. أن لا الأصح الغد، وفي السراج الوهاج ولو انقطع دمها في بعض ليالي رمضان، فإن وجدت في الليل مقدار ما تغتسل ويبقى ساعة من الليل فإنه يجب عليها قضاء العشاء ويجوز صومها من الغد، وإن بقي من الليل أقل من ذلك لا يجب عليها قضاء العشاء ولا يجوز صومها من الغد. ومن التوشيح : : إن كانت أيامها دون العشرة لا يجزئها صوم هذا اليوم إذا لم يبق من الوقت قدر الاغتسال والتحريمة لأنه لا يحكم بطهارتها إلا بهذا، وإن بقي مقدار الغسل والتحريمة فإنه يجزئها صومها لأن العشاء صارت ديناً عليها وأنه من حكم الطهارات فحكم بطهارتها ضرورة وهذا هو الحق فيما يظهر. وفي الكافي للحاكم ولو كانت نصرانية تحت مسلم فانقطع عنها الدم فيما دون العشرة وسع الزوج أن يطأها ووسعها أن تتزوّج لأنه لا اغتسال عليها الخطاب وهي مخرجة من حمل قراءة التشديد على ما دون الأكثر كما لا يخفى، فإن أسلمت بعد الانقطاع لا تتغير الأحكام لأنا حكمنا بخروجها من الحيض بنفس الانقطاع فلا يعود بالإسلام بخلاف ما إذا عاودها الدم فرؤية الدم مؤثرة في إثبات الحيض به ابتداء، اهـ. المدة حيض ونفاس وأقل الظهر خمسة عشر يوماً ولا حد لأكثره إلا عند نصب العادة فكذلك يكون مؤثراً في البقاء بخلاف الإسلام كذا في المبسوط وفي الخلاصة : فإن أدركها الحيض في شيء من الوقت سقطت الصلاة عنها إن افتتحها وأجمعوا أنها إذا طهرت وقد بقي من الوقت قدر ما لا يسع فيه التحريمة لا يلزمها قضاء هذه الصلاة، وإذا أدركها الحيض بعد شروعها في التطوع كان عليها قضاء تلك الصلاة إذا طهرت ا هـ . وكذا إذا شرعت في صوم التطوع ثم حاضت فإنه يلزمها قضاؤه فلا فرق بين الصلاة والصوم. ذكره في فتح القدير من الصوم، وكذا في النهاية، وكذا ذكره الأسبيجابي هنا، فتبين أن ما في شرح الوقاية من الفرق بينهما غير صحيح.
If a man marries her and the blood does not return to her, it is permissible. If it returns, then if it is within ten days and does not exceed ten, the second marriage is invalid. Likewise, the one who observes istibra' avoids her as a precaution. End quote. He said in Fath al-Qadir: The implication of the restriction is that if it exceeds, it is not invalid, and his intent is if the return is after the end of the habit; as for before it, it is invalid even if it exceeds, because the increase necessitates returning to the habit, and the assumption is that it returned during it. So it appears that [ruling on] marriage [occurs] before the completion of the menstrual period. Know that the duration of ghusl is considered from menstruation in the case of cessation for less than ten, even if it is at the completion of her habit, unlike cessation for ten. So if she becomes pure in the first [period] and remaining time suffices for ghusl and takbir, she must make up that prayer. If she becomes pure in the second, it is conditional that only the time for takbir remains. In al-Mujtaba: The correct view is that dressing is considered along with ghusl, and similarly the answer for her fast if she becomes pure before dawn, but the most correct is that takbir is not considered for the fast. Then he said: Our shaykhs said: The time of ghusl is from purity for the one with a ten-day habit and from menstruation for one with less. But what they said applies to [rulings of] sacrifice, termination of the right to take back, and permission to marry another husband, not to all rulings. Do you not see that if she becomes pure immediately after the disappearance of the twilight, then she bathes at the false dawn, then sees blood on the sixteenth night after the twilight has disappeared, this is a complete purity even if fifteen [days] have not passed from the time of ghusl. End quote. And his statement: 'Takbir is considered for the fast' apparently means that mere passing of the time of ghusl suffices. ... And in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: If her blood stops during some nights of Ramadan, and she finds at night enough time to bathe and an hour of the night remains, then she must make up the 'Isha' prayer and her fast from the next day is permissible. If less than that remains, she does not have to make up 'Isha' and her fast from the next day is not permissible. And from al-Tawshih: If her days are less than ten, fasting that day is not sufficient if there does not remain enough time for ghusl and takbir, because purity is not ruled unless with that; if there remains the amount for ghusl and takbir, then her fast is sufficient because 'Isha' becomes a debt upon her and it is from the rulings of purifications, so purity is ruled by necessity, and this is the truth as it appears. And in al-Kafi by al-Hakim: If a Christian woman was under a Muslim and her blood stops within ten days, it is permissible for her husband to have intercourse with her and permissible for her to marry [another], because there is no ghusl on her, the address [to ghusl] is removed by interpreting the strict reading as for less than the majority, as is not hidden. If she accepts Islam after the cessation, the rulings do not change because we have ruled that she exited menstruation by the cessation itself, so it does not return by Islam, unlike if the blood returns to her, for seeing blood has an effect in establishing menstruation initially. End quote. The period [of menstruation] and postpartum and the minimum of purity is fifteen days, and there is no maximum except when a habit is established. So likewise it has an effect in continuation unlike Islam. Thus in al-Mabsut and in al-Khulasa: If menstruation overtakes her at any time, prayer becomes invalid if she had started it. And they agreed that if she becomes pure and there remains time that cannot accommodate takbir, she is not required to make up that prayer. And if menstruation overtakes her after starting supererogatory prayer, she must make up that prayer when she becomes pure. End quote. Similarly, if she starts supererogatory fasting and then menstruates, she is required to make it up, so there is no difference between prayer and fasting. This was mentioned in Fath al-Qadir regarding fasting, and also in al-Nihaya, and also mentioned by al-Asbijabi here. So it becomes clear that what is in Sharh al-Wiqayah regarding a difference between them is incorrect.
Source pages p. 355

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses several rulings connected to a woman who becomes pure from menstruation and then experiences a return of blood. It begins by stating that if a woman marries after her iddah and the blood does not return, the marriage is valid. If blood returns within the ten-day maximum of hayd and does not exceed it, the second marriage is invalidated because the return of blood proves she was still in hayd. The commentator from Fath al-Qadir clarifies that if the return occurs after her habitual period ends, the marriage is not invalidated even if blood exceeds, because the increase is disregarded as istihadah. However, if the return occurs before the habit ends, the marriage is invalid even if the blood increases, because the default is that she is still in hayd. The passage then shifts to the duration required for ghusl after purity. The time of ghusl is counted from hayd when bleeding stops before ten days, even if it's at the end of her habit, because the remaining bleeding is considered hayd. If she becomes pure before the end of her habit and there remains time for ghusl and takbir, she must make up that prayer. If she becomes pure at the end of ten days, only the time for takbir is required. The text also notes a difference of opinion regarding whether dressing after ghusl is required, and whether takbir is considered for fasting. It then cites al-Siraj al-Wahhaj for the case of Ramadan: if blood stops at night and there is enough time for ghusl and an hour of the night remains, she must pray 'Isha and may fast the next day; otherwise not. A similar ruling is given from al-Tawshih. The passage also discusses a Christian woman under a Muslim husband: if her blood stops within ten days, it is permissible for her husband to have intercourse and for her to remarry, because the obligation of ghusl is lifted, and the reading 'on those who menstruate' is interpreted as referring to Muslim women. If she accepts Islam after the cessation, the rulings do not change because the cessation itself is the indicator of purity. Finally, the text quotes a consensus that if a woman becomes pure but only a very short time remains (less than takbir), she does not have to make up that prayer. It then equates this to supererogatory fasting: if she starts a supererogatory fast and then menstruates, she must make it up, contradicting the view in Sharh al-Wiqayah that distinguished between prayer and fasting. All these rulings are based on the principle that the time needed for ghusl and takbir is a condition for considering a woman purified for the purpose of prayer and fasting obligations.

Key Terms
التحريمة (al-tahrimah): The opening takbir (Allahu Akbar) that begins the prayer; used as a measure of minimal time for prayer validity.
الاستبراء (al-istibra'): The period of waiting after a temporary contract to ensure a woman is not pregnant; here it refers to avoiding intercourse after an apparent purity to confirm no return of blood.
الطهر (al-tuhr): The state of purity from menstruation; also the duration of purity between menses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on a marriage if a woman's blood returns after her habitual period ends, even if the total bleeding exceeds ten days?
A) The marriage is invalid because it exceeded ten days.
B) The marriage is valid because the return occurred after the habit.
C) The marriage is valid only if she performs ghusl before marriage.
D) The marriage is invalid unless she waited one full day.

Key Takeaway
Marriage validity upon return of blood after apparent purity depends on whether the return occurs within or after the woman's habitual menstrual period.

Module 4 · Lesson 706

Taharah — Purification
advanced
10 min
Time Required for Ghusl and Its Effect on Prayer and Fasting Obligations
Explains the duration required for ghusl and takbir to establish purity for prayer and fasting.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine, for a woman who becomes pure from menstruation, the minimum time required for ghusl and takbir, and apply this to decide whether she must make up prayer and whether her fast is valid.

Core Idea
For a woman to be considered pure and obligated to pray/fast, sufficient time for ghusl and takbir must remain in the time window.

This lesson delves into a key nuance in Hanafi taharah: the exact moment a woman who has stopped menstruating is considered legally pure for the purposes of prayer and fasting. Simply stopping bleeding is not enough; she must have enough time to perform ghusl and, for prayer, also the opening takbir (tahrimah). This ruling has implications for qada of missed prayers and the validity of a fast on the following day.

Guided Path
1
Understand the base rule: time for ghusl is from hayd
When bleeding stops for less than ten days, the time needed for ghusl is calculated from the beginning of hayd, not from the moment of cessation. This is because the remaining bleeding is considered hayd until she actually bathes.
The passage says: 'مدة الاغتسال معتبرة من الحيض في الانقطاع لأقل من العشرة'.
2
Distinguish between two cessation scenarios
If she becomes pure in the first scenario (stopping before her habit ends) and there is enough time for ghusl plus takbir, she must make up the prayer. If she becomes pure in the second scenario (at the end of ten days), only the time for takbir is sufficient; ghusl time is not considered.
This is because in the latter case, the cessation at ten days definitively ends hayd.
3
Examine the ikhtilaf on dressing and takbir for fasting
The text notes a difference of opinion: some say dressing after ghusl is part of the requirement, but the correct view is that it is not. For fasting, the question is whether takbir (the minimal prayer time) is considered. The authoritative opinion is that takbir is not required for fasting; only the time for ghusl is relevant.
This is from al-Mujtaba and the statement 'الأصح أن لا تعتبر التحريمة في حق الصوم'.
4
Apply the ruling to the case of Ramadan
If bleeding stops during a night of Ramadan, and she has enough time to bathe and at least an hour of the night remains, she must make up 'Isha and her fast the next day is valid. If less time remains, she does not have to pray 'Isha and her fast is not valid.
This is from al-Siraj al-Wahhaj and al-Tawshih.
5
Note the consensus and the refutation of a contrary view
The passage ends with a consensus that if only a very short time remains (insufficient for takbir), she is not required to make up that prayer. It also equates supererogatory prayer and fasting: if she starts a voluntary act and then menstruates, she must make it up, contrary to the statement in Sharh al-Wiqayah that distinguished them.
The text explicitly says 'فتبين أن ما في شرح الوقاية من الفرق بينهما غير صحيح'.

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses several rulings connected to a woman who becomes pure from menstruation and then experiences a return of blood. It begins by stating that if a woman marries after her iddah and the blood does not return, the marriage is valid. If blood returns within the ten-day maximum of hayd and does not exceed it, the second marriage is invalidated because the return of blood proves she was still in hayd. The commentator from Fath al-Qadir clarifies that if the return occurs after her habitual period ends, the marriage is not invalidated even if blood exceeds, because the increase is disregarded as istihadah. However, if the return occurs before the habit ends, the marriage is invalid even if the blood increases, because the default is that she is still in hayd. The passage then shifts to the duration required for ghusl after purity. The time of ghusl is counted from hayd when bleeding stops before ten days, even if it's at the end of her habit, because the remaining bleeding is considered hayd. If she becomes pure before the end of her habit and there remains time for ghusl and takbir, she must make up that prayer. If she becomes pure at the end of ten days, only the time for takbir is required. The text also notes a difference of opinion regarding whether dressing after ghusl is required, and whether takbir is considered for fasting. It then cites al-Siraj al-Wahhaj for the case of Ramadan: if blood stops at night and there is enough time for ghusl and an hour of the night remains, she must pray 'Isha and may fast the next day; otherwise not. A similar ruling is given from al-Tawshih. The passage also discusses a Christian woman under a Muslim husband: if her blood stops within ten days, it is permissible for her husband to have intercourse and for her to remarry, because the obligation of ghusl is lifted, and the reading 'on those who menstruate' is interpreted as referring to Muslim women. If she accepts Islam after the cessation, the rulings do not change because the cessation itself is the indicator of purity. Finally, the text quotes a consensus that if a woman becomes pure but only a very short time remains (less than takbir), she does not have to make up that prayer. It then equates this to supererogatory fasting: if she starts a supererogatory fast and then menstruates, she must make it up, contradicting the view in Sharh al-Wiqayah that distinguished between prayer and fasting. All these rulings are based on the principle that the time needed for ghusl and takbir is a condition for considering a woman purified for the purpose of prayer and fasting obligations.

Key Terms
التحريمة (al-tahrimah): The opening takbir (Allahu Akbar) that begins the prayer; used as a measure of minimal time for prayer validity.
الاستبراء (al-istibra'): The period of waiting after a temporary contract to ensure a woman is not pregnant; here it refers to avoiding intercourse after an apparent purity to confirm no return of blood.
الطهر (al-tuhr): The state of purity from menstruation; also the duration of purity between menses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on a woman's fast the next day if her menstrual blood stops during the night of Ramadan and she has only enough time to bathe (ghusl) but not enough time remaining for the takbir before dawn?
A) Her fast is valid because only ghusl time is required.
B) Her fast is not valid because takbir time is also required.
C) Her fast is valid only if she had also dressed.
D) She cannot fast because she did not make up 'Isha.

Key Takeaway
For a woman who becomes pure from menstruation, the obligation to make up prayer depends on having sufficient time for both ghusl and takbir; for fasting, only ghusl time is required, not takbir.

The Intervening Purity Between Two Bloods: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on intervening purity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the intervening purity (tuhr mutakhalil) and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding its duration and applicability in hayd vs nifas.

Core Idea
A clean interval between two bloods is not a separator unless it lasts at least 15 days, and even then only during nifas, not hayd.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq examines a nuanced issue in menstrual jurisprudence: how to treat the clean days that occur between two episodes of bleeding within the maximum period of hayd or nifas. The Hanafi school has an internal dispute, primarily between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, on whether such an interval counts as a separate purity or is absorbed into the bleeding period. This lesson unpacks the dispute and its practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Issue
Read the matn statement: 'And the purity between two bloods in the period is hayd and nifas.' What does this mean? The intervening purity is considered part of the bleeding period.
2
Trace the Narration Chain
Note that several companions of Abu Hanifa narrated from him: Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, Zufar, etc. Each has a different riwayah. Focus on Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.
Muhammad has two narrations and adopted one.
3
Analyze Abu Yusuf's Principle
According to Abu Yusuf (the other narration of Abu Hanifa), if the clean interval is less than 15 days, it does NOT separate the two bloods; it is treated as continuous blood. If 15 days or more, it becomes a separator, but only conceivable during nifas.
Why only nifas? Because hayd maximum is 10 days, so a 15-day interval cannot fit.
4
Compare with Muhammad's View
Muhammad reportedly allows the interval to be a separator in hayd as well if it reaches 15 days. The text argues this is practically impossible because the total hayd period is only 10 days.
The dispute is more relevant for nifas.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi
The relied-upon position is that of Abu Yusuf: an interval <15 days is part of hayd/nifas; a separator of ≥15 days is only possible in nifas.
This is consistent with the general principle that purity between menses must be at least 15 days.

His statement: 'And the purity between two bloods in the period is hayd and nifas' means that the purity that intervenes between two bloods, with both bloods during the period of hayd or during the period of nifas, is hayd in the first and nifas in the second. Know that among the companions of Abu Hanifa - they are Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, Zufar, al-Hasan ibn Ziyad, and Ibn al-Mubarak - each narrated from him regarding this issue a narration except Muhammad, for two narrations are narrated from him and he adopted one. If it is fifteen days or more, it becomes a separator, but this is only conceivable during the period of nifas. Then if at one of its ends there is something that can be made hayd, it is hayd; otherwise it is istihadah. Then if it does not exceed ten, it is all hayd. End quote. Its reasoning: since takbir in prayer and fasting is considered from menstruation and she did not have sufficient time, purity is not ruled for her. If we said fasting is obligatory, it would necessitate ruling her pure, and that would necessitate permitting intercourse with her because she is pure by ruling. His statement: 'Thus it becomes clear that what is in Sharh al-Wiqayah [regarding the difference] is incorrect' - that is where he said: 'If a woman fasting menstruates during the day, if at the end, her fast is invalidated and she must make it up if it was obligatory; if it was supererogatory, no, unlike the supererogatory prayer if she menstruates during it.' End quote. He means she must make it up if she menstruates during it, so he differentiated between fasting and prayer. His statement: 'But this is only conceivable in the period of nifas' requires consideration, because its separation is conceivable in hayd as well, by making what precedes it hayd and what follows likewise if it reaches its minimum. And he did not restrict its separation to the period of hayd such that one would say it is not conceivable in hayd. Rather, the discussion is about its intervening between two bloods. That is why, and Allah knows best, he said in al-Sharnubalaliyyah after quoting the author's statement: 'So consider it carefully.' His statement: 'Then if at one of its ends' means one of the ends of the purity that is fifteen days or more. And his statement 'Then...'
Source pages p. 356

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq deals with a key Hanafi dispute about the clear interval (tuhr) that occurs between two episodes of bleeding within the maximum period of hayd or nifas. The matn states that such an intervening purity is considered part of hayd or nifas respectively. The sharh then elaborates the views of Abu Hanifa's companions. The main ikhtilaf: According to Abu Yusuf (which is also the other narration from Abu Hanifa), if the interval is less than 15 days, it does not act as a separator between the two bloods; instead, the entire period is treated as continuous bleeding (either hayd or nifas). If the interval is 15 days or more, it becomes a separator (a valid purity), but this situation only occurs in nifas according to Abu Yusuf, because the total duration of nifas is limited to 40 days; in hayd, the total duration is at most 10 days, so an interval of 15 days cannot fit within hayd. The author then notes that if the interval is 15 days or more and at one end there is blood that can be considered hayd (within 10 days), then it is hayd; otherwise, it is istihadah. If the total blood (first, interval, second) does not exceed 10 days, it is all hayd. The passage then cites al-Zayla'i and Imdad al-Fattah to support the idea that the minimum time for ghusl and takbir is required to consider a woman pure; if not, she is still considered menstruating for the purpose of obligatory acts. After a discussion, the text criticizes Sharh al-Wiqayah for distinguishing between prayer and fasting when menstruation occurs during a supererogatory act, concluding that both require make-up. The intra-Hanafi dispute revolves around whether the intervening purity can separate the two bloods, with Abu Yusuf requiring a minimum of 15 days, while others like Muhammad may have different thresholds.

Key Terms
الطهر المتخلل (al-tuhr al-mutakhalil): The clean interval that occurs between two episodes of bleeding within the maximum period of hayd or nifas.
فاصل (fasil): A separator; a clean interval that is long enough to count as a valid purity between two menstruations (at least 15 days).
الاستحاضة (al-istihadah): Chronic blood flow outside the regular menstrual period; the woman can pray and fast.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 10 days; applies in both hayd and nifas.
B) 15 days; applies in hayd only.
C) 15 days; applies only in nifas according to the relied-upon view.
D) 5 days; applies in neither.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a clean interval between two bloods is treated as part of the bleeding unless it reaches 15 days, and even then it only serves as a separator during nifas, not hayd.

Making Up Supererogatory Worship Interrupted by Menstruation
Explains ruling and evidence for making up supererogatory acts interrupted by menstruation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on making up supererogatory prayer and fast interrupted by menstruation, and explain the evidence and refutation of a contrary view.

Core Idea
A supererogatory act once started becomes a debt — if interrupted by menstruation, it must be made up.

This lesson examines a specific scenario: a woman voluntarily begins a supererogatory prayer or fast, and then menstruation begins before she completes it. The Hanafi school holds that she must make up that act once purified, even though it was voluntary. This ruling is based on the principle that commencing a supererogatory act transforms it into a binding commitment, and the subsequent impurity does not erase that obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is a supererogatory (nafl) prayer or fast interrupted by menstruation after having been started. The ruling is wajib al-qada (obligatory makeup).
The threshold for 'started' in prayer is the opening takbir (tahreemah).
2
Locate the evidence
The author cites al-Mabsut, al-Khulasa, Fath al-Qadir, al-Nihaya, and al-Isbijabi all stating that both supererogatory prayer and fast require makeup if interrupted by menstruation after commencement.
These are authoritative sources of the Hanafi school (zahir al-riwayah).
3
Analyze the refutation
The text explicitly declares that what is found in Sharh al-Wiqaya—a distinction between prayer and fast on this issue—is incorrect. There is no difference.
The refutation underscores that the ruling is uniform for all supererogatory acts.
4
Understand the underlying principle
A supererogatory act becomes binding once commenced; interruption by a legal impurity (menstruation) does not absolve the duty to complete it later. This is analogous to a vow or commitment.
This principle is specific to Hanafi fiqh and applies only after the act has been initiated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطهارة - باب المدة حيض ونفاس وأقل الظهر خمسة عشر يوماً ولا . حد لأكثره إلا عند نصب العادة فكذلك يكون مؤثراً في البقاء بخلاف الإسلام كذا في المبسوط وفي الخلاصة : فإن أدركها الحيض في شيء من الوقت سقطت الصلاة عنها إن افتتحها وأجمعوا أنها إذا طهرت وقد بقي من الوقت قدر ما لا يسع فيه التحريمة لا يلزمها قضاء هذه الصلاة، وإذا أدركها الحيض بعد شروعها في التطوع كان عليها قضاء تلك الصلاة إذا طهرت ا هـ . وكذا إذا شرعت في صوم التطوع ثم حاضت فإنه يلزمها قضاؤه فلا فرق بين الصلاة والصوم. ذكره في فتح القدير من الصوم، وكذا في النهاية، وكذا ذكره الأسبيجابي هنا، فتبين أن ما في شرح الوقاية من الفرق بينهما غير صحيح.
Book of Purification - Chapter on menstruation and postnatal bleeding: The minimal interval of purity is fifteen days, and there is no limit to its maximum except when habit is established. Thus it has an effect on continuation, unlike Islam. So in al-Mabsut and al-Khulasa: If menstruation catches her in any part of the time, the prayer drops from her if she had started it, and they agreed that when she becomes pure and there remains of the time an amount insufficient for the opening takbir, she is not required to make up this prayer. And if menstruation catches her after she has started a supererogatory act, she must make up that prayer when she becomes pure. Similarly, if she starts a supererogatory fast and then menstruates, she is required to make it up. So there is no difference between prayer and fast. This is mentioned in Fath al-Qadir on fasting, and similarly in al-Nihaya, and similarly mentioned by al-Isbijabi here. Thus it becomes clear that what is in Sharh al-Wiqaya of a distinction between them is incorrect.
Source pages p. 356

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq addressing the ruling when a woman starts a supererogatory act of worship (prayer or fast) and then menstruates. The author first establishes that the minimum interval of purity ('tuhr') between two menstrual cycles is fifteen days, which is a basic principle. He then recounts the position reported in al-Mabsut and al-Khulasa: if a woman is overtaken by menstruation during a portion of the prayer time, and she had already begun the prayer, the obligation of that prayer drops. However, if she starts a supererogatory prayer after the time begins and then menstruates, she must make it up when purified. The same applies to supererogatory fasting. The author cites several sources confirming this consensus and concludes that the distinction drawn in Sharh al-Wiqaya between prayer and fast on this point is incorrect. According to the Hanafi school, there is no difference: both supererogatory acts, if interrupted by menstruation after starting, require qada (makeup). Note that for obligatory prayers, if menstruation begins before one starts, there is no obligation to pray; but if one starts a supererogatory prayer and then menstruates, it becomes a debt similar to a missed obligatory prayer, because the act was voluntarily commenced and then invalidated.

Key Terms
تحريمة (tahreemah): The opening takbir (Allahu Akbar) that begins the prayer; in this context, it represents the minimal act that constitutes starting the prayer.
تطوع (tatawwu'): Supererogatory act of worship voluntarily performed, such as nafl prayer or fast.
قضاء (qada'): Making up a missed or invalidated act of worship after its prescribed time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A woman who starts a supererogatory prayer or fast must make it up if menstruation interrupts it—there is no difference between the two acts.
