Minimum Tuhr is Fifteen Days by Ijma
Ruling with proof: ijma establishes the minimum tuhr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum period of tuhr according to the Hanafi school, explain that it is established by ijma of the Companions, and identify the two interpretations of 'luzum' in the commentary.

Core Idea
The minimum tuhr is fifteen days by ijma — no valid ikhtilaf.

This passage establishes a foundational ruling in Hanafi fiqh: the minimum period of purity between menstrual cycles is fifteen days. This ruling is not a mere opinion but is based on the consensus (ijma) of the Companions, making it a definitive and universally accepted rule within the school. The commentary then addresses an interpretive point about the nature of this necessity (luzum), distinguishing between a Shariah-based and a customary understanding.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Find the explicit statement that the minimum tuhr is fifteen days. Note that it is not a mere recommendation but a fixed duration.
2
Recognize the Primary Proof: Ijma
The text cites 'ijma of the Companions' as the primary evidence. Understand that ijma is a definitive proof (qat'i) in Hanafi usul, making the ruling binding.
Ijma is the most authoritative proof after Quran and Sunnah.
3
Examine the Secondary Proof: 'Luzum'
The author adds 'because it is a duration' and mentions 'luzum' (necessity). The commentary discusses two interpretations: necessity of worship vs. customary necessity. Which interpretation is refuted and why?
The commentator rejects the first interpretation as a blunder.
4
Note the Authority and Consensus
Confirm that within the Hanafi school there is no ikhtilaf on this minimum. The ruling is mufta bihi and has the weight of zahir al-riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وأقل الطهر خمسة عشرة يوماً بإجماع الصحابة رضي الله عنهم ولأنه مدة) قوله: (ولأنه من اللزوم) كذا في الزيلعي والدرر واختلف في تفسيره قال بعضهم أي لزوم العبادة، وقال بعضهم بيانه أن مدة الإقامة من حيث هي لازمة والسفر قد يحدث أحياناً، وكذا الطهر بالنسبة إلى الحيض. يرجع إلى كون تلك المدة معتبرة في الشرع توقيتاً لما لزم ونظير هذا ما يجيء في باب الاستسقاء وباب عجز المكاتب أن ثلاثة أيام ضربت لإيلاء الأعذار كإمهال الخصم للدفع والمديون للقضاء، ومن فسر هذا اللزوم بلزوم العبادة فقد خبط خبط عشواء .اهـ ومراده به الرد على الأول، و حاصل كلامه يرجع إلى اللزوم العادي. وقال بعض الفضلاء : الظاهر أن المراد به الشرعي وأنه مراد وحاصله
His statement: (And the minimum of purity is fifteen days by consensus of the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them, and because it is a duration) His statement: (And because it is from necessity) — as in al-Zaylai and al-Durar, and they differed in its interpretation. Some said: i.e., necessity of worship. And some said: its explanation is that the period of residence as such is necessary, and travel may occur sometimes, and similarly purity in relation to hayd. It refers to that period being considered in the Shariah as a timing for what is necessary. And an analogy for this is what comes in the chapter of rain prayer and the chapter of the mukatib's incapacity: that three days were set for giving excuses, like giving the opponent time to defend and the debtor to pay. And whoever interprets this necessity as necessity of worship has blundered greatly. End. And his intention is to refute the first, and the summary of his words returns to customary necessity. And some virtuous said: the apparent is that what is meant is Shariah necessity, and that it is meant, and its summary.
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that the minimum period of purity (tuhr) between two menstrual cycles is fifteen days, established by the consensus (ijma) of the Companions. The text then discusses the proof 'lizoom' (necessity) and its interpretation. There is a difference of opinion over whether this necessity refers to the necessity of worship (i.e., that the woman must perform acts of worship after being clean for fifteen days) or a customary necessity (i.e., the natural pattern). The commentator refutes the first interpretation, arguing that it is a blunder, and explains that the correct understanding is that the Shariah has fixed this period based on the normal pattern (customary necessity). He draws an analogy to other areas where three days are given as a grace period, such as in rain prayer or the mukatab's case. The passage ends with a note that some scholars interpret it as Shariah necessity. Overall, the ruling is clear: the minimum tuhr is fifteen days, proven by ijma and rational analogy.

Key Terms
الطهر (al-tuhr): The period of purity between two menstrual bleedings.
اللزوم (al-luzum): Necessity or obligation; here it refers to the fixed duration of tuhr being necessary by custom or Shariah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Ten days
B) Fifteen days
C) Twenty days
D) One month

Key Takeaway
The minimum tuhr is fifteen days, established by ijma of the Companions, making it a definitive ruling with no valid ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Intercourse During Purity Before Habit Ends
Intra-Hanafi dispute on a hayd purity ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding intercourse during a purity occurring before the habitual duration, and identify the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
When blood stops within the habit, Abu Yusuf prohibits intercourse; Muhammad permits based on likelihood of menses continuing.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq presents a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute. The scenario: a woman whose habit is ten days sees only three days of blood and then becomes pure for six days. The question is whether intercourse is permissible during that purity. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad disagree, and the discussion explores the underlying reasoning and the meaning of 'jawaz'. Understanding this ikhtilaf is essential for correctly applying the rulings of hayd.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario
Identify the habit and the observed pattern: habit = 10 days, blood seen = 3 days, purity = 6 days. Note that the purity is within the habit.
This is the core factual situation for the dispute.
2
Identify the two positions
Abu Yusuf does not permit intercourse; Muhammad permits it. Mark the Imams and their views.
Both are from Zahir al-Riwayah.
3
Analyze the reasoning
Muhammad argues that the likelihood of menses returning after six days is greater than after four, so only the first three days are menses. For Abu Yusuf, the purity is still within the habit, so it may be interrupted menses.
The reasoning is based on taghlib al-wahm (prevailing probability).
4
Examine the second variant
Consider when purity is five days and habit nine days. Some say not permitted due to possibility of two more blood days; others permit, finding the extra day beyond the habit.
This shows the dispute extends to sub-cases.
5
Clarify the meaning of jawaz
The author critiques the citation of Ibn Wahban's versification, noting that it may only indicate karahah, not permissibility. 'Jawaz' can mean either halal or valid (sahih); here, permissibility as halal is not established.
Important distinction: sihha vs. hilliyah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فرع آخر : عادتها عشرة فرأت ثلاثة وطهرت ستة ؛ عند أبي يوسف لا يجوز قربانها، وعند محمد يجوز لأن المتوهم بعده من الحيض يوم الستة أغلب من الأربعة فيجعل الدم الأول فقط حيضاً بخلاف قول أبي يوسف ولو كانت طهرت خمسة وعادتها تسعة اختلفوا على قول محمد؛ قيل لا يباح قربانها لاحتمال الدم في يومين آخرين وقيل يباح وهو الأولى لأن اليوم الزائد موهوم خارج العادة . وفي نظم ابن وهبان إفادة أن المجيز للقربان يكره ا هـ . ما في فتح القدير. وعبارة النظم هذه: ولو طهرت بعد الثلاث وطهرت وعادتها لم تمض فالوطء يذكر لأنه أن کراهته بعض وينفيه بعضهم وبالصوم تأتي والصلاة وتذكر ولا يخفى بعد هذه الإفادة من النظم لأن ما فيه ليس هذه الصورة بل الاغتسال عقب الطهر من غير بيان أن الطهر غالب على الحيض أو لا، وهي المسألة التي قدمناها وهي الدم إذا انقطع لأقل من العادة هل وطؤها حرام أو مكروه، وليس فيه خلاف الإمامين ولم ينقل فيها الجواز أصلاً ونقل الكراهة لا يفيده لأن الجواز بمعنى الحل لا يجامع كراهة التحريم بخلافه بمعنى الصحة .
Another branch: Her habit is ten. She saw three [days] and became pure for six. According to Abu Yusuf, intercourse with her is not permitted. According to Muhammad, it is permitted because the presumed [resumption] of menses after the six days is more likely than after four, so only the first blood is considered menses, contrary to Abu Yusuf's statement. If she was pure for five and her habit is nine, there is disagreement regarding Muhammad's statement: some say intercourse is not permitted due to the possibility of blood in the remaining two days; others say it is permitted, and this is preferable because the extra day is presumptuous outside her habit. In the versification of Ibn Wahban, there is an indication that the one who permits it [considers it] disliked. That is what is in Fath al-Qadir. The wording of the versification: 'And if she becomes pure after three and purifies herself, and her habit has not passed, then intercourse is mentioned...' etc. And it is not hidden that this indication from the versification is remote because what is in it is not this scenario, but rather the ritual bath after purity, without clarifying whether the purity is predominant over menses or not. That is the question we presented: If blood stops for less than the habit, is intercourse with her haram or makruh? There is no disagreement of the two Imams in it, and permissibility is not transmitted at all. The transmission of karahah does not benefit [the argument for permissibility] because jawaz in the sense of halal does not coexist with karahah tahrim, contrary to it in the sense of sihha.
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a woman whose habit is ten days, but she sees blood for only three days and then becomes pure for six days. Abu Yusuf forbids intercourse during this purity, while Muhammad permits it. Muhammad's reasoning is that the probability of menses returning after six days is higher than after four, so only the first three days are counted as menses. The passage then discusses a variant where the purity is five days and the habit is nine, with some scholars saying intercourse is not permitted due to the possibility of two more days of blood, while others allow it because the extra day is beyond the habit. The author clarifies that the versification of Ibn Wahban, often cited, actually deals with a different scenario—ritual bath after purity—and does not directly support permissibility in this case. The core issue is whether 'jawaz' means halal or valid; the author notes that permissibility as halal cannot coexist with prohibitive dislike, whereas permissibility as validity can, but no explicit permissibility is reported from the two Imams. The commentary follows the author's logical progression: stating the variant, explaining the disagreement, critiquing the poetic evidence, and clarifying the terminological distinction.

Key Terms
قربانها (qurbānuhā): Intercourse with her
الوهم (al-wahm): Presumption or likelihood
الجواز (al-jawāz): Permissibility; can mean either halal (hilla) or valid (sihha)
الكراهة (al-karāha): Dislike; can be tanzihi (slight) or tahrimi (prohibitive)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Permissible because the purity is long
B) Not permissible because the purity is within the habit
C) Permissible only if she performs ghusl
D) Not permissible only if there is a possibility of pregnancy

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of intercourse during purity before the habitual duration ends is disputed within the Hanafi school: Abu Yusuf prohibits, Muhammad permits, and the permissibility may be limited to validity (sihha) rather than outright halal.

Minimum Duration of Purity (Tuhr): 15 Days – Ruling and Proof
Ruling on minimum tuhr with proof and secondary application

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that the minimum tuhr is 15 days, cite the Hanafi proof (consensus of the Companions and analogy with residence), and explain the secondary ruling when a woman's actual bleeding is shorter than her habit.

Core Idea
Minimum tuhr is 15 days by consensus; if a woman bleeds only 3 days, she still prays and fasts as a precaution.

The minimum duration of purity between menstrual periods is a foundational ruling in Hanafi taharah. This passage establishes that the minimum is definitively 15 days, supported by the consensus of the Companions and an analogy with the minimum duration of residence that affects prayer and fasting. Additionally, the text addresses a secondary scenario where a woman with a longer habit sees only 3 days of blood – explaining the precautionary ruling regarding intercourse and worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the minimum duration of purity (tuhr) between two menstrual periods. The ruling is that it is fixed at 15 days. Note that this is a wajib consideration – it is the minimum required for a valid tuhr.
The passage explicitly says 'وأقل الطهر خمسة عشرة يوماً'.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites two proofs: first, the consensus of the Companions ('بإجماع الصحابة'), which is a definitive source. Second, an analogy (qiyas) with the minimum duration of residence (15 days) that causes a traveler to complete prayers and fasts.
The qiyas is based on the principle that tuhr, like residence, is a period that affects obligations.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah of ijma
The consensus of the Companions is qat'i al-thubut and qat'i al-dalalah. It provides certainty that the minimum tuhr is 15 days. This is the primary proof.
The text states 'بإجماع الصحابة رضي الله عنهم' without further explanation, indicating its authoritative nature.
4
Understand the qiyas basis
The author compares tuhr to residence: both are durations that determine whether obligations like prayer and fasting are completed or missed. Since the minimum residence for a traveler to be considered a resident is 15 days (based on ahadith), tuhr is analogized to that.
This qiyas is mentioned in the passage: 'مدة الطهر نظير مدة الإقامة'.
5
Apply the secondary ruling
The passage discusses a scenario: if a woman whose habit is longer than 3 days bleeds only 3 days and then performs ghusl, it is disliked for her husband to have intercourse until her habit passes (as a precaution). However, she must pray and fast immediately (again as a precaution). This shows how the minimum tuhr interacts with individual habits.
The secondary ruling is based on precaution (ihtiyat) and is found in the digression about the word 'طهرت'.

المعتادة البركوي في رسالته في الحيض على خلافه فقال : الفصل الرابع في الاستمرار إن وقع في فطهرها وحيضها ما اعتادت في جميع الأحكام إن كان طهرها أقل من ستة أشهر وإلا فيرد إلى ستة أشهر إلا ساعة وحيضها بحاله .اهـ. وقال في حواشيه التي كتبها على تلك الرسالة : هذا قول محمد بن إبراهيم الميداني. قال في العناية وغيره وعليه الأكثر . وفي التتارخانية : وعليه الاعتماد اهـ. قوله: (وقد يقال الخ) قال في الشرنبلالية : فيه نظر لأن الاحتياط في أمر الفروج آكد خصوصاً عليه العلامة
His statement: 'The minimum of purity is fifteen days by consensus of the Companions, and because it is a duration...' (a textual note: 'and it found four [days] blood' as in al-Fath, but it should say 'three'.) His statement: 'and she purified (with tashdid)' i.e., she performed ghusl, and its dislike is the object mentioned at the end of the first couplet, and it is a poetic license. The pronoun refers to intercourse, and the pronoun 'denies it' also and 'she comes' and 'she mentions' for the one who purified. Al-Shurunbulali said in his commentary following Ibn al-Shihnah: The two couplets include two issues: The first scenario: if a menstruating woman becomes pure after three days and her habit is more than that and she performs ghusl, it is disliked for her husband or master to have intercourse with her as in al-Muhit until her habit passes, as a precaution. Some said: It is not disliked for her husband to have intercourse with her. The second: They agreed that she fasts, prays, and performs all acts of worship that are prohibited for a menstruating woman, taking precaution due to the possibility of non-return. His statement: 'and because it is of necessity' as in al-Zayla'i and al-Durar, and interpretation differed. Some said it means necessity of worship; others said its explanation is that the duration of residence is necessary by itself, and travel may happen occasionally, and similarly purity relative to menses. It returns to that duration being considered in the law as a time limit for what is necessary. An analogous case is what comes in the chapter of rain prayer and the chapter of the insolvent slave: that three days are set to excuse the opponent for defense and the debtor for payment. Whoever interprets this necessity as necessity of worship has made a grave mistake. His intention is to refute the first opinion, and the gist of his words returns to conventional necessity. Some scholars said: The apparent meaning is religious necessity, and it is intended, and its summary is necessity, so it became like the duration of residence. His statement: 'There is no limit for its maximum except when establishing a habit in the time of continuity' because it may extend to a year or two, and she may not menstruate at all, so it is not possible to estimate its maximum except due to necessity. His words include three issues: First: If a girl reaches puberty as a mustahadah, it will come later that her menses is estimated as ten from each month and the rest is purity. Second: If she reaches puberty seeing, for example, ten days blood and a year of purity, then bleeding continues, Abu 'Asmah and al-Qadi Abu Hazim said: her menses is what she saw and her purity is what she saw, so her waiting period ends in three years and thirty days. This is based on considering the divorce at the beginning of purity. The correct view is that if the period from the start of continuity to the pronouncement of divorce is known, this estimation is not necessary because it is possible that his calculation may make it the beginning of menses, so it would be more than mentioned by ten days, or the end of purity, so it would be estimated at thirty-one or thirty-two or thirty-three days, etc. If it is not known, then ten days should be added, placing him absolutely at the beginning of menses as a precaution, as in Fath al-Qadir. It may be said: Since divorce in other than... the first opinion. Its justification is what is in al-Mabsut: The duration of purity is analogous to the duration of residence in that it makes up what was missed of fasting and prayer, and it has been established by traditions that the minimum duration of residence is fifteen days, so likewise the minimum duration of purity. For this reason we estimated the minimum duration of travel, as each affects fasting and prayer. His statement: 'The second: If she reaches puberty etc.' i.e., then an estimate for the maximum of purity is made in this scenario. He said in al-Nahr: This is the statement of the majority, contrary to whoever said there is no limit for it. The place of disagreement is in estimating her purity regarding the completion of the waiting period, and there is no disagreement that it is estimated by something. There is a consideration because in al-Siraj it is said that according to Abu 'Asmah's statement, she leaves ten from the beginning of continuity and prays for a year, and so on; there is no end to the maximum of purity according to him in absolute terms. According to the majority of scholars, she leaves ten during continuity and prays for twenty, just as if she began at puberty as a mustahadah; they estimated the purity as twenty days. This difference in estimation is for prayer, not the waiting period. It is mentioned in al-Nihayah from al-Muhit and similarly in al-'Inayah that there is a difference in estimating her purity for the waiting period, and the fatwa is according to the statement of al-Hakim al-Shahid that it is estimated at two months, as the author will mention in the issue of the perplexed woman, along with the rest of the opinions. By this it appears that the disagreement is in both issues, not only in the perplexed woman, as the author's words and others like al-Zayla'i and Ibn al-Humam might suggest, as they only discussed the disagreement in the following issue. Therefore, some scholars alerted: The two months - meaning the view given for fatwa - applies to both the woman with a habit and the perplexed woman. As for the first, it is stated in al-'Inayah, al-Shumnni, etc.; as for the second, al-Zayla'i and al-Bahr, etc., stated it. So be aware. Then it is known that what he followed here from the statement of Abu 'Asmah, al-Birkawi in his treatise on menses followed the opposite: He said: The fourth chapter: On continuity: If it occurs, then her purity and menses are what she was accustomed to in all rulings, if her purity is less than six months; otherwise it is reduced to six months less an hour, and her menses remains as it was. He said in his glosses on that treatise: This is the statement of Muhammad ibn Ibrahim al-Maydani. He said in al-'Inayah and others, and the majority follow it. In al-Tatarakhaniyyah: It is relied upon. His statement: 'It may be said etc.' He said in al-Shurunbulaliyyah: There is a consideration because precaution in matters of private parts is more emphatic, especially...
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This lengthy passage covers two main rulings: the minimum duration of purity (tuhr) between menses is 15 days, and the maximum has no limit except when a habit must be established in cases of continuous bleeding (mustahadah). The author begins by stating the minimum tuhr, citing the consensus of the Companions and analogy with the minimum duration of residence (15 days) which causes a traveler to complete prayers and fasts. He includes a digression about the word 'طهرت' (she purified) discussing a secondary ruling: if a woman with a habit longer than 3 days sees only 3 days of blood and then performs ghusl, some scholars dislike intercourse until the habit passes, while others do not, but all agree she must pray and fast as a precaution. The passage then clarifies the correct interpretation of 'اللزوم' (necessity), rejecting the notion that it refers to worship and affirming it is conventional necessity similar to residence. Next, the author discusses the maximum tuhr: it is undefined normally, but in cases of continuous bleeding, estimates are needed. He presents three issues: (1) a novice mustahadah is given a 10-day menses and 20-day purity cycle; (2) a woman with a past habit of 10 days blood and a year purity then continuous bleeding; (3) later scholars' views. There is an intra-Hanafi disagreement: Abu 'Asmah and al-Qadi Abu Hazim say her menses and purity follow what she saw, while the majority estimate her waiting period at 2 months. The fatwa according to al-Hakim al-Shahid is 2 months for both the habit-holder and the perplexed woman. The passage concludes with al-Birkawi's view that if her purity is less than 6 months, she holds to her habit; otherwise, she is reduced to 6 months minus an hour, relying on al-Tatarakhaniyyah. The commentary follows the author's order: explaining the minimum, the secondary ruling, the necessity analogy, then the maximum and the various opinions.

Key Terms
طهر (tuhr): State of purity between menstrual periods
اللزوم (al-luzūm): Necessity or obligation, interpreted here as conventional necessity (al-luzūm al-'adi) as per the commentator.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum duration of purity (tuhr) between menstrual periods according to the consensus of the Companions?
A) 10 days
B) 15 days
C) 20 days
D) 30 days

Key Takeaway
The minimum tuhr is definitively 15 days by ijma; a woman with a shorter bleed must pray and fast but intercourse is disliked until her habit passes.

Module 4 · Lesson 720

Taharah — Purification
advanced
15 min
Maximum Tuhr and Estimation in Continuous Bleeding
Ruling on maximum tuhr with intra-Hanafi dispute and fatwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the maximum tuhr is undefined, identify the three scenarios requiring estimation, and state the mufta bihi (2 months) for 'iddah and prayer in mustahadah.

Core Idea
Maximum tuhr has no limit except in continuous bleeding, where the majority estimate 20 days purity per month and 2 months for 'iddah.

While the minimum tuhr is fixed, the maximum is generally unlimited — a woman may remain pure for years. However, when a woman experiences continuous bleeding (istihadah), the law must estimate her tuhr to determine her 'iddah and prayer obligations. This passage presents the intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu 'Asmah, who follows the observed habit, and the majority who estimate a 20-day cycle, with the fatwa eventually settling on a 2-month estimate for 'iddah.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule for maximum tuhr
The author states: 'There is no limit for its maximum except when establishing a habit in the time of continuity.' Normally, tuhr can last years or a lifetime, so no maximum is set.
This is because tuhr is not inherently limited; it is defined by the absence of menses.
2
Identify the three scenarios requiring estimation
The passage outlines three issues: (1) a girl who reaches puberty as a mustahadah – her menses is estimated as 10 days per month, purity 20 days. (2) a woman with a past habit of 10 days menses and a year purity, then continuous bleeding – the dispute arises. (3) the perplexed woman (mutahayyirah) – mentioned later.
The third scenario is not detailed here but referenced.
3
Explain the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu 'Asmah and al-Qadi Abu Hazim hold that her menses and purity follow what she actually saw (10 days menses, 1 year purity). Therefore, her 'iddah (if divorced) would be three years and thirty days. The majority disagree and estimate her purity at 20 days per month, making 'iddah 2 months.
The dispute hinges on whether to follow exact observation or to use a standard estimate based on ihtiyat (precaution).
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The fatwa is on the majority view that the maximum tuhr in continuity is estimated at 2 months for 'iddah, and for prayer the estimate is 20 days purity per month. This is the view of al-Hakim al-Shahid, supported by many later authorities.
The passage mentions that al-Hakim al-Shahid's view applies to both the woman with a habit and the perplexed woman.
5
Note the later opinion of al-Birkawi
Al-Birkawi in his treatise on menses holds that if the observed purity is less than 6 months, she follows her habit; if more than 6 months, her purity is reduced to 6 months less an hour. This is attributed to Muhammad ibn Ibrahim al-Maydani and relied upon in al-Tatarakhaniyyah.
This shows the development of the fatwa over time.

هي لازمة والسفر قد يحدث أحياناً، وكذا الطهر بالنسبة إلى الحيض. يرجع إلى كون تلك المدة معتبرة في الشرع توقيتاً لما لزم ونظير هذا ما يجيء في باب الاستسقاء وباب عجز المكاتب أن ثلاثة أيام ضربت لإيلاء الأعذار كإمهال الخصم للدفع والمديون للقضاء، ومن فسر هذا اللزوم بلزوم العبادة فقد خبط خبط عشواء .اهـ ومراده به الرد على الأول، و حاصل كلامه يرجع إلى اللزوم العادي. وقال بعض الفضلاء : الظاهر أن المراد به الشرعي وأنه مراد وحاصله اللزوم فصار كمدة الإقامة. قوله : ( ولا حد لأكثره إلا عند نصب العادة في زمن الاستمرار) لأنه قد يمتد إلى سنة وإلى سنتين وقد لا تحيض أصلاً فلا يمكن تقديراً أكثره إلا عند الضرورة. وشمل كلامه ثلاث مسائل : الأولى إذا بلغت مستحاضة فستأتي أنه يقدر حيضها بعشرة من كل شهر وباقيه طهر والثانية إذا بلغت برؤية عشرة مثلاً دماً وسنة طهراً ثم استمر بها الدم فقال أبو عصمة والقاضي أبو حازم حيضها ما رأت وطهرها ما رأت فتنقضي عدتها بثلاث سنين وثلاثين يوماً. وهذا بناء على اعتباره للطلاق أول الطهر، والحق أنه إن كان من أول الاستمرار إلى إيقاع الطلاق مضبوطاً فليس هذا التقدير بلازم لجواز كون حسابه يوجب كونه أول الحيض فيكون أكثر من المذكور بعشرة أيام أو آخر الطهر فيقدر بسنتين وأحد وثلاثين أو اثنين أو ثلاثة وثلاثين ونحو ذلك، وإن لم يكن مضبوطاً فينبغي أن تزاد العشرة إنزالاً له مطلقاً أول الحيض احتياطاً كذا في فتح القدير. وقد يقال : لما كان الطلاق في في غيرها لا القائل الأول، ووجهه ما في المبسوط مدة الطهر نظير مدة الإقامة من حيث إنها تفيد ما كان سقط من الصوم والصلاة، وقد ثبت بالأخبار أن أقل مدة الإقامة خمسة عشر يوماً فكذلك أقل مدة الطهر، ولهذا قدرنا أقل مدة السفر فإن كل واحد منهما يؤثر في الصوم والصلاة اهـ. قوله : (والثانية إذا بلغت الخ) أي فإنه يقدر لأكثر الطهر حد في هذه الصورة قال في النهر : وهذا قول العامة خلافاً لمن قال لأحد له ومحل الخلاف في تقدير طهرها في حق انقضاء العدة ولا خلاف أنه يقدر بشيء اهـ. وفيه نظر لما في السراج من أنه على قول أبي عصمة تدع من أول الاستمرار عشرة وتصلي سنة هكذا دأبها لا غاية لأكثر الطهر عنده على الإطلاق، وعند عامة العلماء تدع في الاستمرار عشرة وتصلي عشرين كما لو ابتدأت مع البلوغ مستحاضة فقدروا الطهر بعشرين اهـ. وهذا الاختلاف في التقدير للصلاة وهو غير العدة وذكر في النهاية عن المحيط وكذا في العناية اختلافاً في تقدير طهرها للعدة وأن الفتوى على قول الحاكم الشهيد أنه مقدر بشهرين كما سيذكره المؤلف في مسألة المتحيرة مع بقية الأقوال وبه يظهر أن المفتى به - راجع لكل من المعتادة والمتحيرة. أما الأول فقد نص عليه في العناية والشمني وغيرهما، وأما الثاني فقد نص الزيلعي والبحر وغيرهما .اهـ. فتنبه . ثم علم أن ما مشى عليه هنا من قول أبي عصمة مشى Commentary
This lengthy passage covers two main rulings: the minimum duration of purity (tuhr) between menses is 15 days, and the maximum has no limit except when a habit must be established in cases of continuous bleeding (mustahadah). The author begins by stating the minimum tuhr, citing the consensus of the Companions and analogy with the minimum duration of residence (15 days) which causes a traveler to complete prayers and fasts. He includes a digression about the word 'طهرت' (she purified) discussing a secondary ruling: if a woman with a habit longer than 3 days sees only 3 days of blood and then performs ghusl, some scholars dislike intercourse until the habit passes, while others do not, but all agree she must pray and fast as a precaution. The passage then clarifies the correct interpretation of 'اللزوم' (necessity), rejecting the notion that it refers to worship and affirming it is conventional necessity similar to residence. Next, the author discusses the maximum tuhr: it is undefined normally, but in cases of continuous bleeding, estimates are needed. He presents three issues: (1) a novice mustahadah is given a 10-day menses and 20-day purity cycle; (2) a woman with a past habit of 10 days blood and a year purity then continuous bleeding; (3) later scholars' views. There is an intra-Hanafi disagreement: Abu 'Asmah and al-Qadi Abu Hazim say her menses and purity follow what she saw, while the majority estimate her waiting period at 2 months. The fatwa according to al-Hakim al-Shahid is 2 months for both the habit-holder and the perplexed woman. The passage concludes with al-Birkawi's view that if her purity is less than 6 months, she holds to her habit; otherwise, she is reduced to 6 months minus an hour, relying on al-Tatarakhaniyyah. The commentary follows the author's order: explaining the minimum, the secondary ruling, the necessity analogy, then the maximum and the various opinions.

Key Terms
طهر (tuhr): State of purity between menstrual periods
مستحاضة (mustaḥāḍah): A woman experiencing chronic vaginal bleeding (istihadah) that is not menstrual.
الاستمرار (al-istimrār): Continuity of bleeding, i.e., blood that does not stop at the usual time.

Taharah — Purification

The Mudallala: Rulings for a Woman Who Forgets Her Menstrual Pattern
Rulings for a woman who forgets her menstrual pattern

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules for a mudallala to determine when she prays with wudu, when she prays with ghusl, and when she abandons prayer based on certainty and doubt.

Core Idea
Certainty overrides doubt: the mudallala prays with wudu when certain of purity, abandons prayer when certain of menstruation, and uses ijtihad when in doubt.

Imagine a woman who has completely forgotten how many days her menstruation lasts or when it occurs in the month. She is no longer certain of her pattern. This is the mudallala (perplexed woman). The Hanafi school provides detailed rules so she can continue her worship correctly, balancing certainty and doubt. This lesson unpacks the foundational principles and the key subcases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types of confusion
The mudallala may be confused about the number of days (al-idlal bi al-‘adad), the timing within the month (al-idlal bi al-makan), or both (al-idlal bihima). Recognize which category applies to a given scenario.
Each type leads to a different calculation.
2
Apply the principle of certainty
When she is certain of being in a state of purity, she prays and fasts normally with wudu. When certain of menstruation, she abandons both. When in doubt, she must exert ijtihad (taharri) to decide.
Certainty overrides doubt – this is a core usul principle.
3
Determine the three states of doubt
Doubt can be between purity and menstruation, or it can also include the possibility of exiting menstruation. The latter requires ghusl for each prayer.
Ghusl is required because exit from menstruation is a state requiring purification.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on ghusl frequency
Some early scholars suggested ghusl every hour, but the relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is to perform ghusl for each prayer time when doubt includes possible exit from menstruation.
This is based on practicality and istihsan.
5
Apply the rules to a sample calculation
For confusion in number only, if she knows her period occurs once a month but forgets the count, she leaves prayer for three certain days, then prays with ghusl for seven days, then prays with wudu for twenty days, etc.
The exact numbers depend on the specific confusion type.

And the third matter is the case of the mudallala, also called the perplexed woman. It has three chapters: First, confusion in number. Second, confusion in place. Third, confusion in both. The principle is that whenever she is certain of being in a pure state at a time, she prays in it with wudu at the time of each prayer and fasts. Whenever she is certain of menstruation at a time, she abandons both in it. Whenever she doubts whether it is a time of menstruation or purity, she exercises ijtihad. If she has no inclination, she prays in it with wudu at the time of each prayer and fasts, but then makes up for it. Whenever she doubts whether it is menstruation, purity, or exit from menstruation, she prays in it with ghusl for each prayer, because it is possible that it is the time of exit from menstruation. Her husband does not approach her at all due to the possibility of menstruation. (Commentary continues with various explanations and subcases regarding number and place confusion, ending abruptly.)
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq introduces the mudallala (perplexed woman) who has forgotten her menstrual pattern. The commentator outlines three types of confusion: in the number of days, in the timing within the month, or both. The foundational principle is that certainty overrides doubt: when she is certain of being in a pure state, she prays and fasts normally with wudu; when certain of menstruation, she abandons both; when in doubt, she must exert ijtihad (taharri). If she has no opinion, she prays with wudu and later makes up the prayer, but when doubt includes the possibility of exiting menstruation, she must perform ghusl for each prayer to be safe. The commentary then delves into the first form of confusion, explaining that if she knows her period occurs once a month but forgets the count, she leaves prayer for three certain days, then prays with ghusl for seven days due to uncertainty, then prays with wudu for twenty days with certainty of purity. The passage continues with multiple subcases and scholarly discussions, though the OCR ends abruptly.

Key Terms
المضللة (al-mudallala): A woman who has forgotten the count or timing of her menstrual days and is uncertain about her state.
المحيرة (al-muhayyira): Synonym for al-mudallala, the perplexed woman who cannot determine her menstrual pattern.
الاضلال بالعدد (al-idlal bi al-‘adad): Confusion regarding the number of days of menstruation or purity.
الاضلال بالمكان (al-idlal bi al-makan): Confusion regarding the time (place within the month) of menstruation or purity.
الاضلال بهما (al-idlal bihima): Confusion in both number and time simultaneously.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The mudallala's rulings hinge on the degree of certainty: she prays with wudu when certain of purity, abandons prayer when certain of menstruation, and uses ghusl when doubt includes possible exit from menstruation.

Ruling for Mustihadah with Known Tuhr but Unknown Hayd
Ruling with schedule for mustihadah of known tuhr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the complete prayer schedule for a mustihadah who knows her tuhr is 15 days but does not know her hayd duration, and explain the legal reasoning based on yaqin and shakk.

Core Idea
When hayd is unknown but tuhr is known, mustihadah follows a fixed schedule to ensure no prayer in impurity.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling for a woman who has lost track of her menstrual period length but knows that her period of purity between cycles is exactly 15 days. The jurists derive a precise schedule that balances caution with practicality, relying on the principle that certainty is not removed by doubt. You will learn the step-by-step schedule and its rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and legal problem
A mustihadah knows her tuhr is 15 days but does not know her hayd duration. The legal issue is how to determine when she should pray and whether to perform ghusl or wudu.
The schedule is built on the minimum and maximum possible hayd (3-10 days) and the fixed tuhr.
2
Outline the initial 21-day schedule
She abandons prayer for 3 days (minimum hayd), then prays 7 days with ghusl (possible hayd days 4-10), then 8 days with wudu (certain tuhr after 10 days), then 3 days with wudu due to doubt (days 19-21 could be hayd or tuhr).
This ensures she covers all possibilities without unnecessary ghusl.
3
Explain the branching after day 21
If her actual hayd is 3 days, her next tuhr starts at day 22. If her actual hayd is 10 days, she continues for 14 more days (days 22-35) with ghusl for every prayer due to doubt.
The branching accounts for both extremes of hayd.
4
Describe the pattern after day 35
After day 35, she prays one day (day 36) with wudu with certainty (clear tuhr), then 3 days (37-39) with wudu due to doubt, then perpetually performs ghusl before every prayer forever.
This perpetual ghusl arises because every hour could be the moment she exits hayd.
5
Summarize the legal principle
The schedule is built on yaqin (certainty) and shakk (doubt). When certainty of tuhr exists, wudu suffices; when doubt about hayd persists, ghusl is obligatory to avoid invalid prayer.
This aligns with the Hanafi principle bahwa al-yaqin la yazulu bi al-shakk.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وثانيها إذا علمت أن طهرها خمسة عشر ولم تعلم عدد حيضها فإنها تدع ثلاثة أيام، ثم تصلي سبعة بالغسل، ثم تصلي ثمانية بالوضوء باليقين، ثم تصلي ثلاثة أيام بالوضوء بالشك فبلغ ذلك أحداً وعشرين يوماً، فإن كان حيضها ثلاثة فابتداء طهرها الثاني بعد احد وعشرين يوماً، وإن كان حيضها عشرة فابتداء طهرها الثاني بعد خمسة وثلاثين فتصلي في هذه الأربعة عشر التي بعد الأحد والعشرين بالاغتسال لكل صلاة للتردد بين الثلاثة، ثم تصلي يوماً بالوضوء لوقت كل صلاة بيقين لتيقنها بالطهر لأنه اليوم الخامس عشر منه الذي هو السادس والثلاثون ثم تصلي ثلاثة بالوضوء لوقت كل صلاة للتردد فيها بين الحيض والطهر، ثم تغتسل لكل صلاة أبداً لأنه ما من ساعة إلا ويتوهم أنه وقت خروجها من الحيض.
And the second: if she knows that her tuhr is fifteen and does not know the number of her hayd, then she leaves prayer for three days, then prays seven with ghusl, then prays eight with wudu with certainty, then prays three days with wudu due to doubt, so that totals twenty-one days. If her hayd is three, then the start of her second tuhr is after twenty-one days. If her hayd is ten, then the start of her second tuhr is after thirty-five. So she prays during these fourteen after the twenty-one with ghusl for every prayer due to doubt between the three, then prays one day with wudu for the time of each prayer with certainty, because she is certain of tuhr, as it is the fifteenth day of it which is the thirty-sixth, then she prays three with wudu for the time of each prayer due to doubt between hayd and tuhr, then she performs ghusl for every prayer forever, because there is no hour except that she imagines it is the time of her exit from hayd.
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling (hukm) for a mustihadah who has lost track of her hayd duration but knows her tuhr is a fixed 15 days. The ruling is based on the principle that certainty (yaqin) is not removed by doubt (shakk). The text outlines a detailed schedule: she abandons prayer for 3 days (minimum hayd), then prays 7 days with ghusl (since those could be hayd), then 8 days with wudu (certain tuhr), then 3 days with wudu (doubtful). After 21 days, if her hayd was 3, her new cycle starts; if it was 10, she continues with ghusl for 14 more days, then one day certain tuhr, then 3 doubtful, then perpetual ghusl. This schedule ensures she never prays in a state of impurity (hadath) while avoiding unnecessary ghusl. The ruling is from the Hanafi school, relying on the principle of istishab (continuity of state) and the known minimums/maximums of hayd and tuhr.

Key Terms
طهر (tuhr): The period of purity between menstruations, known as the intermenstrual period.
الوضوء باليقين (al-wudu' bil-yaqin): Performing wudu and prayer with certainty of being in a state of tuhr, not hayd.
الاغتسال لكل صلاة (al-ightisal li kull salat): Performing ghusl before each obligatory prayer due to doubt about the end of hayd.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
For the mustihadah with known tuhr but unknown hayd, the Hanafi school prescribes a fixed schedule balancing certainty and doubt to preserve the integrity of prayer.

The Mustihadah with Known Hayd but Unknown Tuhr
Ruling for a mustihadah with known hayd but unknown tuhr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a mustihadah who knows her hayd is three days but does not know her tuhr duration, and apply the schedule of prayer abandonment, wudu, and ghusl.

Core Idea
When tuhr is unknown, the mustihadah follows a fixed schedule based on the minimum tuhr of 15 days.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq discusses a specific case of istihadah: a woman who knows her menstrual period is exactly three days but has no knowledge of her pure period. Since she cannot rely on a known pattern, the Hanafi school prescribes a detailed schedule to ensure she prays correctly while avoiding ritual impurity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the known parameters
The woman knows her hayd is exactly 3 days but does not know her tuhr length. This triggers the need for a schedule based on the minimum tuhr of 15 days.
2
Analyze the first 3 days
She abandons prayer for the first 3 days from the start of continuous bleeding because she is certain those days are hayd.
3
Determine the next 15 days
She prays with wudu for the next 15 days because she is certain of purity (tuhr) for at least the minimum duration of 15 days.
The certainty comes from the Hanafi minimum tuhr of 15 days.
4
Examine the doubtful period
After 15 days of certain tuhr, she prays with wudu for 3 days due to doubt between hayd and tuhr. These 3 days could be hayd or tuhr.
5
Justify the perpetual ghusl
From day 21 onward, she must perform ghusl before every prayer because she could exit hayd at any moment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ورابعها إذا علمت أن حيضها ثلاثة ولا تعلم عدد طهرها فإنها تدع الصلاة ثلاثة أيام من أول الاستمرار، ثم تصلي خمسة عشر يوماً بالوضوء لوقت كل صلاة لتيقنها بالطهر فيه، ثم تصلي ثلاثة بالوضوء للتردد بين الحيض والطهر، ثم تغتسل لكل صلاة أبداً لتوهم خروجها عن الحيض كل ساعة.
And the fourth: if she knows that her hayd is three and does not know the number of her tuhr, then she abandons prayer for three days from the beginning of the continuous bleeding, then prays fifteen days with wudu for the time of each prayer because she is certain of tuhr therein, then prays three with wudu due to doubt between hayd and tuhr, then she performs ghusl for every prayer forever due to the likelihood of her exit from hayd every hour.
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling for a mustihadah who knows her hayd is exactly 3 days but does not know her tuhr length. She abandons prayer for 3 days (the known hayd), then prays 15 days with wudu (since she knows she is pure for at least 15 days, the minimum tuhr), then 3 days with wudu due to doubt (could be hayd or tuhr), and then from day 21 onwards she must perform ghusl before every prayer (since she could exit hayd at any moment). This schedule respects the Hanafi minimum for tuhr (15 days) and the principle of precaution in worship.

Key Terms
الاستمرار (al-istimrar): The continuous bleeding from the beginning of the condition of istihadah.
تيقنها بالطهر (tayaqqubuha bil-tuhr): Her certainty of being in a state of purity based on the known minimum tuhr of 15 days.

Key Takeaway
For a mustihadah with known hayd but unknown tuhr, the Hanafi schedule uses the minimum tuhr of 15 days to establish certainty, followed by a period of precaution, then perpetual ghusl.

The Forgotten Hayd Pattern: Precautionary Schedule for the Mustihadah
Ruling for a mustihadah who used to have hayd once a month but forgot the count

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling for a mustihadah with a forgotten hayd pattern by calculating the prescribed precautionary schedule.

Core Idea
When hayd history is lost, the schedule is ruled by doubt: first 3 days wudu, next 7 days ghusl, then wudu to month's end.

This lesson addresses a specific case of istihadah: a woman who knows she used to menstruate once per month but has forgotten both the duration and whether it occurred at the beginning or end. The Hanafi school provides a precise schedule to ensure she prays validly while accounting for the possibility that any day could be hayd. The key insight is that hayd cannot exceed 10 days, so the middle ten days of the month are certain tuhr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of mustihadah
Confirm that the woman knows her hayd frequency (once per month) but has forgotten the exact days and duration. This creates doubt about whether any given day is hayd or tuhr.
This is distinct from a mustihadah with a known habit.
2
Mark the doubtful zones
Since hayd maximum is 10 days, the first ten days (days 1-10) and last ten days (days 21-30) are doubtful. The middle ten days (days 11-20) are certain tuhr.
الوسطى refers to days 11-20.
3
Construct the precautionary schedule
For the doubtful first ten days: perform wudu (for tuhr) for the first 3 days, then ghusl (for possible hayd) for the next 7 days. For the certain tuhr middle days and second doubtful zone: perform wudu until the end of the month, then perform one ghusl at month's end to cover the possibility that hayd ended sometime in the last ten days.
The schedule ensures she never prays during actual hayd.
4
Determine prayer validity
On days she does wudu, she prays as a mustihadah (wudu for each prayer). On days she does ghusl, she does not pray (considered hayd). The final ghusl at month's end allows her to resume prayer for the next month.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن علمت أنها كانت تحيض في كل شهر مرة من أوله أو آخره ولا تدري العدد تتوضأ ثلاثة أيام في أول الشهر لتردد حالها فيه بين الحيض والطهر، ثم تغتسل سبعة أيام للتردد بين الثلاثة ثم تتوضأ إلى آخر الشهر وتغتسل مرة واحدة لتمام الشهر لجواز خروجها من الحيض لأن الشك في العشرة الأولى والأخيرة لا في الوسطى.
And if she knows that she used to menstruate once every month at its beginning or end, and she does not know the count, she performs wudu for three days at the beginning of the month due to the doubt of her state therein between hayd and tuhr, then she performs ghusl for seven days due to doubt between the three, then she performs wudu until the end of the month and performs ghusl once at the completion of the month because it is possible that she has exited from hayd, because doubt is in the first ten days and the last ten, not in the middle.
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
In this scenario, the woman knows she used to menstruate once a month but has forgotten both the duration and whether it occurred at the beginning or end. She cannot pinpoint her hayd. The ruling prescribes a precautionary schedule: she does wudu for the first 3 days (doubtful), then ghusl for the next 7 days (covers possibility of hayd up to 10 days), then wudu for the rest of the month until the end, concluding with one ghusl at month's end. The reasoning is that doubt exists only in the first and last ten days of the month, not the middle (days 11-20). This is based on the Hanafi principle that hayd maximum is 10 days.

Key Terms
العشرة الأولى والأخيرة (al-asharat al-ula wa al-akhirah): The first ten days and last ten days of the month, which are doubtful for hayd.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) 3 days

Key Takeaway
A mustihadah with a forgotten hayd pattern must follow a fixed precautionary schedule of wudu (3 days), ghusl (7 days), wudu (remaining days), and a concluding ghusl at month's end.

The Principle of Idlaal bil-Makan: Certainty and Doubt
General principle for mustahadah with idlaal bil-makan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for a mustahadah who knows the number of her hayd days but forgot their location, and apply the principle of double or less than double to determine certainty of hayd.

Core Idea
When a mustahadah forgets the place of her hayd, she follows a schedule based on whether the lost interval is within double the number — certainty guides her prayer and fasting.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq deals with a specific form of confusion (idlaal) where a woman knows how many days her menses lasted but cannot recall where in the month they occurred. The Hanafi school provides a detailed schedule to resolve the doubt, rooted in the principle of certainty (yaqin) prevailing over doubt (shakk). In this lesson, we will unpack the foundational logic before examining the schedules for each possible duration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize that the woman knows the number of her hayd days (e.g., 3, 4, 5...) but does not know their specific place within the month. This is 'idlaal bil-makan'.
She must have a regular habit (number) but has forgotten the timing.
2
Apply the principle of double
If the period of loss is equal to or more than double the number of her hayd days, she has no certainty of hayd anywhere in that period. If less than double, she is certain of hayd on some days.
Example: losing 3 days in 6 or more = no certainty; losing 3 in 5 = certainty on one day (the 3rd day).
3
Derive the schedule from the principle
When there is no certainty, all days are treated as doubtful: she prays with wudu (in case she is in tuhr) and performs ghusl for each prayer (in case she is in hayd). When there is certainty, some days are definitely hayd (must abandon prayer/fasting) and others are doubtful.
The schedules reflect this: for longer known durations, the number of certain hayd days increases.
4
Understand the 10-day boundary
In the Hanafi school, hayd maximum is 10 days. After 10 days, the blood is considered istihada. Therefore, schedules only extend to the 10th day; beyond that she is certain of tuhr.
This explains why for 4 and 5 days, she performs ghusl until the end of the ten, not the whole month.

Source Text

His statement: And the second is idlaal bil-makan, its basis is: whenever she loses her days within double of the number or more, and whenever she loses her days within less than double of the number, then she is certain of hayd in something from it, such as if she lost three in five, then she is certain of hayd on the third day, for it is the beginning or end of hayd. If she knows that her days were three and does not know their place in the month, she prays three days from the beginning of the month with wudu for each prayer due to doubt between hayd and tuhr, then she performs ghusl for twenty-seven for every prayer due to the likelihood of her exit from hayd every hour. If she knows that her days are four, she performs wudu in the four, then performs ghusl for every prayer until the end of the ten. Similarly, if she knows that her days are five, she performs wudu for five, then performs ghusl until the end of the ten. If she knows that her days are six, she performs wudu for four from the beginning of the ten and abandons prayer and fasting for two days due to her certainty of hayd in them, as we transmitted from the principle, then she performs ghusl for four for every prayer due to the likelihood of her exit from hayd every hour. If she knows that her days are seven, she prays with wudu for three days from their beginning and abandons four days due to certainty of hayd in them, then she performs ghusl for three days for every prayer. And on this analogy for eight and nine.
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This long passage combines commentary and the main ruling for the second category: idlaal bil-makan (confusion regarding the place of hayd days within the month). The section begins with marginal commentary clarifying earlier rulings and correcting textual variants. Then it presents the core ruling: if a woman knows the number of her hayd days (e.g., 3, 4, 5, etc.) but does not know where in the month they occur, the ruling depends on whether the number of lost days is within double (ضعف) or less than double relative to the period of doubt. If lost in more than double (e.g., 3 days in 6 or more), she has no certainty of hayd anywhere. If lost in less than double (e.g., 3 in 5), she is certain of hayd on one day (the middle day). Then for each known duration (3 to 9), a specific schedule is given. For example, if her hayd used to be 3 days but she forgot their place, she prays with wudu for the first 3 days (doubt), then performs ghusl for the remaining 27 days of the month. If her hayd is 4 days, she does wudu for 4 days and ghusl until the 10th day. The pattern uses the principle of certainty (yaqin) and doubt (shakk), assigning wudu for doubtful days and ghusl when the possibility of hayd arises. The schedule is based on the maximum hayd of 10 days in the Hanafi school; after the 10th day, she is certain of tuhr. The commentary discusses textual variations but confirms the overall method.

Key Terms
الاضلال بالمكان (idlaal bil-makan): The state where a mustihadah forgets the time (position within the month) of her hayd, though she may remember its duration.
ضعف العدد (di'f al-`adad): Double the number of her hayd days; if she lost days in a period equal to or more than double, she has no certainty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
When a mustahadah knows her hayd duration but not its place, Hanafi fiqh provides a schedule based on certainty and doubt, maintaining the validity of her worship.

Detailed Schedules for Idlaal bil-Makan (3-9 Days)
Specific schedules for idlaal bil-makan durations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to recite the specific prayer and fast schedule for a mustahadah with idlaal bil-makan for hayd durations of 3, 4, 5, 6, 7, 8, and 9 days.

Core Idea
For known durations of 3-5 days, all days are doubtful; for 6-9 days, some days are certain hayd and must be abandoned.

This lesson consolidates the specific schedules given in the passage for each possible known duration of hayd when the location is forgotten. Knowing these schedules is essential for a mufti or student of fiqh to advise a woman in this situation.

Guided Path
1
List the given durations
The passage covers durations from 3 to 9 days. 10 is not included because it would be the entire maximum and there is no doubt.
2
Memorize the three categories
For 3-5 days: no abandon days. For 6-9: abandon days appear. For 3: wudu 3, ghusl 27. For 4: wudu 4, ghusl until end of ten (6 days). For 5: wudu 5, ghusl until end of ten (5 days).
3
For 6-9, note the pattern
For 6: wudu 4, abandon 2, ghusl 4. For 7: wudu 3, abandon 4, ghusl 3. For 8: (by analogy) wudu 2, abandon 6, ghusl 2. For 9: wudu 1, abandon 8, ghusl 1.
The pattern ensures that the total days in the first ten are accounted for, and the abandon days represent the minimum certain hayd days based on the overlap of possible positions.
4
Understand the basis
The pattern ensures that the total days in the first ten are accounted for, and the abandon days represent the minimum certain hayd days based on the overlap of possible positions.

Then he completed the speech on the issues as what the shaykh mentioned here, so let it be examined. End. And it is consistent with what we said. Then I saw in al-Tatarikhaniyyah that he explicitly stated the ten. His statement: (as when she has istihadah and forgot the number of her days and her place) is conditioned by her forgetting that to be from idlaal bihima, otherwise the rulings that he mentioned include when she knows her habit in hayd and tuhr also, as in al-Tatarikhaniyyah: She came seeking a fatwa while she does not know the place of her hayd nor the place of her tuhr, and she knows her habit in hayd and tuhr or she does not know, then she does taharrur etc. And we will mention the ruling of when she knows in the issue of fasting. His statement: And the second is idlaal bil-makan, its basis is: whenever she loses her days within double of the number or more, and whenever she loses her days within less than double of the number, then she is certain of hayd in something from it, such as if she lost three in five, then she is certain of hayd on the third day, for it is the beginning or end of hayd. If she knows that her days were three and does not know their place in the month, she prays three days from the beginning of the month with wudu for each prayer due to doubt between hayd and tuhr, then she performs ghusl for twenty-seven for every prayer due to the likelihood of her exit from hayd every hour. If she knows that her days are four, she performs wudu in the four, then performs ghusl for every prayer until the end of the ten. Similarly, if she knows that her days are five, she performs wudu for five, then performs ghusl until the end of the ten. If she knows that her days are six, she performs wudu for four from the beginning of the ten and abandons prayer and fasting for two days due to her certainty of hayd in them, as we transmitted from the principle, then she performs ghusl for four for every prayer due to the likelihood of her exit from hayd every hour. If she knows that her days are seven, she prays with wudu for three days from their beginning and abandons four days due to certainty of hayd in them, then she performs ghusl for three days for every prayer. And on this analogy for eight and nine.
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This long passage combines commentary and the main ruling for the second category: idlaal bil-makan (confusion regarding the place of hayd days within the month). The section begins with marginal commentary clarifying earlier rulings and correcting textual variants. Then it presents the core ruling: if a woman knows the number of her hayd days (e.g., 3, 4, 5, etc.) but does not know where in the month they occur, the ruling depends on whether the number of lost days is within double (ضعف) or less than double relative to the period of doubt. If lost in more than double (e.g., 3 days in 6 or more), she has no certainty of hayd anywhere. If lost in less than double (e.g., 3 in 5), she is certain of hayd on one day (the middle day). Then for each known duration (3 to 9), a specific schedule is given. For example, if her hayd used to be 3 days but she forgot their place, she prays with wudu for the first 3 days (doubt), then performs ghusl for the remaining 27 days of the month. If her hayd is 4 days, she does wudu for 4 days and ghusl until the 10th day. The pattern uses the principle of certainty (yaqin) and doubt (shakk), assigning wudu for doubtful days and ghusl when the possibility of hayd arises. The schedule is based on the maximum hayd of 10 days in the Hanafi school; after the 10th day, she is certain of tuhr. The commentary discusses textual variations but confirms the overall method.

Key Terms
الاضلال بالمكان (idlaal bil-makan): The state where a mustihadah forgets the time (position within the month) of her hayd, though she may remember its duration.
ضعف العدد (di'f al-`adad): Double the number of her hayd days; if she lost days in a period equal to or more than double, she has no certainty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) 8 days
B) 9 days
C) 1 day
D) 7 days

Key Takeaway
The schedules for mustahadah with idlaal bil-makan are precisely defined for each known duration, ensuring that worship is performed with proper attention to certainty and doubt.

Rulings for a Mustihadah with Idlaal Bihima
Rulings for a mustihadah with complete confusion of hayd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rules for a mustihadah who has forgotten both the number and timing of her hayd, and identify which rulings are based on precaution (ihtiyat).

Core Idea
When a mustihadah forgets both number and place, she relies on taharrur and follows strict precaution to ensure validity of worship.

The case of idlaal bihima occurs when a mustihadah cannot recall the number of hayd days or their timing. The Hanafi school gives detailed rulings to preserve the sanctity of worship while managing uncertainty. This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq outlines the core rules: she must perform taharrur, and if that fails, follow a set regimen regarding ghusl, prayer, fasting, and Quranic recitation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case: idlaal bihima
Recognize that the mustihadah has forgotten both the count (e.g., 3 or 7 days) and the placement (e.g., beginning or end of month) of her hayd. This is the third category of forgetfulness.
Distinguish from cases where she remembers one or the other.
2
Apply the primary ruling: taharrur
The mustihadah must first exert effort (taharrur) to determine her habit based on any available evidence. If she has no opinion, she moves to the next step.
Taharrur is a personal estimation, not arbitrary.
3
Determine ghusl and prayer schedule
On the correct (sahih) view, she performs ghusl for every fard prayer. She prays all obligatory, wajib, and mu'akkad sunnah prayers, but avoids supererogatory prayers and voluntary fasts.
There is a difference of opinion: some say ghusl per prayer time, not per prayer.
4
List restrictions and special rulings
She does not recite Quran outside prayer, touch the mushaf, or enter the mosque. If she hears a verse of sajdah, immediate prostration is valid without repetition; delayed prostration requires repetition after 10 days.
These are precautionary due to possible hayd.
5
Apply qada' and fasting rules
If she makes up missed prayers, she must repeat them after 10 days (and before 15, per the correct view). For Ramadan, she must fast every day because she might be pure.
The 10-day limit is based on the possibility that the qada' coincided with actual hayd.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الثالث وهو الاضلال بهما كما إذا استحيضت ونسيت عدد أيامها ومكانها فإنها تتحرى وإن لم يكن لها رأي اغتسلت لكل صلاة على الصحيح وقيل لوقت كل صلاة وتصلي المكتوبات والواجبات والسنن المؤكدة ولا تصلي تطوّعاً كالصوم تطوعاً وتقرأ القدر المفروض والواجب على الصحيح وقيل تقتصر على المفروض وتقرأ في الركعتين الأخيرتين على الصحيح لأنها سنة وقيل لا ولا تقرأ في الوتر اللهم إنا نستعينك» لأنها سورة عند عمر وغيره يقوم مقامه. ولا تقرأ شيئاً من القرآن خارج الصلاة ولا تمس المصحف ولا تدخل المسجد ولو سمعت آية السجدة فسجدت في الحال لا تجب الإعادة عليها لأنها إن كانت طاهرة فقد صح أداؤها وإلا لم تلزمها، وإن سجدت بعد ذلك أعادت بعد العشرة لاحتمال طهارتها وقت السماع وحيضها وقت السجود وأما قضاء الفوائت فإن كان عليها فوائت فقضتها فعليها إعادتها بعد عشرة أيام لاحتمال حيضها وقت القضاء. وقال أبو علي الدقاق: تقضيها بعد العشرة قبل أن تزيد على خمسة عشر وهو الصحيح لجواز أن يعود حيضها بعد خمسة عشر يوماً. وأما الصوم فإنها تصوم كل شهر رمضان لاحتمال طهارتها
And the third is idlaal bihima, as when she has istihadah and forgot the number of her days and their place, then she performs taharrur. If she has no opinion, she performs ghusl for every prayer on the correct view, and it is said at the time of every prayer. And she prays the obligatory, necessary, and emphasized sunnah prayers, and she does not pray supererogatory (tatawwu') like voluntary fasting. And she recites the obligatory and necessary amount on the correct view, and it is said she restricts to the obligatory. And she recites in the last two rak'ahs on the correct view because it is sunnah, and it is said she does not. And she does not recite 'Allahumma inna nasta'inuka' in witr because it is a surah according to 'Umar and others and it stands in its place. And she does not recite anything from the Quran outside prayer, nor touch the mushaf, nor enter the mosque. If she hears a verse of sajdah and prostrates immediately, repetition is not required upon her, because if she was pure, then her performance is valid, otherwise it was not required of her. If she prostrates after that, she repeats after ten days due to the possibility of her purity at the time of hearing and her hayd at the time of prostration. As for making up missed prayers, if she had missed prayers and then made them up, she must repeat them after ten days due to the possibility of hayd at the time of qada'. Abu Ali al-Daqqaq said: She makes them up after ten days before exceeding fifteen, and that is correct, because it is possible that her hayd returns after fifteen days. As for fasting, she fasts every Ramadan due to the possibility of her purity.
Source pages p. 364

Commentary
This passage covers the third category: idlaal bihima, where the mustihadah has forgotten both the number and the timing of her hayd days. The primary ruling is that she must perform taharrur (estimation based on her best effort). If she has no clear opinion, the correct view is that she performs ghusl for each prayer (i.e., before every fard prayer) to ensure purity. She prays all obligatory, wajib, and mu'akkad sunnah prayers but avoids supererogatory prayers and voluntary fasts. She recites the minimum obligatory amount in prayer. Various details follow: she does not recite Quran outside prayer, cannot touch a mushaf or enter a mosque. If she hears a verse of sajdah and prostrates immediately, no repetition is needed; but if later, she must repeat after 10 days. For missed prayers, if she makes them up, she must repeat them after 10 days (because she might have been in hayd during the qada'). Abu Ali al-Daqqaq's view that she should not delay beyond 15 days is considered correct. Regarding fasting, she must fast every Ramadan because she might be pure. These rulings reflect the Hanafi principle of precaution (ihtiyat) and respect for the sanctity of worship.

Key Terms
التحري (taharrur): The effort to determine her habit and schedule by estimation based on available evidence.
الفوائت (fawa'it): Missed obligatory prayers that have not been performed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A mustihadah with idlaal bihima must follow a strict regimen of ghusl per prayer, limited worship, and repetition of qada' after 10 days, all based on precaution to ensure validity.

Ruling for Mustahada Who Forgets Both Number and Timing of Hayd
Expands ruling for mustahada with complete forgetfulness of hayd pattern

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the obligations and prohibitions for a mustahada with complete forgetfulness of her menstrual pattern and apply the precautionary measures to determine valid worship.

Core Idea
A mustahada who forgets her entire pattern performs ghusl before each fard prayer and strictly avoids all voluntary acts and Quran recitation outside prayer.

This passage from Bahr al-Raiq expands the ruling for a mustahada who has completely lost track of her menstrual pattern—neither remembering the number of days nor their timing. Because she cannot rely on any known habit, she must adopt the most cautious approach to ensure her worship is valid. The ruling covers her purification, prayer, recitation, and other prohibitions, with internal differences resolved by the soundest view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Type of Forgetfulness
The scenario is a mustahada who has forgotten both the number of hayd days and their location (i.e., which days they were). This is the most severe case of idlal (forgetfulness).
If she remembers only one aspect, different rules apply; this lesson covers the combined forgetfulness.
2
Understand the Primary Duty: Taharrī and Ghusl
She must first exert her best judgment (taharrī) to determine her pattern. If she cannot form an opinion, she performs ghusl before every fard prayer on the soundest view; another view allows wudu at prayer time.
The mufta bihi is ghusl for each prayer due to caution.
3
List the Acts She May Perform
She prays all fard, wajib, and emphasized sunnah prayers. She does not perform voluntary (nafl) prayers or voluntary fasting. She recites the obligatory and necessary (wajib) amount of Quran in prayer.
The soundest view also allows recitation in the last two rak'ahs because it is sunna.
4
Determine Recitation Rules in Prayer
In the last two rak'ahs she recites according to the soundest view (it is sunna). In witr, she does not recite the supplication 'Allahumma inna nasta'inuka' because it is considered a sura by Umar and others that takes its place.
This is a specific prohibition for witr in her condition.
5
Outline Restrictions Outside Prayer
She must not recite any Quran outside prayer, touch the mushaf, or enter the mosque. If she hears an ayah of sajdah and prostrates immediately, no repetition is needed; otherwise, she repeats after ten days.
The ten-day period accounts for the possibility that she was menstruating at the time of prostration.
6
Understand Qada of Missed Prayers
If she had missed prayers and already performed them, she must repeat them after ten days (between ten and fifteen days according to Abu Ali al-Daqqaq), because she might have been menstruating when she originally performed them.
The ten-day waiting period is a precaution to ensure purity.

As for the third [type], which is forgetting both [number and location], such as when a woman experiences istihada and forgets the number of her days and their location. This passage is a detailed expansion (sharh) of the ruling for a mustahada who has completely forgotten both the number of her menstrual days and their timing within the month. Key Terms
استحاضة (istihāḍah): Chronic uterine bleeding that is not menstrual or postnatal; a woman with this condition is called mustahāḍah.
اضلال (iḍlāl): Forgetting the details of one's menstrual pattern, whether number of days, timing, or both.
تحري (taḥarrī): Exerting one's best judgment to determine the likely pattern of menses based on available signs.
مكتوبات (maktūbāt): The obligatory (fard) prayers, specifically the five daily prayers.
