Qada for a Woman with No Knowledge – The Base Scenario and the Dispute
Base scenario and intra-Hanafi dispute on qada days

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the required qada days for a woman with no knowledge of menstruation timing and explain why Abu Ja'far's view is preferred as al-ashah.

Core Idea
For an uncertain menstruation start, precaution demands up to 38 qada days.

When a woman is unsure about the exact days of her menstruation during Ramadan, she must fast enough days to cover all possible missed fasts. This lesson examines the base scenario where she has no knowledge and Ramadan is complete, and the intra-Hanafi disagreement between the majority of mashayikh and Imam Abu Ja'far al-Hinduwani.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the objective
The scenario is a woman who does not know when her menstruation started or ended during Ramadan. The objective is to determine the minimum number of qada days that ensures she has made up all missed obligatory fasts with certainty.
Certainty (yaqeen) in worship is a key principle; mere probability is insufficient.
2
Understand the majority position (25 days)
The majority of Hanafi scholars (عامة مشايخنا) said she fasts 25 days. This is based on the typical menstrual cycle: maximum hayd is 10 days, minimum tuhr is 15 days. Assuming Ramadan is 30 days, the worst-case missed fasts are 15 (10 from start, 5 from end) plus 10 for possible overlap, totalling 25.
This calculation assumes a balanced possibility.
3
Understand Abu Ja'far's position (32 or 38 days)
Abu Ja'far said if she makes up qada consecutively (موصولاً) she fasts 32 days; if separately (مفصولاً), 38 days. His method considers all possible positions of the menstrual cycle relative to Ramadan and Shawwal, leading to more precaution.
Consecutive means starting immediately after Eid; separate means with gaps.
4
Compare the positions: ihtiyat and tarjih
The text declares Abu Ja'far's view 'al-ashah' (more correct) because it leaves no room for doubt; it is the safest. The majority's 25 days might be valid in many cases but does not cover all possibilities.
Ihtiyat (precaution) is a fundamental Hanafi principle in acts of worship.
5
Apply the mufta bihi to a hypothetical case
Example: A woman completes Ramadan but cannot recall any details of her menstruation. Ramadan was 30 days. She must fast 32 days if she does so consecutively, or 38 if separately. Following Abu Ja'far's view ensures she fulfills her obligation with certainty.
The mufta bihi is the operative ruling for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطهارة - باب الحيض فسد فيها ويجزئها في خمسة عشر بعدها وعلى العكس فيوم الفطر أول يوم من طهرها لا تصوم فيه ثم يجزئها الصوم في أربعة عشر يوماً، ثم لا يجزئها في عشرة، ثم يجزئها في آخر يوم فجملته خمسة وعشرون يوماً. وكذلك إن قضته مفصولاً لتوهم أن ابتداء القضاء كان وافق أول يوم من حيضها فلا يجزئها الصوم في عشر ثم يجزئها في خمسة عشر. وإن علمت أن ابتداء حيضها كان بالنهار تقضي اثنين وثلاثين يوماً إن قضته موصولاً برمضان لأن أكثر ما فسد من صومها من أول الشهر ستة عشر يوماً، وإن قضته مفصولاً تقضي ثمانية وثلاثين يوماً لتوهم أن ابتداء القضاء وافق أول يوم من حيضها فلا يجزئها الصوم في أحد عشر ثم يجزئها في أربعة عشر ثم لا يجزئها في أحد عشر ثم يجزئها في يومين، فجملته ثمانية وثلاثون يوماً. وإن كانت لا تعلم شيئاً قال عامة مشايخنا : تصوم خمسة وعشرين يوماً. وقال الفقيه أبو جعفر : إن قضته موصولاً صامت اثنين وثلاثين وإن قضته مفصولاً صامت ثمانية وثلاثين يوماً وهو الأصح لما بينا. وهذا كله إذا كان شهر رمضان كاملاً فإن كان ناقصاً وعلمت أن ابتداء حيضها كان بالليل أو لم تعلم فإن وصلت قضت ثلاثة وثلاثين يوماً، وإن فصلت صامت سبعة وثلاثين يوماً. مر قوله : (لأن أكثر ما فسد من صومها من أول الشهر ستة عشر يوماً) الظاهر أن لفظة «أول» زائدة من قلم الناسخ وبيان ما قاله أنا لو فرضنا أن ابتداء الحيض كان في أول يوم وقت الزوال مثلاً فآخره يكون وقت الزوال من اليوم الحادي عشر، وطهرها يكون من وقتئذ إلى زوال اليوم السادس والعشرين، وهذا اليوم يحتمل طرق الحيض فيه فيفسد صومها في أحد عشر من أوله وخمسة من آخره. وهذا على أن يكون ابتداء الحيض في أول الشهر، فإن كان قبله فيحكم بفساد خمسة من أوله واحد عشر من آخره كما في المسألة السابقة. وعلى التقدير الأول تطهر في أثناء اليوم السادس من شوّال فإذا قضته موصولاً تقضي اثنين وثلاثين يوماً لأن يوم الفطر هو السادس من حيضها فلا تصومه، ثم لا يجزئها صوم بعده، ثم يجزىء في أربعة عشر بعدها، ثم لا يجزىء في أحد عشر، ثم يجزىء في يومين، فالجملة اثنان وثلاثون يوماً ولم يتعرض لما يلزمها على التقدير الثاني كما فعل في المسألة السابقة قلت : ومقتضى ما مر أن تقضي سبعة وعشرين يوماً لأنها بناء عليه طهرت في أثناء اليوم الأخير من رمضان فيوم الفطر ثاني يوم من طهرها فلا تصوم فيه ثم يجزئها في ثلاثة عشر بعده، ثم لا يجزئها في أحد عشر، ثم يجزئها في ثلاثة بعدها فالجملة سبعة وعشرون، وكان الأصل أن يجزئها ذلك ولكن الاحتياط الأول لاحتمال التقديرين معاً، وبالأول تخرج عن العهدة بيقين على نحو ما مر فتدبر . قوله : (فإن وصلت الخ قال في المحيط : إن وصلت قضت ثلاثة وثلاثين لأنا تيقنا بجواز الصوم في أربعة عشر وبفساده في خمسة عشر فيلزمها قضاء خمسة عشر، ثم لا يجزئها الصوم في من أول شوّال لأنه بقية حيضها فيجزئها في أربعة عشر ولا يجزئها في أحد عشر، ثم يجزئها في يوم فجملته ثلاثة وثلاثون. وإن فصلت قضت سبعة وثلاثين لجواز أن يوافق ابتداء صومها ابتداء حيضها فلا يجزئها الصوم في أحد عشر ، ثم يجزئها في أربعة عشر ثم لا يجزئها في أحد عشر ثم يجزئها في يوم فجملته سبعة وثلاثون .اهـ. قال بعض الفضلاء بعد نقله هذه العبارة قلت : الظاهر أنها إن وصلت تقضي اثنين وثلاثين يوماً كما صرح به في مقصد الطالب معزواً للصدر الشهيد، لأن أول يوم من شوّال هو يوم لا تصوم فيه كما تقدم فليتأمل اهـ . وهي قلت : ويغلب على ظني أن في عبارة المؤلف سقطاً أو تحريفاً، والصواب أن يقول: وعلمت أن ابتداء حيضها كان بالنهار فليتأمل. ثم راجعت التتارخانية فوجدته ذكر ما ذكره المؤلف هنا فيما إذا علمت أن ابتداء حيضها بالنهار وذكر قبله في مسألة ما إذا علمت أنه بالليل أن عليها أن تصوم بعد الفطر إذا وصلت عشرين يوماً، وإذا فصلت أربعة وعشرين وعزاه للصدر الشهيد فثبت أن في كلام المؤلف سقطاً. ورأيت فيها التعبير باثنين وثلاثين موافقاً لما نقلناه أولاً عن بعض الفضلاء وإنما كانت تقضي عشرين إذا وصلت لأنها إما أن تحيض خمسة في أوله وتسعة في آخره أو عشرة في أوّله وأربعة في آخره أو تحيض في أثنائه بأن حاضت ليلة السادس وطهرت ليلة السادس عشر؛ ففي الوجه الأول تقضي في شوّال أربعة عشر وفي الثاني تسعة عشر وفي الثالث عشرين، فقلنا بالأخير احتياطاً. وبيانه على ما صورناه أنها صامت من أوّله خمسة ومن آخره أربعة عشر صومها فيها صحيح ويوم الفطر آخر طهرها، فإذا قضت العشرة موصولة احتمل أن يكون أول القضاء أول الحيض فتصوم عشرة أخرى، وقد رأيت رسالة للعلامة محمد البركوي في الحيض ذكر فيها هذه المسألة ملخصة محررة فأحببت ذكر عبارته لجمعها لحاصل ما مر :وهي ثم إن لم تعلم أن دورها في كل شهر مرة وأن ابتداء حيضها بالليل أو بالنهار، أو علمت أنه بالنهار وكان شهر رمضان ثلاثين يجب عليها قضاء اثنين وثلاثين يوماً إن قضت موصولاً برمضان، وإن مفصولاً فثمانية وثلاثين. وإن كان شهر رمضان تسعة وعشرين تقضي في الوصل اثنين وثلاثين وفي الفصل سبعة وثلاثين. وإن علمت أن ابتداء حيضها بالليل وشهر رمضان ثلاثون تقضي في الوصل والفصل خمسة وعشرين. وإن تسعة وعشرين تقضي في الوصل عشرين وفي الفصل أربعة وعشرين وإن علمت أن حيضها في كل شهر .
Book of Purification - Chapter of Menstruation: It becomes invalid (i.e., fasting) in it (i.e., during menstruation) and it suffices her in fifteen after it. And conversely, the day of Fitr is the first day of her purity, she does not fast on it, then fasting suffices her in fourteen days, then it does not suffice her in ten, then it suffices her in the last day, so its total is twenty-five days. And likewise if she makes it up separately, due to the possibility that the start of the qada coincided with the first day of her menstruation, then fasting does not suffice her in ten, then it suffices her in fifteen. And if she knows that the start of her menstruation was during the day, she makes up thirty-two days if she makes it up consecutively with Ramadan, because the most of what became invalid of her fasting from the beginning of the month is sixteen days. And if she makes it up separately, she makes up thirty-eight days due to the possibility that the start of the qada coincided with the first day of her menstruation, so fasting does not suffice her in eleven, then it suffices her in fourteen, then it does not suffice her in eleven, then it suffices her in two days, so its total is thirty-eight days. And if she does not know anything, the majority of our scholars said: She fasts twenty-five days. And Faqih Abu Ja'far said: If she makes it up consecutively, she fasts thirty-two; if separately, she fasts thirty-eight days, and that is the more correct (al-ashah) for what we have stated. And all of this if the month of Ramadan is complete. If it is incomplete and she knows that her menstruation started at night or does not know, then if she makes it up consecutively, she makes up thirty-three days; if separately, she fasts thirty-seven days. A marginal note: He said: (Because the most of what became invalid of her fasting from the beginning of the month is sixteen days) It appears that the word 'beginning' is superfluous from the scribe's pen. Explanation of what he said: If we suppose that the start of menstruation was on the first day at the time of noon, for example, then its end would be at noon on the eleventh day, and her purity would be from then until noon on the twenty-sixth day, and this day (the 26th) potentially has the onset of menstruation, so her fasting is invalid in eleven from its beginning and five from its end. And this is if the start of menstruation is at the beginning of the month. If it was before that, then one rules the invalidity of five from its beginning and eleven from its end as in the previous case. According to the first estimation, she becomes pure during the sixth day of Shawwal, so if she makes it up consecutively, she makes up thirty-two days because the day of Fitr is the sixth of her menstruation, so she does not fast it, then fasting does not suffice her after it, then it suffices in fourteen after it, then it does not suffice in eleven, then it suffices in two days, so the total is thirty-two days. And he did not address what is incumbent upon her according to the second estimation as he did in the previous case. I said: According to what has passed, the requirement is that she makes up twenty-seven days because, on that basis, she became pure during the last day of Ramadan, so the day of Fitr is the second day of her purity, so she does not fast it, then fasting suffices her in thirteen after it, then it does not suffice in eleven, then it suffices in three after it, so the total is twenty-seven days. The original would have sufficed her with that, but the first precaution is due to the possibility of both estimations together, and with the first she emerges from the responsibility with certainty in the manner mentioned, so ponder. He said: (If she makes it up consecutively...) He said in al-Muhit: If she makes it up consecutively, she makes up thirty-three because we are certain of the validity of fasting in fourteen and its invalidity in fifteen, so she must make up fifteen, then fasting does not suffice her from the beginning of Shawwal because it is the remainder of her menstruation, so it suffices her in fourteen and does not suffice in eleven, then it suffices in one day, so its total is thirty-three. And if she makes it up separately, she makes up thirty-seven because it is possible that the start of her fasting coincided with the start of her menstruation, so fasting does not suffice her in eleven, then it suffices in fourteen, then does not suffice in eleven, then suffices in one day, so its total is thirty-seven. End quote. Some learned person said after quoting this statement: I say: It appears that if she makes it up consecutively, she makes up thirty-two days, as stated in Maqsad al-Talib attributed to al-Sadr al-Shahid, because the first day of Shawwal is a day she does not fast, as previously, so ponder. End. I said: It strongly appears to me that there is an omission or distortion in the author's expression; the correct thing is to say: And she knows that the start of her menstruation was during the day, so ponder. Then I checked al-Tatarkhaniyya and found that it mentioned what the author mentioned here regarding when she knows that the start of her menstruation was during the day, and mentioned before it in the case when she knows it was at night that she must fast after Fitr if she makes it up consecutively twenty days, and if separately twenty-four, and attributed it to al-Sadr al-Shahid. So it is confirmed that there is an omission in the author's words. And I saw in it the expression 'thirty-two' agreeing with what we initially transmitted from some learned person. She only makes up twenty if she makes it up consecutively because either she menstruates five at its beginning and nine at its end, or ten at its beginning and four at its end, or she menstruates in between, i.e., she menstruated on the night of the sixth and became pure on the night of the sixteenth. In the first case, she makes up in Shawwal fourteen; in the second, nineteen; in the third, twenty. So we chose the latter as a precaution. Its explanation according to our illustration is that she fasted five from its beginning and fourteen from its end; her fasting in these is valid, and the day of Fitr is the end of her purity. So if she makes up the ten consecutively, it is possible that the start of the qada is the start of her menstruation, so she fasts another ten. And I have seen a treatise by the scholar Muhammad al-Birkawi on menstruation in which he mentioned this issue summarized and well-organized, so I liked to mention his statement to gather the essence of what has passed: It is that if she does not know that her cycle is once every month and that the start of her menstruation is at night or during the day, or she knows it is during the day and the month of Ramadan is thirty, she must make up thirty-two days if she makes it up consecutively with Ramadan, and if separately then thirty-eight. And if the month of Ramadan is twenty-nine, she makes up in the consecutive case thirty-two and in the separate case thirty-seven. And if she knows that the start of her menstruation is at night and the month of Ramadan is thirty, she makes up in both consecutive and separate twenty-five. And if it is twenty-nine, she makes up in the consecutive case twenty and in the separate case twenty-four. And if she knows that her menstruation is every month...
Source pages p. 366

Commentary
This passage deals with the rules for a woman who missed fasts in Ramadan due to menstruation and needs to make them up. The core issue is that since she is uncertain about exactly when her menstruation began and ended, she must fast a sufficient number of days to ensure that she has made up all the obligatory fasts. The passage presents multiple scenarios based on what she knows about the timing of her menstruation (whether it started at night or during the day, or she has no knowledge) and whether Ramadan was complete (30 days) or incomplete (29 days). The general principle is ihtiyat (precaution): she must fast enough days so that in all possible scenarios she will have observed the correct number of qada fasts. For example, if she knows her menstruation started at night and Ramadan was 30 days, she must fast 25 days whether she makes them up consecutively or separately. If she knows it started during the day, she fasts 32 if consecutive, 38 if separate. If she knows nothing, the majority rule is 25 days, but Imam Abu Ja'far al-Hinduwani says 32 or 38, and this is considered the more cautious (ashah) view. The commentary also includes a critical discussion about a possible omission in the text, referencing al-Tatarkhaniyya and a treatise by al-Birkawi. The key takeaway is that the qada period must cover all contingencies to be certain the obligation is fulfilled.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada): Making up missed obligatory fasts after Ramadan
حيض (hayd): Menstruation, a state that invalidates fasting and prayer
طهر (tuhr): The state of purity between menstruations
احتياط (ihtiyat): Legal precaution taken when the exact ruling is uncertain

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which view is declared 'al-ashah' (the more correct) for a woman with no knowledge of her menstruation timing?
A) The majority view: 25 days
B) Abu Ja'far's view: 32 or 38 days
C) Neither; both are equally valid
D) Only Abu Yusuf's view

Key Takeaway
For a woman with no knowledge of her menstruation timing, the mufta bihi is to fast 32 days (if consecutive) or 38 days (if separate) as a precautionary measure to ensure all obligatory fasts are made up.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Istihadah and the Obligation to Pray Despite Uncertainty
Defining istihadah and the rule for prayer when bleeding exceeds habit but stays within maximum.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of istihadah and apply the rule that a woman does not stop praying due to doubt about the nature of bleeding.

Core Idea
Blood beyond ten days is certainly istihadah; within ten days, doubt does not stop prayer.

When a woman experiences prolonged bleeding, distinguishing between menstruation (hayd) and non-menstrual bleeding (istihadah) is crucial for her worship. This lesson examines how the Hanafi school defines istihadah when blood exceeds the normal maximum and resolves the question: should she stop praying upon seeing an increase? The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq provides the framework of certainty and doubt that determines her actions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three zones of bleeding
Recognize that the passage divides bleeding into three categories: (1) within the habit – certain hayd; (2) beyond ten days – certain istihadah; (3) between habit and ten days – uncertain, requiring a ruling based on istishab.
2
Apply the rule of certainty (yaqin)
Understand that what is within her normal habit (ʿadah) is hayd with certainty, and what exceeds ten days is istihadah with certainty. The uncertain middle zone is governed by the principle that certainty is not overridden by doubt.
Hanafi usul: al-yaqinu la yazulu bi al-shakk.
3
Evaluate the two opinions on stopping prayer
Some say she stops upon seeing the increase (istishab of hayd); others say she does not stop because the increase might be istihadah. The validated view (al-Nihayah) is that she does not stop, due to istishab of the original ruling (al-asl al-sihhah).
The dispute is intra-Hanafi; the preferred view is mufta bihi.
4
Derive the consequence: qada of missed prayers
If she mistakenly stopped praying due to doubt, she must make up those prayers because the original obligation remains valid. The passage concludes that she does not abandon qada due to doubt.
This applies when blood exceeds ten days – then only qada is possible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في زمن الاستمرار ولو زاد الدم على أكثر الحيض والنفاس فما زاد على عادتها استحاضة لأن ما رأته في أيامها حيض بيقين وما زاد على العشرة استحاضة بيقين وما بين ذلك متردد بين أن يلحق بما قبله فيكون حيضاً فلا تصلي وبين أن يلحق بما بعده فيكون استحاضة فتصلي فلا تترك الصلاة بالشك فيلزمها قضاء ما تركت من الصلاة والمراد بالأكثر عشرة أيام وعشر ليال في الحيض حتى إذا كان عشرة أيام وتسع ليال ثم زاد الدم فإنه حيض حتى يزيد على ليلة الحادي عشر كذا في السراج الوهاج وهل تترك بمجرد رؤيتها الزيادة؟ قيل لا إذ لم تتيقن بكونه حيضاً لاحتمال الزيادة على العشرة، وقيل نعم استصحاباً للحال ولأن الأصل الصحة وكونه استحاضة بكونه عن داء. وصححه في النهاية وغيرها. وكذا في النفاس، فما زاد على الأربعين ولها عادة معروفة فإنها ترد إليها أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان ختم عادتها بالدم أو بالطهر. وهذا عند أبي يوسف وعند محمد إن كان ختم عادتها بالدم مرة وأن ابتداءه بالنهار أو لم تعلم أنه بالنهار تقضي اثنين وعشرين مطلقاً أي وصلت أو فصلت، وإن علمت أن ابتداءه بالليل تقضي عشرين مطلقاً .اهـ. قوله : ( وعن محمد بن الحسن شهران الخ) قال في معراج الدراية قال الحاكم الشهيد : وهو رواية ابن سماعة عن محمد لأن العادة مأخوذة من المعاودة والحيض والطهر مما يتكرر في الشهرين عادة إذ الغالب أن النساء تحيض في كل شهر مرة، فإذا طهرت شهرين فقد طهرت في أيام حيضها، والعادة تنتقل بمرتين فصار ذلك الطهر عادة لها فوجب التقدير به، والفتوى على قول الحاكم لأنه أيسر على المفتي .اهـ. قال في الشرنبلالية : فعلى هذا تنقضي عدتها بسبعة أشهر لاحتياجها إلى ثلاثة أطهار بستة أشهر وثلاث حيضات بشهر اهـ . لكن في السراج قال الصيرفي وأكثر المشايخ على تقديره بشهرين إلا أنه قال إنما تنقضي عدتها بسبعة أشهر وعشرة أيام إلا ساعة لأنه ربما يكون طلقها في أول الحيض فلا يحتسب بتلك الحيضة فتحتاج إلى ثلاثة أطهار وهي ستة أشهر وعشرة أيام إلا ساعة وهي الساعة التي مضت من الحيض الذي وقع فيه الطلاق اهـ. وقد نبهناك على أن ذلك أيضاً يجري في المعتادة التي استمر بها الدم فلا تغفل . قوله : (فلا تترك الصلاة بالشك الخ) يعني لا تترك قضاءها بالشك لأن الكلام مفروض فيما إذا رأت الزائد على العشرة، وحينئذ لا يمكن سوى القضاء، وليس المراد أنها لا تترك أداء الصلاء قبل ذلك بمجرد
In the period of continuity, and if blood exceeds the maximum of menstruation and postpartum bleeding, then what exceeds her habit is istihadah. Because what she sees in her days is menstruation with certainty, and what exceeds ten is istihadah with certainty, and what is between is uncertain between being attached to what preceded and thus being menstruation so she does not pray, and being attached to what follows and thus being istihadah so she prays. So she does not abandon prayer due to doubt, rather she must make up what she missed of prayer. And the meaning of 'maximum' is ten days and ten nights in menstruation, such that if it is ten days and nine nights then blood increases, it remains menstruation until it exceeds the night of the eleventh. Thus in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. And does she abandon prayer just by seeing the increase? It is said: No, because she is not certain it is menstruation, due to the possibility of exceeding ten. And it is said: Yes, by istishab (presumption of continuity), and because the original is validity, and its being istihadah is because it is from a disease. And it was validated in al-Nihayah and others. Similarly in postpartum: what exceeds forty, and she has a known habit, then she returns to it. It is general, so it includes whether the end of her habit was with blood or with purity. This is according to Abu Yusuf. And according to Muhammad, if the end of her habit was with blood once and its beginning was during the day, or she does not know it was during the day, she makes up twenty-two absolutely, whether connected or separated. If she knows its beginning was at night, she makes up twenty absolutely. End. His statement: (And from Muhammad ibn al-Hasan: two months, etc.) He said in Mi'raj al-Dirayah, al-Hakim al-Shahid said: It is a narration of Ibn Sama'ah from Muhammad, because habit ('adah) is derived from recurrence, and menstruation and purity usually recur in two months, since most women menstruate once a month. So if she becomes pure for two months, she has been pure during her menstrual days, and habit transfers by two occurrences, so that purity becomes her habit, so estimation by it is necessary. And the fatwa is on the saying of al-Hakim because it is easier for the mufti. End. He said in al-Shurnublaliyyah: Based on this, her 'iddah ends after seven months, because she needs three pure periods (six months) and three menstruations (one month). End. But in al-Siraj, al-Sayrafi and most mashayikh are upon estimation of two months, except that he said her 'iddah ends only after seven months and ten days minus one hour, because perhaps he divorced her at the beginning of menstruation, so that menstruation is not counted, so she needs three pure periods, which are six months and ten days minus one hour, which is the hour that passed from the menstruation in which divorce occurred. End. And we have reminded you that this also applies to the woman with a habit who has continuous bleeding, so do not be heedless. His statement: (So she does not abandon prayer due to doubt, etc.) means she does not abandon making it up due to doubt, because the discussion is premised on when she sees the excess over ten, and then nothing is possible except making up. It does not mean that she does not abandon performing the prayer before that just by...
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq covers two interrelated rulings: First, the definition of istihadah (non-menstrual bleeding) when blood exceeds the maximum duration of hayd (10 days) or nifas (40 days). The key principle is that anything within her usual habit is hayd/nifas, and anything beyond the maximum is istihadah with certainty, while the in-between period is uncertain—she must pray and later make up missed prayers due to the doubt. The text also discusses whether she should stop praying upon seeing the increase; the correct view (validated in al-Nihayah) is that she does not stop, due to istishab. Second, the passage addresses the qada of fasts for a woman with a known habit that ends with blood (according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). If her habit ends with blood, she must make up 22 or 20 fasts depending on whether she knows the start of hayd. Then it introduces a separate opinion from Muhammad (via Ibn Sama'ah) that the 'iddah of a mustahadah should be estimated by two months of purity, as the habit transfers after two months. The fatwa is on al-Hakim al-Shahid's view for ease. The detailed calculation for 'iddah (7 months, 10 days minus 1 hour) accounts for the possibility of divorce at the start of menstruation. The passage ends with a reminder not to abandon prayer or qada due to doubt.

Key Terms
استحاضة (istihadah): Non-menstrual bleeding due to disease; it does not prevent prayer, fasting, or sexual relations.
عادة ('adah): The established pattern of a woman's menstrual or pure days; used to determine which days are hayd when bleeding is irregular.
أكثر الحيض (akthar al-hayd): The maximum duration of menstruation: ten days and ten nights.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) When it exceeds her normal habit
B) When it exceeds ten days for menstruation
C) When it is accompanied by pain
D) When it appears at an unusual time

Key Takeaway
A woman with uncertain bleeding between her habit and ten days must pray and later make up any missed prayers due to the doubt, because certainty is not overridden by doubt.

Counting Qada Fasts and 'Iddah for Women with Irregular Bleeding
Qada of fasts based on custom ending and 'iddah estimation using two months of purity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the number of fasts a mustahadah must make up based on her habit's end, and explain the 'iddah estimation using two months of purity according to later Hanafi authorities.

Core Idea
Qada counts depend on how her habit ends; 'iddah for mustahadah is estimated by two months of purity, easing the mufti's task.

When a woman with a known habit experiences continuous bleeding, determining how many fasts she owes becomes complex. The Hanafi school offers specific numbers based on whether her habit ends with blood or purity. Additionally, her 'iddah (waiting period) after divorce cannot rely on actual menstruations, so scholars use an estimation of two months of purity, derived from the recurrence of habits. This lesson unpacks the arithmetic and the reasoning behind the numbers.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish Abu Yusuf's and Muhammad's approaches
Abu Yusuf holds that she returns to her habit regardless of whether it ended with blood or purity. Muhammad distinguishes: if the habit ended with blood and she knows the start was during the day, she makes up 22 fasts; if she knows it started at night, she makes up 20. If she doesn't know, 22.
The numbers come from counting the days of purity in her habit that she missed.
2
Understand the 'iddah estimation by al-Hakim al-Shahid
For a mustahadah whose habit is lost, later scholars like al-Hakim al-Shahid estimate her 'iddah as two months of purity (60 days) because most women menstruate once a month, and habit transfers after two occurrences.
This is from Muhammad via Ibn Sama'ah; the fatwa is on this view because it's easier.
3
Calculate the actual 'iddah period
If she needs three pure periods (quru') and each is two months, total is six months for purity, plus three months for the hayd days she would have had, totaling seven months. However, a more precise calculation adds ten days minus one hour to account for the possibility of divorce at the start of menses.
This shows the meticulousness of Hanafi fiqh in estimating obligations.

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq covers two interrelated rulings: First, the definition of istihadah (non-menstrual bleeding) when blood exceeds the maximum duration of hayd (10 days) or nifas (40 days). The key principle is that anything within her usual habit is hayd/nifas, and anything beyond the maximum is istihadah with certainty, while the in-between period is uncertain—she must pray and later make up missed prayers due to the doubt. The passage ends with a reminder not to abandon prayer or qada due to doubt.

Key Terms
استحاضة (istihadah): Non-menstrual bleeding due to disease; it does not prevent prayer, fasting, or sexual relations.
عادة ('adah): The established pattern of a woman's menstrual or pure days; used to determine which days are hayd when bleeding is irregular.
عدة ('iddah): The waiting period after divorce or death before a woman may remarry, typically three menstrual cycles or three months for non-cycling women.

Ruling on Blood Exceeding Maximum Hayd or Nifas
Exposition of the ruling when blood exceeds maximum hayd or nifas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on istihada when blood exceeds the maximum of hayd or nifas, distinguishing between definite, ambiguous, and definitely istihada periods, and identify the mufta bihi regarding prayer during ambiguity.

Core Idea
Blood beyond the maximum of hayd (10 days) or nifas (40 days) is definitely istihada; the period between habit and maximum is ambiguous, requiring prayer with later qada.

The Hanafi school provides a clear framework for a woman who sees bleeding beyond her usual habit. The key is to determine which days are definitely hayd, which are definitely istihada, and which fall in an ambiguous middle zone. In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, Ibn Nujaym explains these categories and the ruling on prayer during the ambiguous period, including an important intra-Hanafi dispute on whether she should stop praying immediately upon seeing the increase.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three bleeding zones
There are three zones: (1) days within her habit (definitely hayd), (2) days between habit and the maximum (ambiguous), (3) days beyond the maximum (definitely istihada).
The maximum for hayd is ten days and ten nights; for nifas, forty days.
2
Apply the ruling for each zone
During zone 1: she does not pray. Zone 2: she must pray (due to doubt) and later make up those prayers if they turn out to be hayd. Zone 3: she prays normally and does not need to make up.
This is the general rule based on the principle that certainty is not removed by doubt.
3
Understand the proof for the maximum
The maximum of ten days for hayd and forty for nifas is established by consensus (ijma) of the Companions and transmitted rulings.
This is considered qat'i in transmission but zanni in interpretation regarding individual cases.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on abandoning prayer
Some early Hanafis said she does not abandon prayer upon seeing increased bleeding because she is not certain it is hayd. Others said she abandons prayer as a continuation (istishab) of her previous state of hayd. The authenticated view in al-Nihayah is the latter.
The mufta bihi is that she abandons prayer during ambiguous days and makes them up later.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that she leaves prayer during the ambiguous period (between habit and maximum) and later performs qada for those prayers if they turn out to be istihada.
This balances the need for caution (ihtiyat) and the principle that doubt does not override certainty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو زاد الدم على أكثر الحيض والنفاس فما زاد على عادتها استحاضة لأن ما رأته في أيامها حيض بيقين وما زاد على العشرة استحاضة بيقين وما بين ذلك متردد بين أن يلحق بما قبله فيكون حيضاً فلا تصلي وبين أن يلحق بما بعده فيكون استحاضة فتصلي فلا تترك الصلاة بالشك فيلزمها قضاء ما تركت من الصلاة والمراد بالأكثر عشرة أيام وعشر ليال في الحيض حتى إذا كان عشرة أيام وتسع ليال ثم زاد الدم فإنه حيض حتى يزيد على ليلة الحادي عشر كذا في السراج الوهاج وهل تترك بمجرد رؤيتها الزيادة؟ قيل لا إذ لم تتيقن بكونه حيضاً لاحتمال الزيادة على العشرة، وقيل نعم استصحاباً للحال ولأن الأصل الصحة وكونه استحاضة بكونه عن داء. وصححه في النهاية وغيرها. وكذا في النفاس، فما زاد على الأربعين ولها عادة معروفة فإنها ترد إليها أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان ختم عادتها بالدم أو بالطهر.
And if the blood exceeds the maximum of menstruation and postpartum bleeding, then what exceeds her habit is istihada, because what she sees in her days is definitely menstruation, and what exceeds ten is definitely istihada, and what is between that is uncertain: between being attached to what precedes it so it is menstruation and she does not pray, and between being attached to what follows it so it is istihada and she prays. So she does not abandon prayer due to doubt, and it is incumbent upon her to make up the prayers she abandoned. What is meant by the maximum is ten days and ten nights in menstruation, such that if it is ten days and nine nights and then the blood increases, it is menstruation until it exceeds the eleventh night. Thus in Al-Siraj Al-Wahhaj. And should she abandon prayer simply by seeing the increase? It is said no, since she is not certain it is menstruation due to the possibility of exceeding ten, and it is said yes, as a continuation of the current state and because the original ruling is soundness and its being istihada due to being from an illness. And it is authenticated in Al-Nihayah and others. And similarly in postpartum bleeding: what exceeds forty, and she has a known habit, then she is referred to it. He (the author) made it absolute, so it includes whether the end of her habit is with blood or with purity.
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on determining istihada when blood exceeds the maximum duration of menstruation (10 days) or postpartum bleeding (40 days) in a woman who has a known habit. The author of Al-Bahr Al-Ra'iq, Ibn Nujaym, explains that if a woman with a habit sees bleeding beyond the maximum, the blood beyond her habit is considered istihada (irregular bleeding) because the days within her habit are definitely hayd, and the days beyond the maximum are definitely istihada. The intermediate period (between habit and maximum) is ambiguous, and she must pray during it and later make up any prayers she missed due to doubt. The text then clarifies that the 'maximum' in menstruation is ten days and ten nights; if bleeding continues into the eleventh night, it becomes istihada. There is a difference of opinion on whether she stops praying immediately upon seeing the increase: some say no due to uncertainty, others say yes based on istishab (continuity of the previous state). The author notes that the latter view is authenticated in Al-Nihayah. The same rule applies to postpartum bleeding, where the maximum is forty days. If she has a known habit (e.g., thirty days), she returns to it, regardless of whether her habit ends with blood or purity—this is the position of Abu Yusuf as will be explained later.

Key Terms
استحاضة (istihāḍah): Irregular vaginal bleeding outside of the days of menstruation or postpartum bleeding, not of womb origin.
استصحاب (istiṣḥāb): Presumption of continuity of a previous state (here, that bleeding is hayd until proven otherwise).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Blood beyond the maximum (10 days for hayd, 40 for nifas) is definitely istihada; the period between habit and maximum is ambiguous, and the mufta bihi is that she abandons prayer during this period and makes it up later.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on End of Habit and Estimation of Tuhr
Intra-Hanafi dispute on end of habit and estimation of tuhr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding qada after nifas and explain the Hanafi preference for Muhammad's estimation of tuhr.

Core Idea
Number of prayers to make up depends on how the habit ends; fatwa prefers Muhammad's easier estimation of tuhr as two months.

This lesson examines a critical intra-Hanafi dispute about postpartum women: if her habit ends with blood or purity, how many prayers must she make up? Abu Yusuf and Muhammad ibn al-Hasan give different answers. The passage also discusses the estimation of a woman's purity period (tuhr) when bleeding continues beyond her habit, a point settled by Al-Hakim al-Shahid who preferred Muhammad's transmission for ease.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Abu Yusuf holds that if the habit ends with purity (tuhr), no qada is required for those days. Muhammad holds that if the habit ends with blood, specific numbers apply: 22 prayers if bleeding started during the day or unknown, 20 if it started at night.
This is an intra-Hanafi difference; both imams are authoritative.
2
Understand the condition 'khatm al-ada'
'Khatm al-ada' refers to how the woman's habit ends—whether with blood or with purity. The dispute centers on the final day of the habit.
The habit is the usual number of days she bleeds.
3
Trace the transmitted numbers
Muhammad's numbers: 22 prayers (for day or unknown start) and 20 prayers (for night start). These include all missed prayers over the extra bleeding days.
The numbers are derived from averaging and are considered specific to nifas.
4
Examine the estimation of tuhr
For a woman who bleeds continuously beyond her habit, Muhammad (via Ibn Sam'ah) estimated a purity period (tuhr) as two months, based on the recurrence of menses. This estimation is used to calculate 'iddah and other rulings.
Al-Hakim al-Shahid preferred this for fatwa because it is easier for the mufti.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The text notes that the fatwa is on Muhammad's estimation of tuhr (two months) due to ease. However, the dispute on qada numbers does not specify which view is mufta bihi; both remain transmitted.
The later mashayikh (al-Sayrafi) also followed the two-month estimation but refined the 'iddah calculation.

This passage addresses two related points. First, a difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding a postpartum woman with a habit of e.g. 30 days: if her habit ends with blood (i.e., she sees blood on the last day of her habit) or if she ends with purity, there is a dispute on how many prayers she must make up. Abu Yusuf has one view, Muhammad another, with specific numbers (22 or 20 prayers depending on when bleeding started). Second, the passage revisits the estimation of tuhr for a mustahada, emphasizing that the fatwa is on the two-month estimation by Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, transmitted via Ibn Sam'ah. The author notes that this applies even to a woman with a known habit who experiences continuous bleeding. The final sentence (cut off in OCR) clarifies that the earlier ruling about not leaving prayer due to doubt refers to qada (making up missed prayers), not to the performance of prayer during the ambiguous days. This is a critical refinement: a woman should not postpone making up prayers once she knows they were missed due to istihada.

Key Terms
ختم العادة (khatm al-ʿādah): The manner in which her menstrual or postpartum habit ends, either with blood or with purity.
قضاء (qaḍāʾ): Making up missed religious obligations (like prayers or fasts) that were missed due to valid reasons such as menstruation.
تقدير الطهر (taqdīr al-ṭuhr): Estimation of the purity period for a woman whose bleeding continues beyond her habit; set as two months in the mufta bihi view.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, if a postpartum woman's habit ends with blood and the start was during the day (or unknown), how many prayers must she make up?
A) Twenty prayers.
B) Twenty-two prayers.
C) Ten prayers.
D) No prayers need to be made up.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has two positions on qada after nifas; the fatwa prefers Muhammad's estimation of tuhr for practical ease, but the dispute on qada numbers remains unresolved.

When Pre-Customary Blood Becomes Hayd: The Sahibayn vs. Abu Hanifa
Intra-Hanafi dispute on irregular menstruation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on blood seen before customary days and apply them to determine whether the blood is hayd or istihadah.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa suspends judgment until the next month; the Sahibayn rule it hayd immediately – but each on different grounds.

When a menstruating woman with a regular habit sees blood outside her usual days, we must decide if it is menstruation (hayd) or irregular bleeding (istihadah). Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, reach different conclusions. This passage explains their arguments and provides detailed scenarios to help you navigate these rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions
First, note Abu Hanifa's position: the ruling is suspended until the second month. Then, Abu Yusuf's view: a single occurrence breaks the habit. Finally, Muhammad's view: substitution (ibdal) applies if the total blood reaches the minimum hayd period.
All three are within the Hanafi school.
2
Understand the rationale behind each position
Abu Hanifa insists on caution: a single irregularity is not enough to confirm hayd; repetition is needed. Abu Yusuf holds that one instance is sufficient to change the habit. Muhammad focuses on the total days of bleeding: if the blood before and during the days together make at least three days, it is all hayd.
These principles are called 'naqd al-‘ādah' and 'ibdāl'.
3
Apply to the four scenarios
The passage lists four cases: (a) blood before is sufficient, blood during is insufficient; (b) both are insufficient alone but together suffice; (c) blood before is sufficient, none during; (d) blood before is insufficient, blood during sufficient. Work through each and see how the ruling differs among the three imams.
Scenario (d) is unanimous: all is hayd.
4
Note the two narrations from Abu Hanifa
In the fifth scenario, where both sets are sufficient, there are two reports from Abu Hanifa. This shows that even the founder of the school did not have a single settled view on every case.
The text leaves this ambiguity unresolved.
5
Identify the practical consequence
According to Abu Hanifa, the woman must wait a full month before knowing her ruling; meanwhile she should refrain from prayer and fasting. According to the Sahibayn, she immediately treats the blood as hayd.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf (fruit of the difference).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطهارة - باب الحيض عند أبي حنيفة إن رأت في الشهر الثاني مثله فهذا والأول حيض وإلا فهو استحاضة. وقالا : حيض لأن أبا يوسف يرى نقض العادة بمرة ومحمد يرى الإبدال إن أمكن كما صرح به في الكافي فيما إذا رأت يومين فيها يوماً قبلها. وفي الفتاوى الظهيرية : ولو رأت صاحبة العادة قبل أيامها ما يكون حيضاً، وفي أيامها ما لا يكون حيضاً، أو رأت قبل أيامها ما لا يكون حيضاً وفي أيامها ما لا يكون حيضاً لكن إذا جمعا كانا حيضاً أو رأت قبل أيامها ما يكون حيضاً ولم تر في أيامها شيئاً لا يكون شيء ذلك حيضاً عند أبي حنيفة والأمر موقوف إلى الشهر الثاني فإن رأت في الشهر الثاني مثل ما رأت في الشهر الأول يكون الكل حيضاً، وعندهما يكون حيضاً غير أن عند أبي يوسف بطريق العادة، وعند محمد بطريق البدل. ولو رأت قبل أيامها ما لا يكون حيضاً وفي أيامها ما يكون حيضاً فالكل حيض بالاتفاق، ويجعل ما قبل أيامها تبعاً لأيامها. ولو رأت قبل أيامها ما يكون حيضاً وفي أيامها ما يكون حيضاً، فعن أبي حنيفة روايتان
The Book of Purity - Chapter on Menstruation: According to Abu Hanifa, if she sees the like [of it] in the second month, then this and the first are menstruation; otherwise it is irregular bleeding. And the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] said: It is menstruation, because Abu Yusuf holds that the habit is broken by one occurrence, and Muhammad holds substitution if possible, as clarified in al-Kafi regarding the case where she sees two days during [her habit] and one day before it. And in al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah: If a woman with a habit sees before her days what would be menstruation, and during her days what would not be menstruation, or she sees before her days what would not be menstruation and during her days what would not be menstruation, but if combined they become menstruation, or she sees before her days what would be menstruation and does not see anything during her days, then none of that is menstruation according to Abu Hanifa, and the matter is suspended until the second month: if she sees in the second month like what she saw in the first month, then all of it is menstruation; according to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad], it is menstruation, except that according to Abu Yusuf it is by way of habit, and according to Muhammad it is by way of substitution. And if she sees before her days what would not be menstruation and during her days what would be menstruation, then all is menstruation by consensus, and what is before her days is made to follow her days. And if she sees before her days what would be menstruation and during her days what would be menstruation, then there are two narrations from Abu Hanifa.
Source pages p. 370

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning a woman with a known menstrual habit who sees blood before her customary days. Imam Abu Hanifa suspends the ruling until the next month: if the same pattern repeats, both months' blood is hayd; otherwise, it is istihadah. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) rule it as hayd immediately, but each on different grounds. Abu Yusuf holds that a single occurrence breaks the habit, so the blood before the days establishes a new habit. Muhammad holds the principle of substitution (ibdal): if the blood before the days combines with blood during the days to make a minimum hayd period (3 days), it substitutes for the usual days and is considered hayd. The passage then details four scenarios: (1) blood before is sufficient, blood during is not; (2) both are insufficient alone but together make hayd; (3) blood before is sufficient, none during; (4) blood before is insufficient, blood during is sufficient. For (1)-(3), Abu Hanifa's position is suspension; the Sahibayn rule it hayd. For (4), by consensus the whole is hayd, with the prior blood following the days. For the fifth scenario where both sets are sufficient, there are two narrations from Abu Hanifa, leaving the ruling unsettled in that case.

Key Terms
استحاضة (istihadah): Irregular bleeding that is not menstruation; the woman remains in a state of purity regarding prayer and fasting but must perform wudu for each prayer.
عادة (‘ādah): The established menstrual habit (duration and timing) based on previous regular cycles.
إبدال (ibdāl): Substitution – the principle that if a woman sees blood at a different time, it substitutes for her normal days if it completes the minimum hayd period.
نقض العادة (naqd al-‘ādah): Breaking the habit – a single occurrence of blood at a different time is sufficient to change the established habit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Muhammad al-Shaybani, which condition is necessary for blood seen before customary days to be considered hayd?
A) It must be at least one day.
B) It must combine with blood during the days to reach the minimum hayd period.
C) It must be seen for two consecutive months.
D) It must exceed the customary days.

Key Takeaway
The three Hanafi imams disagree on whether a single irregular occurrence changes the menstrual habit, leading to different rulings on the spot versus after a month.

Transfer of the Menstrual Habit (Intiqal al-Ādah): Conditions and Sub-Cases
Explains conditions for transfer of menstrual habit and ten sub-cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for transfer of a menstrual habit according to the majority of Hanafi imams and apply it to a scenario with differing blood patterns.

Core Idea
A menstrual habit only transfers after two consecutive instances of a new pattern.

Determining whether a woman's menstrual habit has changed is crucial for distinguishing between menstruation (hayd) and non-menstrual bleeding (istihadah). The Hanafi school presents a nuanced debate on this issue, with the majority requiring two consecutive occurrences of the new pattern before a transfer is established. This lesson unpacks that debate, its practical consequences, and the detailed sub-cases that arise when blood appears before or after the habitual days.

Guided Path
1
Identify the concept of ada and intiqal
Understand that a woman's menstrual habit (adah) is her usual duration and pattern of bleeding. Transfer (intiqal) means her habit shifts to a new pattern due to observed changes.
Ada can be original or placed; here we focus on its modification.
2
Understand the intra-Hanafi dispute
Note that Abu Hanifah and Muhammad require two consecutive sightings of the differing pattern, while Abu Yusuf holds that one sighting suffices for transfer.
The text emphasizes that the majority view (two occurrences) is the mufta bihi.
3
Apply the condition to a hypothetical
Take a woman with a habit of 5 days. If she bleeds for 6 days one month, then 7 the next, then 6 again, her habit becomes 6 by consensus (since she saw 6 twice). But if she saw 6 only once, her habit remains 5 according to Abu Hanifah.
This illustrates the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence).
4
Recognize the ten sub-cases
The passage outlines five cases for blood before the habitual days and five for after. The ruling varies depending on whether the blood appears within the habit, after it, and whether total bleeding exceeds ten days.
These sub-cases are essential for accurate fatwa in complex scenarios.

انتقال العادة من حيضاً رواية واحدة عن أبي حنيفة وقد بين الإبدال على قول محمد وأطال فيه فمن رامه فليراجعها. وما في الظهيرية هو الانتقال من حيث المكان، وما تقدم هو حيث العدد وعلى هذا الخلاف لو انقطع دون عادتها على ثلاث أو أربعة. كذا في السراج الوهاج. وفي الظهيرية والعادة كما تنتقل برؤية الدم المخالف للدم المرئي في أيامها مرتين فكذلك تنتقل بطهر أيامها مرتين قيد بكونها معتادة لأنه لو لم يكن لها عادة معروفة بأن كانت تری شهراً ستاً وترى شهراً سبعاً فاستمر بها الدم فإنها تأخذ في حق الصوم والصلاة والرجعة بالأقل، وفي حق انقضاء العدة والغشيان بالأكثر فعليها إذا رأت ستة أيام في الاستمرار أن تغتسل في اليوم السابع لتمام السادس وتصلي فيه وتصوم إن كان دخل عليها شهر رمضان لأنه يحتمل أن يكون السابع حيضاً ويحتمل أن لا يكون حيضاً فوجب احتياطاً، فإذا جاء الثامن فعليها الغسل ثانياً وتقضي اليوم الذي صامته في السابع لاحتمال كونها حائضاً فيه ولا تقضي الصلاة وإن كانت عادتها خمسة فحاضت ستة ثم حاضت أخرى سبعة ثم حاضت أخرى ستة فعادتها ستة بالإجماع حتى يبني الاستمرار عليها لأن عند أبي يوسف يبني الاستمرار على المرة الأخيرة وأما عندهما فقد رأت الستة مرتين. كذا في البدائع

Book of Purification - Chapter of Menstruation. The transfer of the habit from menstruation: a single narration from Abu Hanifah, and he explained the substitutions according to Muhammad and elaborated on it, so let whoever seeks it consult it. What is in al-Zahiriyyah is the transfer in terms of place, and what preceded is in terms of number, and on this difference, if it stops short of her habit at three or four days. Likewise in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. In al-Zahiriyyah: the habit transfers by seeing blood that differs from the blood seen in her days twice, so also it transfers by the purity of her days twice, conditioned on her being customary, because if she did not have a known habit, such that she would see six days one month and seven days another, and bleeding continued, then she takes, regarding fast, prayer, and reconciliation, the lesser, and regarding the completion of the waiting period and intercourse, the greater. So if she sees six days in the continuation, she must perform ghusl on the seventh day upon completing the sixth, and pray and fast on it if Ramadan has entered upon her, because it is possible that the seventh is menstruation and possible that it is not, so precaution became obligatory. When the eighth comes, she must perform ghusl a second time and make up the day she fasted on the seventh due to the possibility that she was menstruating on it, but she does not make up the prayer. If her habit was five and she menstruated six, then another seven, then another six, her habit is six by consensus, so that continuation builds upon it, because according to Abu Yusuf continuation builds on the last occurrence, but according to the two companions, she saw six twice. Similarly in al-Badai'. Place: as will be pointed out, and ten issues arise from it: five concerning what precedes her days, and five concerning what comes after them. The five for the preceding are fully mentioned, and as for the five for the later, their explanation according to al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: if she sees during her days what is [blood] and after it what is not, then all is menstruation; if she sees during her days what is and after it what is, and she sees an increase over her habit without exceeding ten, then all is menstruation; if it exceeds, she is returned to her habit and the excess is istihadah; if she sees after her days what is and does not see during her days anything, or she sees during her days what is not and after that this [blood] is seen, or she sees during her days what is not and after it what is not, then from Abu Hanifah there are two narrations in the three [cases]: one that the ruling is suspended as said for the preceding over her days, and in another narration it is menstruation, and that is the saying of his two companions, except that Muhammad says: it does not become a habit, and Abu Yusuf says: it becomes a habit. End. By this you learn what is in the commentator's speech of brevity, and that the correct is to exclude the second issue together with the first and restrict it that it does not exceed ten. His saying: (All is menstruation) is one narration from the Imam, i.e., without suspension on her seeing the like in the second month. By this, with what we presented from al-Siraj, you learn that what he mentioned in the consideration from the speech of the author of Fath al-Qadir is completely baseless, so pay attention. His saying: (Similarly) in al-Siraj: I say: Mentioned in al-Siraj first that transfer occurs only by two occurrences according to Abu Hanifah and Muhammad, and according to Abu Yusuf it occurs by one occurrence. Then he said: Its benefit appears when her bleeding continues. Then he said: And they agreed that if she sees that twice then her bleeding continues in the third month, she is returned to what happened twice consecutively, and similarly if her blood stops short of her habit at three days or four days, it is according this estimation. End. So ponder what the author transmitted from him. His saying: .
Source pages p. 371

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the transfer (intiqal) of a woman's menstrual habit (adah). It begins by stating that according to a single narration from Abu Hanifah, the habit transfers from menstruation. The author then mentions that al-Zahiriyyah distinguishes between transfer based on place versus number. The core dispute is whether the habit changes upon seeing a single differing occurrence or requires two consecutive occurrences. Abu Hanifah and Muhammad require two times, while Abu Yusuf accepts one time. The text then explains the ruling for a woman without a fixed habit: she uses the least in some matters (fast, prayer, reconciliation) and the most in others (completion of iddah, intercourse). A detailed example is given: if she sees six days of bleeding, she must perform ghusl on the seventh, pray and fast cautiously, and later make up the fast if bleeding resumes. The passage then outlines ten sub-cases involving blood seen before or after her customary days. These sub-cases depend on whether the blood occurs within her days, after them, and whether total bleeding exceeds ten days. For example, if she sees blood in her days and after, within ten days, it is all menstruation; if it exceeds ten, only the habitual days count. The text concludes by noting a consensus (ijma') that if she sees a pattern twice, it establishes her habit. The discussion emphasizes the importance of caution in matters of worship and the need to reconcile between rulings on various aspects of menstrual law.

Key Terms
العادة (al-ādah): A woman's established menstrual habit, i.e., the number of days she usually bleeds and the pattern of purity between periods.
الانتقال (al-intiqāl): The shift of a woman's menstrual habit from one duration/pattern to another based on observed changes.
الاستحاضة (al-istiḥāḍah): Non-menstrual bleeding that occurs outside the habitual days or beyond ten days, which does not prevent prayer or fasting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Twice
C) Three times
D) It never transfers

Key Takeaway
The transfer of menstrual habit requires two consecutive instances of the new pattern, according to the relied-upon Hanafi view.

The Mubtadi'ah: Default Rulings and Habit Establishment by One Occurrence
Ruling on the mubtadi'ah's default and habit establishment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the default menstrual and postnatal rulings for a mubtadi'ah, explain that her habit is established by one occurrence, and identify the correct view on when she leaves prayer.

Core Idea
A mubtadi'ah's habit is set by one occurrence; her maximum menstruation is ten days, and she leaves prayer immediately upon seeing blood.

This lesson covers the basic rulings for a woman who begins experiencing istihadah from puberty or after her first child (mubtadi'ah). The text from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies her default maximums for menstruation and postnatal bleeding, her obligation to perform wudu, and how she establishes a menstrual habit. Understanding these rules is essential for distinguishing her case from that of a woman with a prior habit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the category of woman
Recognise that a mubtadi'ah is a woman who experiences istihadah with no prior menstrual habit, either from the start of puberty or after her first childbirth.
The text specifies 'ولو مبتدأة' meaning 'even a beginner'.
2
State the default maximums
State that her menstruation is set to ten days and nifas to forty days by default, because the origin is soundness (istiṣḥāb) and the extrinsic is not judged without certainty.
These are the upper limits; her actual habit may be less.
3
Determine prayer obligations
The mustahadah and one with incontinence perform wudu for each prayer. The mubtadi'ah, upon seeing blood, leaves prayer immediately according to the correct view, though a narration from Abu Hanifah says she waits three days.
The correct view is immediate leave, as stated in the text.
4
Establish the habit
Explain that the habit of a mubtadi'ah is established by one occurrence of a blood-purity pattern (مرة واحدة), because she is transferring from a state of non-menstruation (الصغر).
This is unlike a habitual woman who requires repetition.
5
Apply an example
Given an example: a mubtadi'ah sees five days blood and fifteen days purity, then bleeding continues. She stops prayer for five days and prays fifteen days thereafter, as that becomes her habit.
Note: The text says 'وتثبت عادة هذه المبتدأة بمرة واحدة'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
استحاضة ولو مبتدأة فحيضها عشرة ونفاسها أربعون وتتوضأ المستحاضة ومن به سلس
أصلية
وهي
والمبسوط . ومنهم - كصاحب المحيط والمصفى - جعل هذا نظير العادة الجعلية وإنها نوعان : أن ترى دمين متفقين وطهرين متفقين على الولاء أو أكثر وأن الخلاف جار فيها، والجعلية تنتقل برؤية المخالف مرة واحدة اتفاقاً وهي أن ترى أطهاراً مختلفة ودماء مختلفة بأن رأت في الابتداء خمسة دماً وسبعة عشر طهراً ثم أربعة وستة عشر ثم ثلاثة وخمسة عشر، ثم استمر بها الدم. فعلى قول محمد بن ابراهيم يبني على أوسط الأعداد فتدع من أول الاستمرار أربعة وتصلي ستة عشر وذلك دأبها، وعلى قول ابن مزاحم تبني على أقل المرئيين الأخيرين فتدع ثلاثة وتصلي خمسة عشر فهذه عادتها جعلية لها في زمن الاستمرار، ولذلك سميت جعليه لأنها جعلت عادة للضرورة، ولا يخفى أن ما في البدائع وغيره أولى لأنه أحوط . ثم اختلفوا في العادة الجعلية إذا طرأت على العادة الأصلية هل تنتقض الأصلية؟ قال أئمة بلخ : لا لأنها دونها. وقال أئمة بخارى : نعم لأنها لا بد أن تتكرر في الجعلية خلاف ما كان في الأصلية فإن المرأة متى كانت عادتها الأصلية في الحيض خمسة فلا تثبت العادة الجعلية إلا برؤية ستة وسبعة وثمانية ويتكرر فيها خلاف العادة الأصلية مراراً، فالعادة الأصلية تنتقل بالتكرار بخلافها. كذا في المحيط. وفي المجتبى والعادة تنتقل عند أبي يوسف بأحد أمور ثلاثة بعدم رؤية مكانها مرة وبطهر صحيح صالح لنصب العادة يخالف الأول مرة، ودم صالح مخالف مرة وعندهما بتكرر هذه الأمور مرتين على الولاء اهـ.
:
قوله : (ولو) مبتدأة فحيضها عشرة ونفاسها أربعون أي لو كانت المستحاضة ابتدأت مع البلوغ مستحاضة أو مع الولد الأول فحيضها ونفاسها الأكثر لأن الأصل الصحة فلا يحكم بالعارض إلا بيقين وتترك الصلاة . بمجرد رؤية الدم على الصحيح كصاحبة العادة، وعن أبي حنيفة أنها لا تترك ما لم تستمر ثلاثة أيام وتثبت عادة هذه المبتدأة بمرة واحدة، فلو رأت خمسة دماً وخمسة عشر طهراً ثم استمر الدم فإنها تترك الصلاة من أول الاستمرار خمسة ثم تصلي خمسة عشر وذلك عادتها لأن الانتقال عن حالة الصغر في النساء لا يحصل إلا بمرة واحدة بخلاف المعتادة. ثم العادة في حق المبتدأة أيضاً نوعان أصلية وجعلية، فالأولى على وجهين: أحدهما أن ترى دمين خالصين وطهرين خالصين متفقين على الولاء بأن رأت مبتدأة ثلاثة دماً وخمسة عشر طهراً وثلاثة دماً وخمسة عشر طهراً ثم استمر بها الدم، فإنها تدع من أول الاستمرار وتصلي خمسة عشر لأن ذلك صار عادة أصلية لها بالتكرار. والثاني
الصلاة
(وأنها نوعان) أي جعل العادة مطلقاً نوعين: أصلية وهي أن ترى دمين الخ. وجعلية وهي أن ترى إطهاراً الخ. وقوله وإن الخلاف جارٍ فيها أي الخلاف السابق بين الإمامين وأبي يوسف في نقل بمرة أو لا. كذا يفهم من فتح القدير قوله : ( وتترك الصلاة أي المبتدأة. قوله : (لا يحصل إلا بمرة واحدة كذا في هذه النسخة بزيادة (إلا) ولم أرها في غيرها والصواب ما هنا تأمل. قوله :
العادة
Istihadah and even a beginner: her menstruation is ten and her postnatal bleeding is forty. The mustahadah and one with urinary incontinence perform wudu. Original: It is. And al-Mabsut. Among them, like the author of al-Muhit and al-Musaffa, considered this analogous to the placed habit (al-ādah al-ja'liyyah). And it is of two types: that she sees two matching bloods and two matching purities consecutively or more, and the difference runs in it. The placed habit transfers by seeing a differing [pattern] once by agreement, and it is that she sees different purities and different bloods, such as she saw initially five days blood and seventeen days purity, then four and sixteen, then three and fifteen, then bleeding continued. According to the saying of Muhammad ibn Ibrahim, she builds on the middle numbers, so she leaves from the beginning of the continuation four days and prays sixteen days, and that is her pattern. According to Ibn Muzahim's saying, she builds on the least of the last two seen, so she leaves three and prays fifteen, and this is her placed habit for the time of continuation. Therefore it was called placed because a habit was placed for necessity. And it is not hidden that what is in al-Badai' and others is more appropriate because it is more precautionary. Then they differed regarding the placed habit when it occurs upon the original habit: does it break the original? The scholars of Balkh said: No, because it is less than it. The scholars of Bukhara said: Yes, because it must be repeated in the placed habit contrary to what was in the original, for a woman whose original habit in menstruation is five, the placed habit is not established except by seeing six, seven, and eight, and the contrary of the original habit is repeated many times, so the original habit transfers by repetition unlike that. Likewise in al-Muhit. In al-Mujtaba: The habit transfers according to Abu Yusuf by one of three things: by not seeing its place once, by a sound purity fit for establishing a habit that differs from the first once, and by a sound blood that differs once. And according to the two companions, by repeating these things twice consecutively. End. His saying: (And even) a beginner: her menstruation is ten and her postnatal bleeding is forty, meaning if the mustahadah began with puberty as istihadah or with the first child, then her menstruation and postnatal bleeding are the maximum, because the origin is soundness, so the extrinsic is not judged except with certainty. She leaves prayer upon merely seeing blood according to the correct view, like the woman with a habit. From Abu Hanifah that she does not leave until bleeding continues for three days. And the habit of this beginner is established by one occurrence. So if she sees five days blood and fifteen days purity, then bleeding continues, she leaves prayer from the beginning of the continuation five days, then prays fifteen days, and that is her habit, because the transfer from the state of non-menstruation (minority) only occurs once, unlike the habitual woman. Then the habit regarding the beginner is also of two types: original and placed. The first has two aspects: one that she sees two pure bloods and two pure purities consecutive, such that a beginner sees three blood and fifteen purity and three blood and fifteen purity, then bleeding continues, she leaves from the beginning of the continuation and prays fifteen, because that became her original habit by repetition. The second: prayer. (And that it is two types): i.e., establishing the habit absolutely is two types: original, and it is that she sees two bloods, etc., and placed, and it is that she sees purities, etc. And his saying: 'and the difference runs in it' i.e., the previous difference between the two Imams and Abu Yusuf regarding transfer by once or not, as understood from Fath al-Qadir. His saying: (and she leaves prayer) i.e., the beginner. His saying: (does not occur except by one occurrence) — thus in this copy with an extra (except), and I have not seen it in others, and the correct is what is here, ponder. His saying: the habit.
Source pages p. 372

Commentary
This passage discusses rulings for a mubtadi'ah (a woman experiencing istihadah from the onset of puberty or after her first childbirth). It states that her menstruation period defaults to the maximum of ten days, and postnatal (nifas) to forty days. The mustahadah and one with chronic incontinence perform wudu for each prayer. The text then explains two types of habit: original (asliyyah) and placed (ja'liyyah). Original habit is established by seeing two matching bloods and purities consecutively. Placed habit is set by seeing a pattern of different purities and bloods, and it transfers by one occurrence of a differing pattern according to consensus. The text presents two methods of calculation from later scholars: Muhammad ibn Ibrahim builds on the average of the numbers, while Ibn Muzahim builds on the least of the last two seen. The more precautionary view is from al-Badai'. A dispute among Hanafi scholars regarding whether the placed habit can override the original habit is mentioned: scholars of Balkh say no, while scholars of Bukhara say yes if it is repeated. The passage then cites al-Mujtaba for the transfer of habit according to Abu Yusuf by three things (once) and the two companions require repetition twice. Finally, the commentary on the matn clarifies that for a beginner, her habit is established by one occurrence, and she leaves prayer immediately upon seeing blood according to the correct view, though there is a narration from Abu Hanifah that she waits three days.

Key Terms
المبتدأة (al-mubtadi'ah): A woman who experiences istihadah from the beginning of puberty or from her first childbirth, having no established menstrual habit.
العادة (al-ādah): The menstrual habit, i.e., the consistent pattern of blood and purity that she relies on when bleeding continues.
الصغر (al-ṣighar): Literally 'minority', refers to the state before puberty or before having a menstrual habit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A mubtadi'ah sees her first blood pattern: 3 days blood, 20 days purity, then continuous bleeding. How many days does she stop praying at the beginning of the continuation?
A) 10 days
B) 3 days
C) 20 days
D) She does not stop praying until the blood lasts 3 days.

Key Takeaway
A mubtadi'ah's menstrual habit is set by one visible blood-purity pattern, and she acts on that pattern when bleeding continues, with the correct view being she leaves prayer immediately upon seeing blood.

Original and Placed Habits: Definition, Calculation, and the Dispute on Overriding
Expansion on habit types, calculation, and disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between original (asliyyah) and placed (ja'liyyah) habits, explain two methods for calculating the placed habit, and evaluate the scholarly dispute on whether a placed habit can override the original habit.

Core Idea
The placed habit is a practical necessity for continuous bleeding; its overriding of the original habit is disputed based on repetition.

This lesson delves into the two types of menstrual habit for a mubtadi'ah: original (asliyyah) established by two matching patterns, and placed (ja'liyyah) established artificially when patterns vary. The text presents two calculation methods for the placed habit and records a significant intra-Hanafi dispute among the scholars of Balkh and Bukhara on whether the placed habit can override the original habit. Additionally, the general rules for transferring a habit between schools (Abu Yusuf vs Sahibayn) are discussed.

Guided Path
1
Define the two types of habit
Identify original habit (asliyyah) as established by two consecutive matching blood-purity patterns. Identify placed habit (ja'liyyah) as a constructed habit for cases where patterns differ and bleeding continues.
The text says 'والجعلية هي أن ترى أطهاراً مختلفة ودماء مختلفة'
2
Understand the two calculation methods for the placed habit
Recognise the method of Muhammad ibn Ibrahim: take the average of the numbers of blood days from the past patterns. Recognise the method of Ibn Muzahim: take the least of the last two blood days seen.
The text prefers the view in al-Badai' (Muhammad ibn Ibrahim's) as more precautionary (أحوط).
3
Analyse the dispute on whether the placed habit overrides the original
Scholars of Balkh say the placed habit does not override the original because the original is stronger. Scholars of Bukhara say it does override if the placed habit repeats enough to transfer the original habit.
The text cites al-Muhit and al-Mujtaba for this dispute.
4
Examine the rules for habit transfer (intra-Hanafi)
According to Abu Yusuf, the habit transfers by any one of three things occurring once: not seeing by its place, a sound purity differing once, or a sound blood differing once. According to the two companions (Sahibayn), these must occur twice consecutively.
This is a general rule for women with an established habit, not specific to the mubtadi'ah.
5
Apply the placed habit to a case
Given the example in the text: a woman sees patterns of (5 blood + 17 purity), (4+16), (3+15), then continuous bleeding. She constructs a habit: under Muhammad ibn Ibrahim, leave 4 (average of 5,4,3) and pray 16; under Ibn Muzahim, leave 3 (least of last two: 4 and 3) and pray 15.
The constructed habit is called 'placed' because it is created for necessity.

Commentary
This passage discusses rulings for a mubtadi'ah (a woman experiencing istihadah from the onset of puberty or after her first childbirth). It states that her menstruation period defaults to the maximum of ten days, and postnatal (nifas) to forty days. The mustahadah and one with chronic incontinence perform wudu for each prayer. The text then explains two types of habit: original (asliyyah) and placed (ja'liyyah). Original habit is established by seeing two matching bloods and purities consecutively. Placed habit is set by seeing a pattern of different purities and bloods, and it transfers by one occurrence of a differing pattern according to consensus. The text presents two methods of calculation from later scholars: Muhammad ibn Ibrahim builds on the average of the numbers, while Ibn Muzahim builds on the least of the last two seen. The more precautionary view is from al-Badai'. A dispute among Hanafi scholars regarding whether the placed habit can override the original habit is mentioned: scholars of Balkh say no, while scholars of Bukhara say yes if it is repeated. The passage then cites al-Mujtaba for the transfer of habit according to Abu Yusuf by three things (once) and the two companions require repetition twice. Finally, the commentary on the matn clarifies that for a beginner, her habit is established by one occurrence, and she leaves prayer immediately upon seeing blood according to the correct view, though there is a narration from Abu Hanifah that she waits three days.

Key Terms
العادة الأصلية (al-ādah al-aṣliyyah): The original menstrual habit established by seeing two matching bloods and two matching purities consecutively.
العادة الجعلية (al-ādah al-ja'liyyah): A habit imposed artificially for continuity (when a woman's pattern varies and bleeding continues) based on averaging or least of last two.
أوسط الأعداد (awsaṭ al-a'dād): The middle (average) of the numbers of blood days seen in the past patterns, used in Muhammad ibn Ibrahim's method.
أقل المرئيين الأخيرين (aqall al-mar'iyyayn al-ākhirayn): The lesser of the last two blood day numbers seen, used in Ibn Muzahim's method.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the difference between the methods of Muhammad ibn Ibrahim and Ibn Muzahim for the placed habit?
A) Muhammad ibn Ibrahim uses the average of all past blood days; Ibn Muzahim uses the most recent.
B) Muhammad ibn Ibrahim uses the average; Ibn Muzahim uses the least of the last two blood day numbers.
C) Both use the average but with different starting points.
D) Ibn Muzahim uses the mode, Muhammad ibn Ibrahim uses the median.

Key Takeaway
The placed habit (ja'liyyah) is a constructed schedule for irregular bleeding; its overriding of the original habit is disputed and requires repetition according to the preferred view.

Establishing the Menstrual Habit for a Mubtadi'ah
Explaining the ruling on establishing the menstrual habit for a first-time menstruator and the types of habitual periods.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on establishing the menstrual habit for a first-time menstruator and apply the rules for determining the habit in cases of original and artificial habits.

Core Idea
A first-time menstruator's habit is established by one cycle, and her habit determines prayer during irregular bleeding.

A woman who begins menstruation and then experiences irregular bleeding (istihadah) must know her habit (ada) to know when to pray and fast. The Hanafi school provides detailed rules for establishing this habit, distinguishing between a first-time menstruator (mubtadi'ah) and one with an established pattern. This lesson unpacks the rulings from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, covering default maximums, when to stop praying, and how to define the habit from diverse cycles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default maximum durations
For a mubtadi'ah who begins as mustahadah, the default hayd is 10 days and nifas 40 days because the original state of purity is presumed sound until certainty of alteration.
This applies if she has no prior habit.
2
Determine when she stops praying
According to the majority (Sahibayn and later Hanafis), she stops praying immediately upon seeing blood. Abu Hanifa held she must wait three days to confirm it is hayd.
The correct view (asahh) is immediate stop, as per the text.
3
Establish the habit with one occurrence
For a mubtadi'ah, one complete cycle of blood and purity establishes her habit. Example: if she sees 5 days blood then 15 purity, and then continuous bleeding, her habit is 5 blood and 15 purity.
This is based on the rule that transition from childhood to menstruation occurs with one instance.
4
Distinguish original vs artificial habit
Original habit (adah asliyyah) is formed by two identical consecutive cycles. Artificial habit (adah jaliyyah) is derived from three or more different cycles during istihadah.
For original, if cycles are identical, that becomes the habit. If differing, Abu Yusuf takes the first cycle; others take the lesser.
5
Apply the artificial habit rules
For three differing cycles, scholars differ: some take the middle numbers (awsat al-a'dad), others take the minimum of the last two (aqall al-mar'iyayn al-akhirayn). When both methods agree, it is unanimous.
The text mentions al-Muhit endorses the middle numbers as preferred.

His saying: (And if) a first-time menstruator, then her menses is ten and her postpartum bleeding is forty, meaning if the woman with istihadah began with puberty as mustahadah or with the first child, then her menses and postpartum bleeding are the maximum because the default is soundness, so the incidental is not ruled upon except with certainty, and she leaves prayer upon merely seeing blood according to the correct view like the woman with a habit. So if she saw five blood and fifteen purity then blood continued, she leaves prayer from the start of continuation five then prays fifteen, and that is her habit because the transition from childhood in women does not occur except with one occurrence unlike the accustomed. If she saw three blood and fifteen purity and four blood and sixteen purity and three blood and fifteen purity, then her habit is three in blood and fifteen in purity because we consider what she saw last as attached to what she saw first since it is confirmed by repetition so it becomes an artificial habit. Thus in al-Muhit. And the remaining issues of the first-time menstruator are mentioned in it, so whoever seeks them should refer to it, and we did not present them due to the fear of prolongation leading to boredom.
