Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute passage explaining the ruling on establishing the menstrual habit (ada) for a first-time menstruator (mubtadi'ah). The commentator first clarifies that a woman who begins menstruation at puberty or after first childbirth as a mustahadah (irregular bleed) has the maximum duration of hayd (10 days) and nifas (40 days) as her default, because the default is considered sound until proven otherwise. She stops praying upon seeing blood immediately, according to the majority view, though Abu Hanifa held she waits until three days to confirm. Her habit is established with one occurrence: e.g., if she sees 5 days blood then 15 purity, then blood continues, she considers the initial pattern as her habit. The 'ada (habit) for a mubtadi'ah also has two types: original (asliyyah) and artificial (jaliyyah). Original habit occurs when she sees two identical cycles of blood and purity consecutively, e.g., 3 days blood and 15 purity repeated; then her habit is 3/15. If the two cycles differ (e.g., 3 blood/15 purity then 4 blood/16 purity), Abu Yusuf takes the first occurrence as the habit, while his companions (Abu Yusuf's two? Actually it says 'they differed concerning his two companions (qawluhuma)' meaning Abu Yusuf's two companions: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad? The text mentions differing views: some take the first occurrence, some take the lesser of the two because the lesser is contained in the greater. The artificial habit (adah jaliyyah) applies when she sees three cycles with different numbers, e.g., 5/17, 4/16, 3/15. Scholars differ: some take the middle numbers (4 blood, 16 purity), others take the minimum of the last two cycles (3 blood, 15 purity). If possibilities agree, the ruling is unanimous. The passage ends noting that more details are in al-Muhit.

Key Terms
مبتدأة (mubtadi'ah): A woman who begins menstruation for the first time, either at puberty or after her first childbirth, and then experiences istihadah (irregular bleeding).
عادة أصلية (adah asliyyah): The original habit of a woman, established by seeing two identical cycles (blood and purity) consecutively.
عادة جعلية (adah jaliyyah): An artificial habit derived from different cycles during istihadah, used to determine when to pray during continuous bleeding.

Key Takeaway
A mubtadi'ah's menstrual habit is established with one cycle; during istihadah, she acts on that habit, and artificial habits are derived by either middle numbers or the minimum of the last two cycles.

Wudu for Mustahadah and Those with Continuous Invalidating States
Ruling with proof for wudu per prayer time.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wudu for a mustahadah and those with similar conditions, identify the proof, and distinguish between wudu for a prayer time versus wudu for each prayer.

Core Idea
One wudu per prayer time suffices for all prayers within that time.

This passage clarifies a crucial concession for those with chronic invalidating states. While normal wudu breaks upon exiting an impurity, those with continuous conditions (istihadah, urinary incontinence, etc.) are required to perform wudu only once for the entire time segment of each obligatory prayer. The key is the Arabic phrase 'li-waqti kulli fard' – for the time of each obligatory prayer – which is derived from a hadith and interpreted by the Hanafi school to ease the burden on such individuals.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject of the ruling
Who is included? The mustahadah (woman with non-menstrual bleeding), one with urinary incontinence, chronic diarrhea, persistent flatulence, continuous nosebleed, or a wound that does not stop bleeding. Note the definition of istihadah: vaginal blood not from the uterus, lacking the odor of hayd.
The passage lists multiple causes for a woman to be considered mustahadah (blood during pregnancy, exceeding ten days, etc.).
2
State the ruling and its level
The ruling: such a person must perform wudu for the time of each obligatory prayer (e.g., Zuhr time). This wudu is wajib (obligatory) for that time period. With one wudu, she may pray any number of prayers (fard, sunnah, nafil) until that time ends.
It is not required to renew wudu for each individual prayer within the same time.
3
Examine the proof (dalil)
The proof is the hadith: 'al-mustahadah tatawaddu' li-waqti kulli salat' (the mustahadah performs wudu for the time of each prayer). The Hanafi school interprets the lam (li) as indicating time, not the prayer act. Another variant 'tatawaddu' likulli salat' is also interpreted to mean 'for the time' for consistency.
This hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), but its meaning is clear (qat'i al-dalala) according to Hanafi usul.
4
Contrast with other madhahib
The Shafi'i school holds that such a person must perform wudu for each fard prayer, not just for the time. If she makes wudu before the time, it does not count. The practical difference: a Hanafi can pray multiple farḍ prayers within one time (e.g., make-up prayers) with one wudu, while a Shafi'i must renew wudu for each fard.
The Hanafi position is the relied-upon (mufta bīhi) and is based on the literal interpretation of the hadith.
5
Apply to a scenario
Example: A mustahadah woman performs wudu at the start of Zuhr time. She can pray the sunnah of Zuhr, the fard of Zuhr, and any nafil prayers until the end of Zuhr time. When Asr time begins, she must perform a new wudu.
The wudu remains valid for that entire time segment, even if she is in a state of continuous blood flow.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( وتتوضأ المستحاضة ومن به سلس بول أو استطلاق بطن أو انفلات ربح أو رعاف دائم أو جرح لا يرقأ لوقت كل (فرض) لما كان الحيض أكثر وقوعاً قدمه، ثم أعقبه الاستحاضة لأنه أكثر وقوعاً من النفاس فإنها تكون مستحاضة بما إذا رأت الدم حالة الحبل، أو زاد الدم على العشرة، أو زاد الدم على عادتها وجاوز العشرة أو رأت ما دون الثلاث، أو رأت قبل تمام الطهر، أو رأت قبل أن تبلغ تسع سنين على ما عليه العامة. وكذا من أسباب الاستحاضة إذا زاد الدم على الأربعين في النفاس أو زاد على عادتها وجاوز الأربعين، وكذا ما تراه الآيسة بخلاف النفاس فإن سببه شيء واحد . وقدم حكم الاستحاضة ومن بمعناها على تفريعها لأن المقصود بيان الحكم. ودم الاستحاضة اسم لدم خارج من الفرج دون الرحم وعلامته أنه لا رائحة له ودم الحيض منتن الرائحة ومن به سلس بول وهو من لا يقدر على امساكه والرعاف الدم الخارج . من الأنف والجرح الذي لا يرقأ أي الذي لا يسكن دمه من رقا الدم سكن وإنما كان وضوءها لوقت كل فرض لا لكل صلاة لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام المستحاضة تتوضأ لوقت كل صلاة) رواه سبط ابن الجوزي عن أبي حنيفة. وحديث توضئ لكل صلاة محمول عليه لأن اللام للوقت. وفي الفتاوى الظهيرية : رجل رعف أو سال
His saying: (And the mustahadah and one who has urinary incontinence or diarrhea or passing wind or persistent nosebleed or a wound that does not clot perform wudu for the time of each obligatory prayer) because hayd is more frequent, so he mentioned it first, then followed it with istihadah because it is more frequent than nifas. Commentary
This is a ruling statement with proof, explaining the obligation of wudu for a mustahadah and others with continuous invalidating states (urinary incontinence, diarrhea, persistent flatulence, chronic nosebleed, non-clotting wound). The commentator first explains the order of presentation: hayd is most frequent, then istihadah, then nifas. Istihadah is defined as vaginal bleeding not from the uterus, distinguished from hayd by lacking odor. Causes include bleeding during pregnancy, exceeding 10 days, etc. The key ruling: such a person must perform wudu for the time of each obligatory prayer (like zuhr, asr), not for each prayer (like each rak'ah or each sunnah). The proof is the hadith 'al-mustahadah tatawaddu' li-waqti kulli salat,' meaning she performs wudu at the time of each prayer. Another version 'tatawaddu' likulli salat' is interpreted the same way because the lam (for) indicates time. So one wudu suffices for that time period (e.g., for zuhr and its sunnah, and any nafil until the time expires). There is also a mention from al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah about a nosebleed case.

Key Terms
مستحاضة (mustahadah): A woman who experiences vaginal bleeding outside the normal menstrual period, i.e., bleeding that is not hayd.
سلس بول (sals al-bawl): Urinary incontinence: the inability to retain urine.
استطلاق بطن (istitlaq al-batn): Continuous diarrhea.
لوقت كل فرض (li-waqti kulli fard): For the time of each obligatory prayer (i.e., one wudu suffices for the entire time segment).
رعاف دائم (ru'af da'im): Persistent nosebleed.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school grants a significant concession to those with chronic invalidating states: one wudu per prayer time suffices for all prayers within that time, easing their worship without nullifying their obligation to pray.

Determining Habitual Menstrual Patterns (Ada Jal'iyya)
Intra-Hanafi dispute on constructing menstrual habit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules for constructing a habitual menstrual pattern from multiple cycles and identify the differing positions of Abu Yusuf and other Hanafi scholars.

Core Idea
A woman's menstrual habit is not fixed; it can shift or be constructed from observed patterns.

When a woman experiences irregular bleeding (istihadah), she must rely on her established habit to distinguish menstrual days from non-menstrual days. But what if no single pattern emerges? Hanafi jurists developed the concept of 'ada jal'iyya (constructed habit) to extrapolate a habit from multiple contradictory cycles. In this lesson, we explore the intra-Hanafi dispute over how to construct that habit and apply the differing rulings to real scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario type
Determine whether the woman has observed two cycles or three cycles. The rules differ for each case.
Two-cycle case: simple habit determination. Three-cycle case: constructed habit.
2
State Abu Yusuf's rule for two cycles
According to Abu Yusuf, the habit is based on the last occurrence (blood and purity). The habit shifts upon seeing a single contradictory cycle.
Contrary to a misreading that says 'first time'; the correct ruling is 'last time'.
3
State the alternative views for two cycles
Some say the habit remains the first seen; others say it is the lesser of the two amounts, because the lesser is implicitly contained in the greater.
The 'lesser' view is based on continuity of the smaller amount.
4
Apply the constructed habit (three cycles)
For three different cycles, two views exist: take the middle number of the three, or take the lesser of the last two. If the last cycle repeats the first, the first pattern is confirmed by repetition.
The 'middle number' is the median; the 'lesser of last two' is the minimum of the final two cycles.
5
Determine the habit in a given case
Given a set of observed cycles, calculate the habit using each position and note the practical difference.
Focus on the final ruling: which view is adopted for fatwa?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أن ترى دمين وطهرين مختلفين بأن رأت ثلاثة دماً وخمسة عشر طهراً وأربعة دماً وستة عشر طهراً ثم استمر بها الدم فعند أبي يوسف أيام حيضها وطهرها ما رأت أول مرة صوابه آخر مرة كما في المحيط معللاً بقوله لأن عنده العادة تنتقل برؤية المخالف مرة واحدة. واختلفوا في قولهما فقيل عادتها ما رأته أول مرة وقيل عادتها أقل المرتين لأن الأقل موجود في الأكثر فيتكرر الأقل معنى. وأما العادة الجعلية فهي أن ترى ثلاثة دماء وأطهار مختلفة، ثم استمر الدم بها بأن رأت خمسة دماً وسبعة عشر طهراً. وأربعة دماً وستة عشر طهراً وثلاثة دماً . وخمسة عشر طهراً. واختلفوا فقيل عادتها أوسط الأعداد فتدع من أول الاستمرار أربعة وتصلي ستة عشر، وقيل أقل المرئيين الأخيرين فتدع من أول الاستمرار ثلاثة وتصلي خمسة عشر، فلو رأت مبتدأة ثلاثة دماً وخمسة عشر طهراً وأربعة دماً وستة عشر طهراً وخمسة دماً وسبعة عشر طهراً ثم استمر بها الدم، فعادتها أربعة في الدم وستة عشر في الطهر اتفاقاً لأن ذلك أقل المرئيين الأخيرين وأوسط الأعداد. ولو رأت ثلاثة دماً وخمسة عشر طهراً وأربعة دماً وستة عشر طهراً وثلاثة دماً وخمسة عشر طهراً، فإن عادتها ثلاثة في الدم وخمسة عشر في الطهر لأنا جعلنا ما رأته آخراً مضموماً إلى ما رأته أولاً لأنه تأكد بالتكرار فصار عادة جعلية لها. كذا في المحيط.
That she sees two bleedings and two purities different, for example she sees three blood and fifteen purity, and four blood and sixteen purity, then blood continues with her. According to Abu Yusuf, her days of menstruation and purity are what she saw the first time. Correct: the last time as in al-Muhit, because according to him the habit shifts by seeing a contradictory once. And they differed regarding his statement: some said her habit is what she saw the first time, and some said her habit is the lesser of the two because the lesser exists in the greater so the lesser is repeated in meaning. As for the constructed habit, it is that she sees three bleedings and different purities, then blood continues with her: she saw five blood and seventeen purity, four blood and sixteen purity, three blood and fifteen purity. They differed: some said her habit is the middle number, so she leaves from the start of continuation four and prays sixteen; some said the lesser of the last two sightings, so she leaves from the start three and prays fifteen. If a beginner sees three blood and fifteen purity, four blood and sixteen purity, five blood and seventeen purity, then blood continues, her habit is four in blood and sixteen in purity by agreement because that is the lesser of the last two and the middle number. And if she sees three blood and fifteen purity, four blood and sixteen purity, three blood and fifteen purity, her habit is three in blood and fifteen in purity because we made what she last saw added to what she first saw because it is confirmed by repetition, so it becomes a constructed habit for her. Thus in al-Muhit.
Source pages p. 373

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq is an expansion probe on the rules for establishing a habitual menstrual pattern for a woman who experiences istihadah (chronic bleeding). It discusses two scenarios: when a woman sees two different cycles (case 1) and when she sees three cycles (case 2, the constructed habit). The text begins with the ruling of Abu Yusuf: he considers the habit to be established based on the last occurrence of blood and purity, contrary to a misreading that says 'first time'. This is clarified by a note from al-Muhit. Then a disagreement is mentioned: some say the habit is the first seen, others say the least amount, because the lesser is implicitly present in the greater. For the constructed habit (three cycles), there are two views: either take the middle number or the lesser of the last two. If the woman is a beginner (first time), if she sees three cycles ending with the most numbers, the habit is the middle number by agreement. If she sees three cycles where the last matches the first, the habit is the first one because repetition confirms it. The passage concludes by referring to al-Muhit for the remaining issues about beginners. The key takeaway is that the Hanafi school relies on the concept of habit to distinguish menstrual blood from istihadah, and there is flexibility in how the habit is determined based on individual circumstances.

Key Terms
عادة جعلية ('ada jal'iyya): A habit that is constructed from multiple observations of different blood and purity durations.
مبتدأة (mubtada'a): A woman who experiences bleeding for the first time without a prior habit.
استمرار (istimrar): The continuation of bleeding after observing a few cycles, indicating istihadah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) 3.5 blood, 15.5 purity

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uses the concept of constructed habit ('ada jal'iyya) to determine a woman's menstrual pattern from multiple contradictory cycles, with differing views on whether to adopt the middle number or the lesser of the last two.

Wudu for Mustahadah and Those with Chronic Excuses
Ruling with proof for chronic excuse wudu.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a mustahadah and other persons with chronic excuses perform wudu for the time of each fard prayer, and apply the condition that a new impurity nullifies the wudu.

Core Idea
Mustahadah and similar excuse-holders: one wudu per fard time, not per prayer.

In this passage, the commentator explains the ruling for individuals with continuous impurities—such as mustahadah, chronic nosebleed, or urinary incontinence. The key principle is that they perform wudu for the time of each obligatory prayer, not for every individual prayer. This ruling is derived from a hadith and refined by conditions about new impurities.

Guided Path
1
Identify the persons covered by the ruling
List the six types: mustahadah, urinary incontinence, stomach leakage, persistent flatulence, chronic nosebleed, non-clotting wound. Note that the most common is mustahadah.
The commentator explains why mustahadah is discussed after menstruation: it is more frequent than postpartum bleeding.
2
State the ruling: wudu for each fard time
The matn states they perform wudu for the time of every fard (obligatory prayer), not for each individual prayer or nafl.
The hukm level is wajib, derived from the hadith interpreted with the letter lam indicating time.
3
Identify the hadith proof and its interpretation
The hadith quoted: 'المستحاضة تتوضأ لوقت كل صلاة' (The mustahadah performs wudu for the time of every prayer). The lam in 'li-waqt' is understood as for the time, not for the prayer itself. This refutes the interpretation that wudu is required for each prayer.
The hadith is narrated by Sibte Ibn al-Jawzi from Abu Hanifa, considered zanni in transmission and meaning.
4
Explain the condition about new impurities
From Al-Bada'i: The purity of the excuse-holder remains only if no new impurity occurs. A new event (e.g., blood from a different nostril) nullifies the wudu. However, if both nostrils were bleeding at the time of wudu and one stops, the wudu remains valid.
This is an important qualification: the continuous impurity does not break wudu, but a separate new impurity does.
5
Apply to a nosebleed scenario from Al-Zahiriyya
A man with a nosebleed should wait until near the end of the prayer time. If bleeding continues, he performs wudu and prays before time exits. If bleeding stops after the time and continues to the next time, he must repeat the previous prayer. If it does not stop in the second time, his prayer is valid.
This shows the practical application: the wudu is tied to the time, and if the impurity ceases, the ruling changes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( وتتوضأ المستحاضة ومن به سلس بول أو استطلاق بطن أو انفلات ربح أو رعاف دائم أو جرح لا يرقأ لوقت كل (فرض) لما كان الحيض أكثر وقوعاً قدمه، ثم أعقبه الاستحاضة لأنه أكثر وقوعاً من النفاس فإنها تكون مستحاضة بما إذا رأت الدم حالة الحبل، أو زاد الدم على العشرة، أو زاد الدم على عادتها وجاوز العشرة أو رأت ما دون الثلاث، أو رأت قبل تمام الطهر، أو رأت قبل أن تبلغ تسع سنين على ما عليه العامة. وكذا من أسباب الاستحاضة إذا زاد الدم على الأربعين في النفاس أو زاد على عادتها وجاوز الأربعين، وكذا ما تراه الآيسة بخلاف النفاس فإن سببه شيء واحد . وقدم حكم الاستحاضة ومن بمعناها على تفريعها لأن المقصود بيان الحكم. ودم الاستحاضة اسم لدم خارج من الفرج دون الرحم وعلامته أنه لا رائحة له ودم الحيض منتن الرائحة ومن به سلس بول وهو من لا يقدر على امساكه والرعاف الدم الخارج . من الأنف والجرح الذي لا يرقأ أي الذي لا يسكن دمه من رقا الدم سكن وإنما كان وضوءها لوقت كل فرض لا لكل صلاة لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام المستحاضة تتوضأ لوقت كل صلاة) رواه سبط ابن الجوزي عن أبي حنيفة. وحديث توضئ لكل صلاة محمول عليه لأن اللام للوقت. وفي الفتاوى الظهيرية : رجل رعف أو سال من جرحه دم ينتظر آخر الوقت، إن لم ينقطع الدم توضأ وصلى قبل خروج الوقت، فإن توضأ وصلى ثم خرج الوقت ودخل وقت صلاة أخرى وانقطع الدم ودام الانقطاع إلى وقت صلاة أخرى توضأ وأعاد الصلاة وإن لم ينقطع في وقت الصلاة الثانية حتى خرج الوقت جازت الصلاة ا هـ . وسيأتي إيضاحه. وقيد بالوضوء لأنه لا يجب عليها الاستنجاء لوقت كل صلاة. كذا في الظهيرية أيضاً. وفي البدائع : وإنما تبقى طهارة صاحب العذر في الوقت إذا لم يحدث حدثاً آخر، أما إذا أحدث حدثاً آخر فلا تبقى كما إذا سال الدم من فتوضأ ثم سال من المنخر الآخر فعليه الوضوء لأن هذا حدث جديد لم يكن موجوداً وقت الطهارة، فأما إذا سال منهما جميعاً فتوضأ ثم انقطع أحدهما فهو على وضوئه ما بقي الوقت اهـ.
His statement: (And the mustahadah and whoever has urinary incontinence, or stomach leakage, or passing wind, or persistent nosebleed, or a wound that does not clot performs wudu for the time of every fard) because menstruation is more frequent so he presented it, then he followed it with istihadah because it is more frequent than postpartum. She becomes mustahadah if she sees blood during pregnancy, or the blood exceeds ten [days], or exceeds her habit and exceeds ten, or she sees less than three, or she sees before complete purity, or she sees before reaching nine years according to the general view. Likewise among causes of istihadah: if blood exceeds forty in postpartum, or exceeds her habit and exceeds forty, and likewise what an old woman sees, unlike postpartum whose cause is one. He presented the ruling of istihadah and those like it before its branches because the purpose is to explain the ruling. The blood of istihadah is blood coming out from the vulva not from the womb; its sign is that it has no odor, while menstrual blood is foul smelling. He with urinary incontinence is one who cannot hold it. Nosebleed is blood exiting from the nose. A wound that does not clot means its blood does not stop. Her wudu is for the time of every fard, not for every prayer, because of his saying, peace be upon him: "The mustahadah performs wudu for the time of every prayer" narrated by Sibte Ibn al-Jawzi from Abu Hanifa. The hadith "perform wudu for every prayer" is interpreted as for the time, because the lam is for time. In al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya: A man who has a nosebleed or blood flows from his wound, he waits until the end of the time; if the blood does not stop, he performs wudu and prays before the time exits. If he performs wudu and prays, then the time exits and the time of another prayer enters and the blood stops and the stoppage continues until the time of another prayer, he performs wudu and repeats the prayer. And if it does not stop in the time of the second prayer until the time exits, his prayer is valid. Its clarification will come. It is restricted to wudu because she does not have to perform istinja for every prayer. Thus in al-Zahiriyya also. And in al-Bada'i: The purity of the person with an excuse remains in the time if he does not commit another event. If he commits another event, it does not remain: if blood flows from [one nostril] and he performs wudu, then flows from the other nostril, he must perform wudu because this is a new event that was not present at the time of purification. As for if it flows from both, then he performs wudu, then one stops, he remains upon his wudu as long as the time remains.
Source pages p. 373

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn statement regarding the wudu of those with chronic excuses: mustahadah, urinary incontinence, stomach leakage, persistent flatulence, chronic nosebleed, or a non-clotting wound. The commentator first explains why menstruation is discussed before istihadah (because it is more common). Then lists causes of istihadah including during pregnancy, exceeding 10 days, etc. Then defines istihadah blood: it comes from the vulva but not the womb, and has no foul odor (unlike menstrual blood). The key ruling: such persons perform wudu for the time of each fard prayer, not for each prayer. This is derived from the hadith: 'The mustahadah performs wudu for the time of every prayer.' The letter 'lam' in 'li-waqt' indicates the time. The commentator then cites from Al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah a detailed case of a man with a nosebleed: he should wait until near the end of the prayer time; if the bleeding stops, he performs wudu and prays; if it continues, he prays before time runs out. If the bleeding stops after the time and continues to the next time, he must repeat the previous prayer. Also, istinja is not required for each prayer. From Al-Bada'i, a clarification: the purity of the person with an excuse persists only if no new impurity occurs; if blood flows from a different nostril after wudu, it nullifies the wudu. But if both nostrils were bleeding at the time of wudu and then one stops, the wudu remains valid because the impurity was already existent.

Key Terms
مستحاضة (mustahada): A woman experiencing non-menstrual bleeding from the vulva (not womb) with no foul odor.
سلس بول (sals al-bawl): Urinary incontinence; inability to hold urine.
استطلاق بطن (istitlaq al-batn): Continuous leakage from the stomach (likely diarrhea or similar).
انفلات ريح (infilat rih): Involuntary passing of wind (flatulence).
رعاف دائم (ru'af da'im): Chronic nosebleed that does not stop.
جرح لا يرقأ (jurh la yarqa'): A wound that does not clot or stop bleeding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A mustahadah performs wudu at the beginning of Zuhr time. She prays Zuhr, then Asr time enters while she is still pure (no new impurity). Can she pray Asr with the same wudu?
A) Yes, because wudu is for the time of each fard.
B) No, she must perform new wudu for Asr.
C) It is better to renew wudu.
D) She can only pray one fard per wudu.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that chronic excuse holders perform wudu for each fard prayer time, not for each prayer, and a new impurity breaks the wudu.

Branch Rulings for People with Chronic Excuses
Branch rulings on conduct of those with continuous impurities.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the key furu' from the Hanafi school regarding the prayer and purity of a person with a chronic excuse, and apply the rulings on bandaging, washing garments, stopping flow, gesture prayer, and the condition of time coverage.

Core Idea
A person with a chronic excuse must take reasonable measures, but impurity is excused if continuous.

This passage from Bahr al-Raiq presents several branch rulings (furu') that clarify the obligations and dispensations for those with chronic excuses in matters of purity and prayer. The commentator expands on the matn's statement that excused persons may pray obligatory and supererogatory prayers with one wudu, then addresses specific scenarios that a mufti may encounter.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
The excused person may pray both fard and nafl (including wajib) with one wudu as long as the excuse persists.
Note the linguistic clarification: 'nafl' here includes wajib.
2
Analyze the furu' on impurity containment
Review the rulings: 1) bandaging the wound is recommended; 2) washing the garment depends on benefit; 3) stopping the flow is obligatory if possible.
The mustahadah ruling is disputed.
3
Examine the prayer posture and congregation
If impurity flows during bending, one prays sitting with gestures (ima'). A person with flatulence cannot follow an imam with urinary incontinence because the imam has two excuses.
This prioritizes avoiding impurity over full prostration.
4
Understand the time condition
The excuse must cover the entire prayer time; if it covers only part, the person must make up the prayer if the excuse ceases completely in the next time.
This is derived from the discussion on eye inflammation.
5
Note the intra-madhhab differences
There are two views on the mustahadah who stuffs herself and on washing the garment; the text presents both without strong tarjih.
The chosen view from al-Nawazil is that washing is excused if it would cause immediate re-impurity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ويصلون به فرضاً ونفلاً) أي يصلي أرباب الأعذار بوضوئهم ما شاؤوا فرضاً كان أو واجباً أو نفلاً، فالمراد بالنفل ما زاد على الفرض فيشمل الواجب. فروع وينبغي لصاحب الجرح أن يربطه تقليلاً للنجاسة، ولو سال على ثوبه فعليه أن يغسله إذا كان مفيداً بأن لا يصيبه مرة أخرى، وإن كان يصيبه المرة بعد الأخرى أجزأه ولا يجب غسله ما دام العذر قائماً، وقيل لا يجب غسله أصلاً، واختار الأول السرخسي. والمختار ما في النوازل إن كان لو غسله تنجس ثانياً قبل الفراغ من الصلاة جاز أن لا يغسله وإلا فلا ومتى قدر المعذور على رد السيلان برباط أو حشو أو كان لو جلس لا يسيل ولو قام . سال وجب رده وخرج برده عن أن يكون صاحب عذر بخلاف الحائض إذا منعت الدرور فإنها حائض. واختلفوا في المستحاضة إذا احتشت ؛ قيل كصاحب العذر، وقيل كالحائض. كذا في السراج ويجب أن يصلي جالساً بإيماء إن سال بالميلان لأن ترك السجود أهون من الصلاة مع الحدث، ولا يجوز أن يصلي من به انفلات ريح خلف من به سلس البول لأن الإمام معه حدث ونجاسة فكان صاحب عذرين والمأموم صاحب عذر واحد. ولو كان في عينيه رمد يسيل دمعها يؤمر بالوضوء لكل وقت لاحتمال كونه صديداً. وفي حصة ... من الوقت فلا يكون حينئذ صاحب عذر لعدم استغراقه وقتاً كاملاً، وإنما حملناه على ذلك لقوله إنه يقضي هذه الصلاة لو خرج الوقت وانقطع العذر ودام إلى وقت صلاة أخرى وإلا لم يجب عليه القضاء لما سيأتي عن السراج قبيل النفاس فتأمل. ثم رأيت التصريح بذلك في شرح الوهبانية لابن الشحنة حيث قال : والمراد أن العذر حصل في بعض الوقت اهـ والله الحمد والمنة. قوله: (فالمراد بالنفل الخ) لم يعهد من أئمتنا الله إطلاق النفل على ما يعم الواجب، بل عهد منهم إطلاق الفرض على ما يعمه كقول المصنف في الوضوء وفرضه وكثيراً ما يطلقون الفرض على الواجب فالأصوب أن يقول : فالمراد بالفرض ما لزم فعله ليعم الواجب تأمل قوله: (وقيل كالحائض) جزم رحمهم الله
His statement: (And they pray with it obligatory and supererogatory) i.e., the people with excuses pray with their wudu whatever they wish, whether obligatory, mandatory, or supererogatory. What is meant by supererogatory is what is beyond obligatory, thus including mandatory. Branches: It is recommended for the person with a wound to bandage it to minimize impurity. If blood flows onto his garment, he must wash it if it is beneficial such that it will not be hit again. If it will be hit again after another, it suffices and washing is not obligatory as long as the excuse persists. It was said washing is not obligatory at all, and al-Sarakhsi chose the first. The chosen view is what is in al-Nawazil: if washing it would cause impurity a second time before finishing the prayer, it is permissible not to wash it; otherwise not. Whenever the excused person can stop the flow with a bandage or packing, or if he sits it does not flow and if he stands it flows, he must stop it, and by stopping he leaves the category of being excused, unlike the menstruating woman if she prevents the flow she is still menstruating. They differed regarding the mustahadah if she stuffs herself: it is said she is like an excused person, and it is said she is like a menstruating woman. Thus in al-Siraj. He must pray sitting with gesture if it flows when bowing, because leaving prostration is lighter than praying with impurity. And it is not permissible for a person with flatulence to pray behind a person with urinary incontinence, because the imam has both ritual impurity and physical impurity, being an owner of two excuses, while the follower has one excuse. And if one has an eye inflammation whose tears flow, he is ordered to perform wudu for every time because it might be pus. And in Hissa... of the time, then he is not an excused person because it does not cover the entire time. We interpreted it like that because of his statement that he makes up this prayer if the time exits and the excuse stops and continues to another prayer time; otherwise he does not have to make it up, as will come from al-Siraj before nifas. Then I saw explicit mention in Sharh al-Wahbaniyya by Ibn al-Shihna: 'What is meant is that the excuse occurred in part of the time.' And praise be to Allah. His statement: (What is meant by supererogatory...) It is not known from our imams, may Allah have mercy on them, that they used supererogatory to include mandatory; rather, they used obligatory to include it, like the author's statement in wudu: 'and its fard', and they often use fard for mandatory. So the more correct is to say: 'What is meant by fard is what is binding to do' to include mandatory. Consider. His statement: (And it was said like a menstruating woman) he firmly stated, may Allah have mercy on him.
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on the matn's statement that those with excuses can pray both fard and nafl with their wudu. The commentator clarifies that 'nafl' here includes wajib (necessary acts). Then he lists several branch rulings (furu'): (1) It is recommended to bandage the wound to reduce impurity. (2) If blood stains the garment, it must be washed if it helps, but if blood repeatedly touches it, washing is not obligatory while the excuse persists. The chosen view from al-Nawazil is that if washing would cause a new impurity before finishing prayer, it is excused. (3) If the person can stop the flow by sitting or packing, he must do so, and by doing so he ceases to be excused (unlike a menstruating woman who remains so). (4) Regarding a mustahadah who stuffs herself, there is ikhtilaf: some liken her to an excused person, others to a menstruating woman. (5) If the impurity flows when bowing, he must pray sitting with gestures, because avoiding impurity is prioritized over prostration. (6) A person with flatulence cannot pray behind someone with urinary incontinence because the imam has two excuses (impurity and filth) while the follower has one. (7) Eye inflammation with tearing: wudu for each time if the discharge is likely pus. (8) A discussion about whether the excuse must cover the entire time: it is concluded that if the excuse occurs in part of the time, he is still excused and must make up the prayer if it stops completely within the next time. The commentator ends with a linguistic note: 'nafl' in the matn actually means 'fard' in the sense of binding acts, not supererogatory, because Hanafi scholars often use 'fard' to include 'wajib'.

Key Terms
نفل (nafl): In this context, includes both supererogatory and obligatory (wajib) acts beyond fard.
إيماء (ima'): Gesture prayer (sitting and bowing by head movement) for those unable to perform full prostrations.
صاحب عذر (sahib 'udhr): A person with a chronic excuse that prevents complete purity, such as continuous bleeding or incontinence.
المستحاضة إذا احتشت (al-mustahada idha ihtashat): A woman with chronic non-menstrual bleeding who stuffs herself to stop the flow.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man with urinary incontinence prays 'Asr with one wudu. During the prayer, he feels urine dripping repeatedly. What is the ruling?
A) The prayer is invalid because the impurity is continuous.
B) The prayer is valid as long as he performed wudu at the beginning of the time and the excuse is continuous.
C) He must stop the prayer and renew wudu.
D) He must wash his garment immediately.

Key Takeaway
A person with a chronic excuse must take reasonable steps to contain impurity, but the prayer remains valid with one wudu until the excuse ceases or the time ends.

Ruling on Timing of Wuḍū for the Owner of Chronic Excuse
States the ruling for a person with continuous impurity regarding waiting until the end of prayer time.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a person with a chronic excuse regarding when to perform wudu and identify the conditions that trigger this ruling.

Core Idea
The owner of chronic excuse must wait until near the end of prayer time; if impurity continues, he performs wudu and prays.

This passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the timeline for purification for those suffering from a continuous impurity. It specifies that such a person should not perform wudu immediately but rather wait until the final portion of each obligatory prayer time. The ruling ensures that the prayer is performed within its proper time while accommodating the ongoing impurity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? It is the requirement for a person with a chronic excuse to perform wudu for each prayer time. The ruling is that it is obligatory (wajib) to wait until near the end of the time.
2
List the excuses that qualify a person as ṣāḥib al-ʿudhr
The passage mentions five types of continuous impurities: urine, incontinence of the bowels (istitlaq batn), flatulence, chronic nosebleed (ruʿāf dāʾim), and a wound that does not heal and continuously bleeds.
These are examples; any continuous impurity that persists through a complete prayer time qualifies.
3
Understand the timing rule
The person waits until the final moments of the prayer time. If the impurity continues without stopping, he performs wudu and prays before the time exits. If the impurity stops before the time ends, he performs wudu at that point and prays.
The waiting is not for the impurity to stop, but to minimize the time between wudu and prayer.
4
Analyze the scenario of impurity stopping in the next time
If after praying, the next prayer time enters and the impurity stops and remains stopped until another time, the person must perform wudu and repeat the previous prayer. However, if the impurity continues through the second time, the previous prayer remains valid without repetition.
This handles the case where the impurity temporarily ceases, indicating that the original prayer was performed without a valid excuse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بول أو استطلاق بطن أو انفلات ريح أو رعاف دائم أو جرح لا يرقا لوقت كل فرض سال من جرحه دم ينتظر آخر الوقت، إن لم ينقطع الدم توضأ وصلى قبل خروج الوقت، فإن توضأ وصلى ثم خرج الوقت ودخل وقت صلاة أخرى وانقطع الدم ودام الانقطاع إلى وقت صلاة أخرى توضأ وأعاد الصلاة وإن لم ينقطع في وقت الصلاة الثانية حتى خرج الوقت جازت الصلاة ا هـ
Urine, or incontinence of the bowels, or flatulence, or chronic nosebleed, or a wound that does not heal: for every obligatory prayer time, blood flows from his wound; he waits until the end of the time. If the blood does not stop, he performs wuḍū and prays before the exit of the time. If he performs wuḍū and prays, then the time exits and another prayer time enters, and the blood stops and the cessation continues until another prayer time, he performs wuḍū and repeats the prayer. But if it does not stop during the second prayer time until the time exits, the prayer is valid.
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This passage states the ruling for someone with a chronic excuse (ṣāḥib al-ʿudhr) such as urinary incontinence, chronic diarrhea, constant flatulence, persistent nosebleed, or a wound that does not stop bleeding. The rule is that such a person waits until near the end of each prayer time. If the flow does not stop, he performs wuḍū and prays before the time ends. If after that prayer time ends and a new time begins, and the blood stops and remains stopped until another prayer time, he must perform wuḍū and repeat the previous prayer. However, if the flow continues through the second time until it exits, the prayer is valid. This ruling is from the Hanafi school, specifically from the Bahr al-Rāʾiq commentary. No explicit proof is given here, but the reasoning is based on the principle that the owner of a chronic excuse is commanded to perform wuḍū for each time due to the ongoing impurity.

Key Terms
استطلاق بطن (istitlaq batn): Chronic incontinence of the bowels (diarrhea that cannot be controlled).
رعاف دائم (ruʿāf dāʾim): A nosebleed that continues persistently.
صاحب العذر (ṣāḥib al-ʿudhr): A person who has a continuous impurity that does not stop enough to perform a complete prayer with purity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a person with chronic nosebleed performs wudu and prays Dhuhr near the end of its time, and then the nosebleed stops after Dhuhr time ends and remains stopped until Asr time, he must:
A) Perform wudu and repeat Dhuhr prayer.
B) Not repeat Dhuhr prayer.
C) Perform wudu for Asr only.
D) Wait until the next day.

Key Takeaway
The owner of chronic excuse must wait until near the end of each prayer time; if the impurity continues, he performs wudu and prays; if it stops in the next time, he must repeat the previous prayer.

The Permanence of Wuḍū for the Owner of Chronic Excuse
Explains condition for validity of wuḍū of owner of chronic excuse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that the wuḍū of the owner of chronic excuse remains valid for the prayer time only if no new hadath occurs, and apply this rule to distinguish new hadath from continuation of the existing excuse.

Core Idea
Wuḍū of the owner of chronic excuse lasts the whole prayer time unless a new impurity event arises.

We have learned that the owner of chronic excuse (like a woman with istihāḍah or a person with continuous nosebleed) is exempt from repeating istinjā' for each prayer. The present passage from al-Badāʾiʿ explains a critical condition: this exemption depends on the absence of a new ḥadath. Understanding what counts as a 'new' event is essential to correctly applying the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Person
Recognize who is a ṣāḥib al-ʿudhr: someone with a continuous impurity that does not stop long enough to permit purification (e.g., mustaḥāḍah, chronic nosebleed).
The condition applies to all such persons regardless of the source of impurity.
2
Understand the Temporal Scope
The wuḍū is valid for the entire current prayer time, not indefinitely. If the excuse persists, wuḍū remains valid only until that time expires.
At the entry of the next prayer time, a fresh wuḍū is required (Hanafi view: wuḍū per time, not per prayer).
3
Apply the Condition
If a new ḥadath—one that was not present at the moment of wuḍū—occurs, the wuḍū breaks. The example: blood from a different nostril after wuḍū is a new event.
The test: was this source of impurity already active at the time of wuḍū? If yes, it is not new.
4
Distinguish New from Ongoing
If both sources were bleeding at wuḍū time, and then one stops, the wuḍū remains valid because the ongoing impurity was already accounted for. Only a new source breaks it.
Stopping of one source does not count as a new ḥadath.
5
Practical Consequence
If a new ḥadath occurs, the person must renew wuḍū before continuing to pray. If no new ḥadath, the original wuḍū suffices.
This ruling is specific to the Hanafi school; other schools may have different conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقيد بالوضوء لأنه لا يجب عليها الاستنجاء لوقت كل صلاة. كذا في الظهيرية أيضاً. وفي البدائع : وإنما تبقى طهارة صاحب العذر في الوقت إذا لم يحدث حدثاً آخر، أما إذا أحدث حدثاً آخر فلا تبقى كما إذا سال الدم من فتوضأ ثم سال من المنخر الآخر فعليه الوضوء لأن هذا حدث جديد لم يكن موجوداً وقت الطهارة، فأما إذا سال منهما جميعاً فتوضأ ثم انقطع أحدهما فهو على وضوئه ما بقي الوقت اهـ
He restricted it to wuḍū because istinjā' is not obligatory for every prayer time. Likewise in al-Ẓahīriyya. And in al-Badāʾiʿ: The purity of the owner of chronic excuse remains in the time only if he does not perform another hadath. But if he performs another hadath, it does not remain; for example, if blood flowed from (one nostril) and he performed wuḍū, then blood flowed from the other nostril, then he must perform wuḍū because this is a new hadath that did not exist at the time of purification. However, if it flowed from both together and he performed wuḍū, then one of them stopped, he remains on his wuḍū as long as the time remains.
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This passage clarifies that the owner of chronic excuse is not required to perform istinjā' (washing the private parts) for each prayer time; rather, wuḍū suffices. Then it quotes from al-Badāʾiʿ (al-Badāʾiʿ al-Ṣanāʾiʿ by al-Kāsānī) explaining the ruling about the permanence of wuḍū. The key principle: the wuḍū of the owner of chronic excuse remains valid throughout the prayer time if no new hadath (impurity event) occurs. If a new hadath happens—like blood flowing from a different nostril after wuḍū—that breaks the wuḍū because it is a new event not present at the time of purification. But if both nostrils were bleeding at the time of wuḍū, and then one stops, the wuḍū remains valid because the ongoing impurity was already accounted for. This shows that the wuḍū is not perpetual; it is tied to the condition that no new hadath arises.

Key Terms
الاستنجاء (istinjāʾ): Washing the private parts after relieving oneself.
الحدث (al-ḥadath): An event that nullifies wuḍū, such as the emission of blood, urine, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage from al-Badāʾiʿ, when does the wuḍū of the owner of chronic excuse remain valid?
A) as long as the chronic excuse continues
B) for the entire prayer time, provided no new ḥadath occurs
C) indefinitely, regardless of new ḥadath
D) only if istinjā' is performed

Key Takeaway
The wuḍū of a person with chronic excuse remains valid for the prayer time only if no new ḥadath (impurity event) occurs; a new source of impurity breaks the wuḍū.

Scope of 'Nafl' for the Chronically Excused
Commentary clarifying that 'nafl' includes wājib for the ma'dhur

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi definition of 'nafl' in the context of the ma'dhur and identify which types of prayers are valid with a single wuḍū.

Core Idea
For the ma'dhur, 'nafl' includes wājib – all prayers beyond farḍ are allowed with one wuḍū.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Rā’iq unpacks a phrase from Kanz al-Daqā’iq: 'they pray with it obligatory and supererogatory.' The commentator clarifies that for a person with a chronic excuse (ṣāḥib al-‘udhr), the term 'supererogatory' (nafl) is used broadly to include wājib (necessary) prayers. Understanding this terminology is key to knowing the extent of concession granted to the ma’dhūr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the special category
The passage discusses the act of praying after performing wuḍū while in a state of continuous excuse (e.g., incontinence). The ma’dhūr is allowed to pray multiple prayers with one wuḍū within a prayer time.
2
Locate the key phrase and its commentary
The matn says 'ويصلون به فرضاً ونفلاً' (they pray with it obligatory and supererogatory). The commentator expands the meaning of 'نفلاً' to include wājib.
In Hanafi fiqh, wājib is a distinct category between farḍ and sunnah.
3
Define the Hanafi categories: farḍ, wājib, nafl
Farḍ is obligatory with qaṭ‘ī proof, wājib is necessary with ẓannī proof, and nafl is supererogatory. In normal circumstances, these are distinct. However, here 'nafl' is used in a broader sense.
The commentator explicitly states: 'فالمراد بالنفل ما زاد على الفرض فيشمل الواجب'
4
Understand the expansion: why nafl includes wājib here
Because the concession is about the validity of the wuḍū, not the classification of the prayer. The wuḍū suffices for all prayers – whether farḍ, wājib, or nafl – as long as it remains intact.
This shows that the term 'nafl' can be contextually extended. The ruling is not unique to nafl; it covers all prayers.
5
Apply to a scenario
A person with continuous urine leakage makes wuḍū for Ẓuhr. He can pray farḍ, the sunnah before/after, and any nafl prayers he wishes. If he made wuḍū for a nafl, he can also pray farḍ with that wuḍū.
This is based on the general permission in the ḥadīth: 'Let him perform wuḍū for each prayer' – meaning each time, but within that time, multiple prayers are valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ويصلون به فرضاً ونفلاً) أي يصلي أرباب الأعذار بوضوئهم ما شاؤوا فرضاً كان أو واجباً أو نفلاً، فالمراد بالنفل ما زاد على الفرض فيشمل الواجب.
His saying: 'And they pray with it obligatory and supererogatory' means that the owners of excuses pray with their wuḍū as much as they wish, whether it be obligatory, or necessary (wājib), or supererogatory. The intent by 'supererogatory' is what is in addition to the obligatory, so it includes the wājib.
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This is a brief commentary on the author's phrase 'they pray with it obligatory and supererogatory' from the matn. The commentator clarifies that the owners of chronic excuses can pray any number of prayers with the wuḍū made for each time, whether those prayers are farḍ (obligatory), wājib (necessary), or nafl (supererogatory). The term nafl here is used broadly to include all prayers beyond the farḍ, including wājib. In Hanafi terminology, wājib is a separate category between farḍ and sunnah, but here it is included under nafl for convenience. This indicates that the wuḍū suffices for all worship as long as it remains valid within the time.

Key Terms
النفل (al-nafl): Supererogatory prayer, but here used broadly to include wājib (necessary) in addition to optional.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does 'نفل' in the phrase 'يصلون به فرضاً ونفلاً' include according to this commentary?
A) Only supererogatory prayers.
B) Only necessary (wājib) prayers.
C) Both supererogatory and necessary prayers.
D) All prayers including farḍ.

Key Takeaway
For a person with a chronic excuse, the term 'nafl' in the matn includes wājib, meaning all prayers are valid with one wuḍū within the same prayer time.

8 min
Branches on Rulings for an Owner of Chronic Excuse
Lists subsidiary rulings for chronic excuse owner

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state and apply the key rulings for an owner of chronic excuse, including when to wash clothing, when it is obligatory to stop the flow, and how the mustaḥāḍah differs from the ḥāʾiḍ.

Core Idea
An owner of chronic excuse must actively minimize impurity; if flow can be prevented, he must and reverts to normal rulings.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Rāʾiq lists subsidiary rulings (furūʿ) clarifying how an ṣāḥib al-ʿudhr should manage impurity during prayer. It covers bandaging wounds, washing garments that become impure, stopping the flow by sitting or packing, the difference between a menstruating woman and one with istihāḍah, and more. By working through these branches, you will understand the legal obligations (wājib) and concessions (rukhaṣ) for chronically excused persons.

Guided Path
1
Bandaging the wound and washing the garment
First, the text recommends bandaging to minimize impurity. Then it addresses blood on the garment: if washing is useful (i.e., it will not immediately become impure again), washing is obligatory; if it will immediately become re-impure, it suffices not to wash. Al-Sarakhsī preferred the first view, and the chosen view from al-Nawāzil adds that if washing would cause re-impurification before prayer ends, one may abstain.
Note the conditional obligation: the benefit of washing must be real.
2
Stopping the flow
If the person can stop the discharge by bandage, packing, or sitting down (if flow only occurs when standing), it becomes obligatory to do so. By stopping the flow, the person ceases to be an owner of excuse and must perform prayer with full purity. The menstruating woman is an exception: even if she stops the flow, she remains ḥāʾiḍ and cannot pray.
This shows that the excuse status is contingent on inability to prevent impurity.
3
Dispute on the mustaḥāḍah
There is a disagreement on whether a mustaḥāḍah (woman with chronic non-menstrual bleeding) who packs herself becomes like an owner of excuse or like a menstruating woman. The text records both views without choosing one, indicating a legitimate ikhtilāf.
The practical difference: if treated like owner of excuse, she must pray with wuḍū for each time; if like ḥāʾiḍ, she cannot pray at all.
4
Praying with gesture and following an imam
If bending (for rukūʿ/sajdah) causes the impurity to flow, the person must pray sitting with gesture (īmāʾ) because leaving sajdah is easier than praying with impurity. Also, a person with flatulence cannot follow an imam with urinary incontinence because the imam has two types of impurity (ḥadath and najāsa) while the follower has only one, making the follower's excuse less severe.
These rulings protect the dignity of prayer and prioritize minimizing impurity over posture.
5
Partial-time excuse
A person whose excuse only occurs for part of the prayer time is not considered a full owner of excuse. If the excuse ends after the time, he must make up the prayer; if it ends within the time, he must purify and pray. This is inferred from the requirement of qaḍāʾ when the excuse ceases after time exits.
The excuse must encompass the entire prayer time to qualify for the special rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فروع وينبغي لصاحب الجرح أن يربطه تقليلاً للنجاسة، ولو سال على ثوبه فعليه أن يغسله إذا كان مفيداً بأن لا يصيبه مرة أخرى، وإن كان يصيبه المرة بعد الأخرى أجزأه ولا يجب غسله ما دام العذر قائماً، وقيل لا يجب غسله أصلاً، واختار الأول السرخسي. والمختار ما في النوازل إن كان لو غسله تنجس ثانياً قبل الفراغ من الصلاة جاز أن لا يغسله وإلا فلا ومتى قدر المعذور على رد السيلان برباط أو حشو أو كان لو جلس لا يسيل ولو قام سال وجب رده وخرج برده عن أن يكون صاحب عذر بخلاف الحائض إذا منعت الدرور فإنها حائض. واختلفوا في المستحاضة إذا احتشت ؛ قيل كصاحب العذر، وقيل كالحائض. كذا في السراج ويجب أن يصلي جالساً بإيماء إن سال بالميلان لأن ترك السجود أهون من الصلاة مع الحدث، ولا يجوز أن يصلي من به انفلات ريح خلف من به سلس البول لأن الإمام معه حدث ونجاسة فكان صاحب عذرين والمأموم صاحب عذر واحد. ولو كان في عينيه رمد يسيل دمعها يؤمر بالوضوء لكل وقت لاحتمال كونه صديداً. وفي حصة من الوقت فلا يكون حينئذ صاحب عذر لعدم استغراقه وقتاً كاملاً، وإنما حملناه على ذلك لقوله إنه يقضي هذه الصلاة لو خرج الوقت وانقطع العذر ودام إلى وقت صلاة أخرى وإلا لم يجب عليه القضاء لما سيأتي عن السراج قبيل النفاس فتأمل. ثم رأيت التصريح بذلك في شرح الوهبانية لابن الشحنة حيث قال : والمراد أن العذر حصل في بعض الوقت اهـ والله الحمد والمنة.
Branches: It is recommended for the owner of a wound to bandage it to reduce impurity. If blood flows onto his garment, he must wash it if doing so is beneficial insofar as it will not be struck again. But if it gets struck time after time, it suffices him, and he is not obligated to wash it as long as the excuse persists. It is said that he is not obligated to wash it at all, and al-Sarakhsī chose the first opinion. The chosen view is what is in al-Nawāzil: if washing it would cause it to become impure a second time before completing the prayer, he may not wash it; otherwise he must. And whenever the excused person is able to stop the flow by a bandage or packing, or if when he sits it does not flow and when he stands it flows, then it becomes obligatory to stop it, and by stopping it he ceases to be an owner of excuse, contrary to the menstruating woman who, even if she prevents the flow, remains a ḥāʾiḍ. And they differed regarding the mustaḥāḍah if she packs herself; it is said like the owner of excuse, and it is said like the ḥāʾiḍ. So in al-Sirāj. And it is obligatory for him to pray sitting with gesture if the flow comes due to bending, because leaving sajdah is easier than praying with impurity. And it is not permissible for a person who has flatulence to pray behind one who has urinary incontinence, because the imam has ḥadath and impurity, so he is an owner of two excuses, while the follower has one excuse. And if one has an eye infection (ramad) whose tears flow, he is commanded to perform wuḍū for every prayer time due to the possibility that it is pus. And regarding a portion of the time, he is not then an owner of excuse because he does not fill a complete time. We only infer that from his statement that he must make up this prayer if the time exits and the excuse ceases and continues to another prayer time; otherwise, he would not be obligated to make it up according to what will come from al-Sirāj near the section on nifās; so reflect. Then I saw the explicit statement of that in Sharḥ al-Wahbāniyya by Ibn al-Shiḥna, where he said: The intent is that the excuse occurred in part of the time. End. And to Allah is praise and gratitude.
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This extensive set of branches provides details about the rulings for the owner of chronic excuse. First, it is recommended (mustaḥabb) to bandage the wound to minimize impurity. Regarding blood on the garment: if washing it is useful, i.e., it will not get immediately dirty again, then washing is obligatory; if it will get dirty again immediately, it is not obligatory; there are different views, with al-Sarakhsī preferring the first. The chosen view is from al-Nawāzil, considering if washing would cause impurification again before prayer finishes. Second, if the person can stop the flow by tying or packing, it becomes obligatory to do so, and by stopping, the person becomes like a healthy person, no longer excused. The menstruating woman is different: she remains in menstruation despite stopping the flow. For the mustaḥāḍah (woman with chronic non-menstrual bleeding), the scholars differ: some compare her to the owner of excuse, others to the ḥāʾiḍ. Third, if the impurity flows due to bending, the person must pray sitting with gesture (īmāʾ) because leaving prostration is easier than praying with impurity. Fourth, a person with flatulence cannot follow an imam with urinary incontinence because the imam has two impurities (ḥadath and najāsa) while the follower has one. Fifth, a person with eye discharge (ramad) must perform wuḍū for each time because the discharge might be impure (puṣ). Sixth, a person whose excuse occurs only for part of the time is not considered a full owner of excuse, as indicated by the need for qaḍā' if the excuse ceases after time exits.

Key Terms
صاحب العذر (ṣāḥib al-ʿudhr): A person who has a continuous impurity that does not stop enough to perform a complete prayer with purity.
المستحاضة (al-mustaḥāḍah): A woman who experiences bleeding that is not menstrual (istihāḍah) and is considered a type of chronic excuse.
الحائض (al-ḥāʾiḍ): A woman in her menstrual period; prayer is prohibited and purity not required.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He is still an owner of excuse.
B) He must sit to pray and is not obliged to stop the flow.
C) He must stop the flow by sitting or bandaging, and if he can, he becomes like a healthy person.
D) He must pray standing regardless.

Key Takeaway
The owner of chronic excuse must actively minimize impurity and is only excused as long as prevention is impossible; if the flow can be stopped, it is obligatory to do so and the excuse is lifted.

8 min
Nullification of Wuḍū for the Owner of Chronic Excuse
Ruling with proof: nullification conditions for chronic excuse holders

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two factors that nullify the wuḍū of a mustaḥāḍah and apply the Hanafi rule that both must concur.

Core Idea
The wuḍū of a chronic excuse holder breaks only when time exits AND a new flow occurs.

This lesson unpacks a key Hanafi ruling on chronic excuses (udhr). You might wonder: does a mustaḥāḍah’s wuḍū break simply because a new prayer time starts? The text clarifies that nullification requires two conditions together — exit of time and a new flow. Understanding this composite cause prevents misapplication in prayer and purity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The passage states that wuḍū is nullified 'only by its exit' (i.e., exit of time). The owner of a chronic excuse (mustaḥāḍah, etc.) must perform wuḍū for each prayer time, and it remains valid until the time exits.
The phrase 'yabṭulu bi-khurūjihī faqaṭ' is explained metaphorically — the actual nullifier is the hadath that appears at that moment.
2
Extract the two components of nullification
From Sarakhsī's Jāmiʿ al-Kabīr, the nullifiers are: (1) flow of blood, (2) exit of time. Neither alone suffices; both must coexist.
"الحكم المتعلق بعلة ذات وصفين تنعدم بانعدام أحد الوصفين" — the ruling depends on a cause with two attributes.
3
Examine the counterexample: building (bināʾ)
If a mustaḥāḍah’s wuḍū breaks during prayer, she can renew wuḍū and build (continue) the prayer because her purity was broken by a hadath, not by time exit itself.
This shows that time exit alone is not a hadath — it is merely the moment the underlying impurity is deemed to have been present.
4
Distinguish the owner of excuse from healthy person
The text contrasts with a person who can stop the flow by binding or treatment — such a person is not a ma‘dhūr, and his wuḍū breaks with any outflow. Also, the muftaṣad (cupped) is not a ma‘dhūr because the bleeding is controllable.
This distinction clarifies who qualifies as a chronic excuse holder.
5
Resolve the dispute: wājib vs. mustaḥabb
Some (from Fatḥ al-Qadīr) said the command to perform wuḍū each time is recommended because of doubt. The relied-upon view (as in Sirāj al-Wahhāj) is that it is wājib, because the person is an owner of excuse, and doubt does not remove certainty.
The practical difference: missing a recommended act is not sinful, but missing a wājib is.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويصلون به فرضاً ونفلاً ويبطل بخروجه فقط وهذا إذا لم يمض عليهم وقت فرض إلا فتح القدير : وأقول هذا التعليل يقتضي أنه أمر استحباب فأن الشك والاحتمال في كونه ناقضاً لا يوجب الحكم بالنقض إذ اليقين لا يزول بالشك، نعم إذا علم من طريق غلبة الظن بإخبار الأطباء أو علامات تغلب على ظن المبتلي يجب اهـ . وهو حسن لكن صرح في السراج الوهاج بأنه صاحب عذر فكان الأمر للإيجاب . قوله : ( ويبطل بخروجه فقط أي ولا يبطل بدخوله ومراده يظهر الحدث السابق عند خروجه فإضافة البطلان إلى الخروج مجاز لأنه لا تأثير للخروج في الانتقاض حقيقة، ولهذا لا يجوز لهم المسح على الخفين بعد الوقت إذا كان العذر موجوداً وقت الوضوء، أو اللبس ولا البناء إذا خرج الوقت وهم في الصلاة وظهور الحدث السابق عنده إنما هو مقتصر من كل وجه على التحقيق لا أنه مستند إلى أول الوقت، ولهذا لو شرع صاحب العذر في التطوع ثم خرج الوقت لزمه القضاء، ولو كان ظهوره مستنداً لم يلزمه لأن المراد بظهوره أن ذلك الحدث محكوم بارتفاعه إلى غاية معلومة فيظهر عندها مقتصراً لا أن يظهر قيامه شرعاً من ذلك في البزازية بالأول وعبارته : إذا قدرت المستحاضة أو ذو الجرح أو المفتصد على منع دم بربط وعن منع النش بخرقة الربط لزم وكان كالأصحا ، فإن لم يقدر على منع النش فهو ذو عذر بخلاف الحائض حيث لا تخرج بالربط عن كونها حائضاً ا هـ . وهو ظاهر كلام المنية حيث قال صاحب العذر إذا منع الدم عن الخروج بعلاج يخرج من أن يكون صاحب عذر، ولهذا المعنى المفتصد لا يكون صاحب عذر بخلاف الحائض إذا احتشت لا تخرج من أن تكون حائضاً .اهـ. وفي قوله «ولهذا المعنى المفتصد الخ» شاهد لما قدمناه في نواقض الوضوء عن الشرنبلالي من أن صاحب كي الحمصة لا يكون صاحب عذر بل ينظر إلى ذلك الخارج إن كان فيه قوة السيلان بنفسه يكون نجساً ناقضاً للوضوء ويلزمه غسله، ولا تجوز الصلاة حالة سيلانه ولو استوعب وقتاً كاملاً وإلا فلا ينقض بل هو طاهر ولو أصاب مائعاً خلافاً لمحمد قوله : (ثم إنما يبطل بخروجه الخ) هذا يفيد أن المبطل ليس مجرد خروج الوقت بل هو مع السيلان ويوافقه ما في الجامع الكبير لشمس الأئمة السرخسي : إذا توضأت المستحاضة في وقت العصر والدم منقطع وصلت ركعتين ثم دخل وقت المغرب ثم سال الدم فعليها أن تتوضأ وتبني على صلاتها لأن انتقاض الطهارة كان بالحدث لا بخروج الوقت ولم يوجد منها أداء شيء من الصلاة بعد الحدث فجاز لها أن تبني وهذا لأن خروج الوقت عينه ليس بحدث ولكن الطهارة تنتقض عند خروج الوقت بسيلان مقارن للطهارة، أو موجود بعده ولم يوجد فلا تنتقض بخروج الوقت ثم قال : وحاصل هذا الكلام أن الناقض لطهارة المستحاضة شيئان : سيلان الدم وخروج الوقت. ثم لو تجرد سيلان الدم عن خروج الوقت لم يكن ناقضاً، وكذلك إذا تجرد خروج الوقت عن سيلان الدم لأن الحكم المتعلق بعلة ذات وصفين تنعدم بانعدام أحد الوصفين اهـ. كذا في النهاية ومعراج الدراية. وبهذا يظهر لك ما في كلام الشيخ علاء الدين الحصكفي حيث
And they pray with it obligatory and supererogatory, and it is nullified only by its exit. This is if no obligatory time has passed over them except... Fath al-Qadīr says: I say this reasoning indicates that it is an recommended matter, since doubt and probability that it is nullifying does not require the ruling of nullification because certainty is not removed by doubt. However, if it is known via preponderant opinion through medical reports or signs that overcome the afflicted's suspicion, then it becomes obligatory. That is good, but the Sirāj al-Wahhāj explicitly stated that he is an owner of excuse, so the command is for obligation. His saying: 'And it is nullified only by its exit' means it is not nullified by its entry, and his intent is that the previous hadath appears upon its exit, so attributing nullification to exit is metaphorical because exit has no actual effect on the nullification. For this reason, they are not allowed to wipe over leather socks after the time if the excuse existed at the time of wuḍū or wearing, nor to build upon it if time exits while they are in prayer. The appearance of the previous hadath at that point is limited, not traced back to the beginning of the time. Hence if an owner of excuse begins a supererogatory prayer and then time exits, he must make it up; if the appearance were traced back, he would not need to. In al-Bazzāziyya, the first view: if the mustaḥāḍah or the owner of a wound or the one bled can prevent blood by tying and prevent the flow by a cloth wrap, then he must do so and becomes like a healthy person. But if he cannot prevent the flow, he is an owner of excuse, contrary to the ḥāʾiḍ. This is apparent from the statement of al-Munyat: The owner of excuse, if he prevents blood from exiting by treatment, he exits from being an owner of excuse; for this meaning, the one bled (muftaṣad) is not an owner of excuse, contrary to the ḥāʾiḍ if she packs herself. And his saying 'and for this meaning the muftaṣad' is evidence for what we have earlier in the nullifiers of wuḍū from al-Shurnbulālī, that the owner of burning a pimple is not an owner of excuse; rather, that which exits is looked at: if it has the strength of flowing by itself, it is impure and nullifies wuḍū, and washing it is obligatory; prayer is not allowed while it is flowing even if it fills a complete time; otherwise it does not nullify and is pure even if it hits a liquid, contrary to Muhammad. His saying: 'Then it is only nullified by its exit' means that the nullifier is not merely the exit of time but the flow concurrent with it. This is supported by what is in al-Jāmiʿ al-Kabīr of Shams al-Aʾimma al-Sarakhsī: If the mustaḥāḍah performed wuḍū in the time of ʿaṣr, her blood ceasing, and prayed two rakʿahs, then time of maghrib entered, then blood flowed, she must perform wuḍū and build upon her prayer because the nullification of purity was by the hadath, not by the exit of time. This is because the exit of time itself is not a hadath, but purity is nullified at the exit of time by a flow concurrent with the purity or existing after it. If neither exists, it is not nullified. He then said: The summary is that the nullifier of the mustaḥāḍah's purity are two things: the flow of blood and the exit of time. Then if the flow of blood is isolated from the exit of time, it is not a nullifier, and likewise if the exit of time is isolated from the flow of blood, because the ruling attached to a cause with two attributes ceases with the non-existence of either attribute. This is in al-Nihāyah and Miʿrāj al-Dirāya. And by this, you see the error in the statement of Sheikh ʿAlāʾ al-Dīn al-Ḥaṣkafī where...
Source pages p. 375

Commentary
This passage deals with the important principle that the wuḍū of the owner of chronic excuse is nullified only by the exit of the prayer time if combined with a new flow. First, the author quotes from Fatḥ al-Qadīr a discussion: some say the command to perform wuḍū for each time is recommended (istihbāb) because doubt about breaking does not remove certainty. But the correct view is that it is obligatory, as stated in al-Sirāj al-Wahhāj. Then the commentary explains the phrase 'it is nullified only by its exit' (yabṭulu bi-khurūjihī faqaṭ). This means the wuḍū does not break upon entering the new time, but only when the time exits, because the underlying impurity (ḥadath sābiq) becomes manifest at that moment. This is metaphorical; the actual nullification is due to the continuity of the impurity throughout the time, not the exit itself. Evidence for this is that if an owner of excuse begins a voluntary prayer and then time exits, he must make it up, indicating that the purity was still valid. The passage then includes a lengthy quote from al-Bazzāziyya repeating the ruling about stopping the flow, and a crucial quote from al-Jāmiʿ al-Kabīr of Imam Sarakhsī: the purity of the mustaḥāḍah is nullified by two factors: the flow of blood and the exit of time. Neither alone nullifies; both must exist together. This is a key distinction. For example, if she performs wuḍū while her blood is stopping, and then time exits without a new flow, her wuḍū remains valid. But if blood flows before time exits, it nullifies. If blood flows after time exits, it nullifies as well. But the exact timing matters. The text then critiques al-Ḥaṣkafī's view. This lesson shows the depth of Hanafi reasoning in defining the precise conditions for contract annulment.

Key Terms
المستحاضة (al-mustaḥāḍah): A woman who experiences bleeding that is not menstrual (istihāḍah) and is considered a type of chronic excuse.
البناء (al-bināʾ): Continuing a prayer from where one stopped after a valid act, without repeating the entire prayer.
المفتصد (al-muftaṣad): A person who has been cupped or has a bleeding wound from intentional bloodletting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Sarakhsī, what nullifies the purity of a mustaḥāḍah?
A) Only the flow of blood.
B) Only the exit of time.
C) Both the flow of blood and the exit of time.
D) Either the flow of blood or the exit of time.

Key Takeaway
The wuḍū of a chronic excuse holder breaks only when both the exit of the prayer time and a new flow occur together; neither alone suffices.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Nullification of Wudu for the Excused Person
Explains nullification timing and intra-madhhab dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the relied-upon Hanafi ruling on when the wudu of a mustahadah becomes invalid and explain the difference between the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Zufar.

Core Idea
The excused person's wudu is nullified only at the exit of the prayer time, not at its entry, and only when bleeding occurs.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a key question for those with chronic excuses: when does their wudu break? Understanding this ruling is critical for maintaining valid prayer. We will explore the Hanafi position and why it differs from earlier scholars within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Locate the main statement in the passage regarding the nullification of wudu for the mustahadah: it becomes invalid only by the exit of the prayer time, not the entry.
2
Understand the Reasoning
Analyze why the author says attributing invalidation to exit is metaphorical, and that the real nullifier is the combination of flow and exit of time, not either alone.
Refer to the citation from al-Jami' al-Kabir by al-Sarakhsi.
3
Examine the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Compare the three views: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (exit only), Abu Yusuf (entry or exit), and Zufar (entry only). Note their proofs.
The text labels the exit-only view as 'al-sahih' (sound).
4
Identify the Mufta Bihi
Determine which position is relied upon for fatwa: the exit-only view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.
This is supported by the majority of Hanafi works.
5
Apply to a Scenario
Given a mustahadah who performs wudu at the beginning of Zuhr, state when her wudu becomes invalid according to each of the three views, and what the mufta bihi is.
For the mufta bihi, it remains valid until the exit of Zuhr time, provided flow occurs at that time.

كتاب الطهارة - باب الحيض ويصلون به فرضاً ونفلاً ويبطل بخروجه فقط وهذا إذا لم يمض عليهم وقت فرض إلا فتح القدير : وأقول هذا التعليل يقتضي أنه أمر استحباب فإن الشك والاحتمال في كونه ناقضاً لا يوجب الحكم الصحيح فلا تنتقض إلا بخروج وقت الظهر لا بدخوله خلافاً لأبي يوسف وأنه لو توضأ قبل الطلوع انتقض بالطلوع اتفاقاً خلافاً لزفر، وأنه لو توضأ في وقت الظهر للعصر بطل بخروج وقت الظهر على الصحيح. فالحاصل أنه ينتقض بالخروج لا بالدخول عندهما، وعند أبي يوسف بأيهما وجد، وعند زفر بالدخول فقط. قوله : (وهذا إذا لم يمض عليهم وقت فرض إلا وذلك الحدث يوجد فيه) أي وحكم الاستحاضة والعذر يبقى إذا لم يمض على أصحابهما وقت صلاة إلا والحدث الذي ابتليت به يوجد فيه ولو قليلاً حتى لو انقطع وقتاً كاملاً خرج عن كونه عذراً. قيدنا بكونه شرط البقاء لأن شرط ثبوته ابتداء بأن يستوعب وقتاً كاملاً. كذا في أكثر الكتب. وفي النهاية كل الوقت لا تكون مستحاضة، وظاهره أنه لو انقطع في الوقت زمناً يسيراً لا تكون مستحاضة. وفي الكافي ما يخالفه فإنه قال : إنما يصير صاحب عذر إذا لم يجد في وقت صلاة زماناً يتوضأ فيه خالياً عن الحدث. وفي التبيين أن الأظهر خلاف ما في الكافي. وفي فتح القدير أن ما في الكافي يصلح تفسيراً لما في غيره إذ قل ما يستمر كمال وقت بحيث لا ينقطع لحظة فيؤدّي إلى نفي تحققه إلا في الإمكان بخلاف جانب الصحة منه فإنه يدوم انقطاعه وقتاً كاملاً وهو مما يتحقق اهـ. وفي شرح الدرر والغرر لمنلاخسرو : لا مخالفة بين ما في عامة الكتب وما ذكره في الكافي بدليل أن شراح الجامع الخلاطي قالوا في شرح قوله لأن زوال العذر يثبت باستيعاب الوقت كالثبوت أن الانقطاع الكامل معتبر في إبطال رخصة المعذور والقصر غير معتبر إجماعاً فاحتيج إلى حد فاصل، فقدرنا بوقت الصلاة كما قدرنا به ثبوت العذر ابتداء فإنه يشترط لثبوته ابتداء دوام
