Book of Purity - Chapter of Menstruation. And they pray with it obligatory and supererogatory, and it becomes invalid only by its exit, and this is when no obligatory time has passed upon them except that the [hadath] exists in it. Fath al-Qadir: I say this reasoning implies it is a recommended matter, because doubt and possibility of its being nullifying does not necessitate ruling of nullification, since certainty is not removed by doubt. Yes, if it is known by way of predominant probability from doctors' reports or signs that overcome the afflicted person's assumption, then it is obligatory. It is good, but it is stated in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj that he is a person of excuse, so the command is for obligation. His statement: (And it becomes invalid only by its exit) i.e., it does not become invalid by its entry, and his intent is that the previous hadath appears at its exit, so attributing invalidation to exit is metaphorical because the exit has no actual effect on nullification. Therefore, they are not allowed to wipe over socks after the time if the excuse existed at the time of wudu or wearing, nor to build if the time exits while they are in prayer. The appearance of the previous hadath at that point is restricted entirely to actualization, not that it is attributed to the beginning of the time. Hence, if an excused person begins a supererogatory prayer then the time exits, he must make it up; if its appearance were attributed, he would not have to. Because what is meant by its appearance is that that hadath is ruled to be raised until a known limit, so it appears at that time restricted, not that its legal existence appears from that. In al-Bazzaziyya: 'If a mustahadah or a wounded person or one who is cupped is able to prevent blood by bandaging and to prevent dampness by a cloth tied, then it is necessary and he is like a healthy person. If he cannot prevent the dampness, then he is a person of excuse, unlike a menstruating woman who does not exit from being menstruating by tying.' The apparent statement of al-Minya: 'The person of excuse, if he prevents the blood from exiting by treatment, exits from being a person of excuse, and for this meaning the one who is cupped is not a person of excuse, unlike a menstruating woman who, if she stuffs herself, does not exit from being menstruating.' In his words 'and for this meaning the one who is cupped etc.' is evidence for what we presented in nullifiers of wudu from al-Shurunbulali: that the person who cauterizes a wart is not a person of excuse, but rather one looks at that exiting substance: if it has the power to flow by itself, it is impure, nullifying wudu, and washing it is obligatory, and prayer is not permissible while it flows even if it occupies a complete time; otherwise it does not nullify and is pure even if it hits a liquid, contrary to Muhammad. His statement: (Then it only invalidates by its exit, etc.) This indicates that the invalidator is not merely the exit of time but rather with the flow. And it is supported by what is in al-Jami al-Kabir by Shams al-Aimma al-Sarakhsi: 'If a mustahadah performs wudu in the time of Asr while the blood is stopped and prays two rakats, then the time of Maghrib enters, then blood flows, she must perform wudu and build upon her prayer because the nullification of purity was due to the hadath not due to exit of time, and she did not perform any part of the prayer after the hadath, so it is permissible for her to build. And this is because the exit of time itself is not a hadath, but purity is nullified at the exit of time by a flow concomitant with purity or existing after it, and if it does not exist then it is not nullified by exit of time.' Then he said: 'The summary of this speech is that the nullifier of the mustahadah's purity are two things: the flow of blood and the exit of time. Then if the flow of blood is isolated from exit of time, it is not a nullifier, and likewise if the exit of time is isolated from blood flow, because the ruling attached to a cause with two attributes is absent by the absence of one of the attributes.' Similarly in al-Nihaya and Mirqat al-Diraya. And with this the statement of Sheikh Ala al-Din al-Haskafi becomes clear. ... Then it only invalidates by its exit if they perform wudu while there is flow, or flow occurs after wudu. However, if it is while it is stopped and it continues until the exit of time, then it does not invalidate by the exit as long as no other hadath occurs or her blood does not flow. And it informs that if one performs wudu after sunrise even for Eid or Duha, according to the sound view it is not nullified except by the exit of Zuhr time, not by its entry, unlike Abu Yusuf; and that if he performs wudu before sunrise, it is nullified by sunrise by agreement, unlike Zufar; and that if he performs wudu in Zuhr time for Asr, it becomes invalid by the exit of Zuhr time according to the sound view. The conclusion is that it is nullified by exit, not by entry, according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad); according to Abu Yusuf, by whichever occurs; according to Zufar, by entry only. His statement: (And this is when no obligatory time has passed upon them except that the hadath exists in it) i.e., the ruling of istihadah and excuse remains only if no prayer time passes upon its people without the hadath that they suffer from existing in it, even if little. So if it stops for a complete time, they exit from being excused. We restricted it to being a condition of continuity because the condition for its initial establishment is that it occupies a complete time. As in most books. In al-Nihaya, it is a condition initially that the flow continues from beginning to end of the time, analogously to istihada, for it is not complete unless it stops for the entire time. In the commentary of Shaykh Hamid al-Din al-Darrir, the condition initially is that the hadath be the entire time, even if it does not occupy the whole time, she is not a mustahadah; apparently if it stops for a short time, she is not a mustahadah. In al-Kafi, there is contrary to that, for it says that one becomes a person of excuse only if he does not find in a prayer time a period in which to perform wudu free from hadath. In al-Tabyin, the more apparent is contrary to al-Kafi. In Fath al-Qadir, what is in al-Kafi is suitable as an interpretation of what is in others, since it is rare that a complete time continues without stopping for a moment, leading to its negation except possibly, unlike the side of health, for its stopping can last a complete time. In Sharh al-Durar wa al-Ghurar of Manla Khasru: There is no contradiction between what is in most books and what is in al-Kafi, for the commentators of al-Jami al-Khalati said in explanation of his statement: 'Because the removal of excuse is established by occupying the time like its establishment, complete stoppage is considered in removing the concession for the excused person, and short stoppage is not considered by consensus, so a distinguishing limit was needed, so we estimated it by a prayer time just as we estimated by it the initial establishment of the excuse, for initially the flow must continue for the entire time.' In Sharh al-Tanwir: 'The excused person's purity remains during the time under two conditions: if he performs wudu for his excuse and no other hadath occurs. If he performs wudu for another hadath and his excuse is stopped then it flows, or performs wudu for his excuse then another hadath occurs, then his purity does not remain.' This is explicit that flow without exit of time is a nullifier, but it is not so as you have known from the explicit transmission, so beware. Then I saw in al-Qahistani what is explicit in that: 'If a woman has istihadah and the time of Asr enters while the blood is stopped, she performs wudu and prays Asr, then blood flows in this time, her wudu is not nullified.' Then after a while I saw what removes the confusion and clarifies the situation: that the author of al-Minya has...
Source pages p. 375

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, deals with the rulings of the person with a chronic excuse (صاحب عذر) such as mustahadah (one with irregular bleeding) regarding the validity of wudu and the continuation of the excuse status. The author begins by stating that the wudu of such a person becomes invalid only at the exit of the prayer time, not at the entry, and this is conditional upon the hadath (bleeding) being present during that time. He then discusses the reasoning from Fath al-Qadir, which suggests that the command for them to perform wudu at each time is one of recommendation (istihbab) rather than obligation, due to doubt about nullification. However, the author of al-Siraj al-Wahhaj considers it obligatory because the person is truly excused. The commentary then explains that attributing invalidation to the exit of time is metaphorical; the real nullifier is the occurrence of the hadath, not the mere passage of time. Hence, such a person cannot wipe over socks after the time if the excuse existed at wudu, nor can they build upon a previous prayer if the time exits while they are in prayer. The text also addresses the difference between an excused person and a menstruating woman: a menstruating woman cannot exit her state by blocking the blood, but an excused person can potentially lose the excuse if they can control the bleeding through binding. The passage then cites al-Jami' al-Kabir by al-Sarakhsi, explaining that the nullifier of the mustahadah's purity is the combination of blood flow and exit of time; neither alone is sufficient. This leads to a discussion of when the wudu actually becomes invalid: if the person performed wudu while bleeding was occurring, or if bleeding started after wudu, then at the exit of time it invalidates. But if the bleeding was stopped throughout the time and only after the exit does it start, then the wudu remains valid provided no other hadath occurs. The text then presents an intra-Hanafi disagreement: according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), nullification occurs only at the exit of time; according to Abu Yusuf, it occurs at either entry or exit; according to Zufar, only at entry. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the first. The second major topic is the condition for the excuse to persist: if a complete prayer time passes without any bleeding, the person ceases to be excused. The initial establishment of the excuse requires that bleeding occupy an entire prayer time, but for its continuation, it suffices that bleeding occurs at least once within each prayer time, even if for a short duration. The text notes differences among scholars regarding the strictness of the initial condition, with some requiring continuous bleeding throughout the first time, while others allow gaps small enough to prevent performing wudu without bleeding. The author sides with the view that the excuse is established if the person cannot find a period within the prayer time to perform wudu free from hadath. Practical examples: if a person performs wudu before sunrise for Duha prayer, the wudu remains valid until the exit of Zuhr time, not at its entry. If they perform wudu in Zuhr time for Asr prayer, it becomes invalid only at the exit of Zuhr time. The commentary concludes with a note from Sharh al-Tanwir that the excused person's purity remains only if they perform wudu for the excuse and no new hadath occurs; if they perform wudu for another reason or another hadath occurs, the purity does not remain. However, the author warns that a statement in Sharh al-Tanwir might be misunderstood to imply that flow alone (without exit of time) is a nullifier, whereas the correct position is that both are required.

Key Terms
صاحب عذر (sahib 'udhr): A person who suffers from a chronic or persistent hadath (such as istihadah, a wound that constantly oozes, or a dripping urine) that prevents them from maintaining purity for an entire prayer time.
مستحاضة (mustahadah): A woman who experiences non-menstrual bleeding (istihadah) that continues beyond the normal days of menstruation or occurs irregularly.
سيلان (sayalan): The flow of blood or other liquid from the body; the state of bleeding that nullifies wudu when combined with exit of time.
انقطاع (inqita'): The ceasing of the hadath (e.g., stoppage of bleeding) for a period.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) Hanafi position, when does the wudu of a mustahadah become invalid?
A) At the entry of the prayer time
B) At the exit of the prayer time
C) At both entry and exit
D) Only when bleeding occurs regardless of time

Key Takeaway
The wudu of an excused person is invalidated only at the exit of the prayer time, and only if bleeding occurs at that time or after wudu.

Taharah — Purification
advanced
10 min
Conditions for the Excuse: Establishment and Persistence
Discusses the conditions for establishing and maintaining the excuse status.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for a person to be considered excused (sahib 'udhr) and explain when the excuse status ceases.

Core Idea
The excuse is established if the hadath occupies an entire prayer time initially, and it persists as long as no complete prayer time passes without the hadath.

Having understood when the wudu of an excused person becomes invalid, we now turn to the crucial question: who qualifies as excused? The Hanafi school specifies clear conditions for both the initial establishment and the continuation of the excuse. Misunderstanding these can lead to unnecessary complications in worship.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish Initial and Continuing Conditions
The passage differentiates between the condition for initially becoming a sahib 'udhr and the condition for remaining one. The initial condition is more stringent.
2
Analyze the Initial Condition
The hadath must occupy the entire first prayer time, from beginning to end, or at least the person cannot find a period within that time to perform wudu free from hadath. The majority view requires continuous flow.
Some authorities allow brief interruptions that do not permit complete wudu.
3
Analyze the Persistence Condition
The excuse continues as long as no complete prayer time passes without the hadath. Even a short presence of the hadath within each time suffices to maintain the status.
If a full time passes without any hadath, the excuse ceases.
4
Note the Difference of Opinion
There is a difference among scholars: some (like al-Kafi) require that the person cannot find a clean period for wudu, which is less strict. The majority requires continuous flow. The author reconciles these views.
The conditional aspect is that strict continuity is rare; the practical condition is that the hadath prevents complete purification for the entire time.
5
Apply to a Scenario
Given a woman whose bleeding stops for a few minutes in Zuhr time, determine if she qualifies as excused and whether she remains excused. Consider both initial and persistence conditions.
If she is already excused, brief stops do not remove the excuse unless they last a full prayer time.

Book of Purity - Chapter of Menstruation. And they pray with it obligatory and supererogatory, and it becomes invalid only by its exit, and this is when no obligatory time has passed upon them except that the [hadath] exists in it. Fath al-Qadir: I say this reasoning implies it is a recommended matter, because doubt and possibility of its being nullifying does not necessitate ruling of nullification, since certainty is not removed by doubt. Yes, if it is known by way of predominant probability from doctors' reports or signs that overcome the afflicted person's assumption, then it is obligatory. It is good, but it is stated in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj that he is a person of excuse, so the command is for obligation. His statement: (And it becomes invalid only by its exit) i.e., it does not become invalid by its entry, and his intent is that the previous hadath appears at its exit, so attributing invalidation to exit is metaphorical because the exit has no actual effect on nullification. Therefore, they are not allowed to wipe over socks after the time if the excuse existed at the time of wudu or wearing, nor to build if the time exits while they are in prayer. The appearance of the previous hadath at that point is restricted entirely to actualization, not that it is attributed to the beginning of the time. Hence, if an excused person begins a supererogatory prayer then the time exits, he must make it up; if its appearance were attributed, he would not have to. Because what is meant by its appearance is that that hadath is ruled to be raised until a known limit, so it appears at that time restricted, not that its legal existence appears from that. In al-Bazzaziyya: 'If a mustahadah or a wounded person or one who is cupped is able to prevent blood by bandaging and to prevent dampness by a cloth tied, then it is necessary and he is like a healthy person. If he cannot prevent the dampness, then he is a person of excuse, unlike a menstruating woman who does not exit from being menstruating by tying.' The apparent statement of al-Minya: 'The person of excuse, if he prevents the blood from exiting by treatment, exits from being a person of excuse, and for this meaning the one who is cupped is not a person of excuse, unlike a menstruating woman who, if she stuffs herself, does not exit from being menstruating.' In his words 'and for this meaning the one who is cupped etc.' is evidence for what we presented in nullifiers of wudu from al-Shurunbulali: that the person who cauterizes a wart is not a person of excuse, but rather one looks at that exiting substance: if it has the power to flow by itself, it is impure, nullifying wudu, and washing it is obligatory, and prayer is not permissible while it flows even if it occupies a complete time; otherwise it does not nullify and is pure even if it hits a liquid, contrary to Muhammad. His statement: (Then it only invalidates by its exit, etc.) This indicates that the invalidator is not merely the exit of time but rather with the flow. And it is supported by what is in al-Jami al-Kabir by Shams al-Aimma al-Sarakhsi: 'If a mustahadah performs wudu in the time of Asr while the blood is stopped and prays two rakats, then the time of Maghrib enters, then blood flows, she must perform wudu and build upon her prayer because the nullification of purity was due to the hadath not due to exit of time, and she did not perform any part of the prayer after the hadath, so it is permissible for her to build. And this is because the exit of time itself is not a hadath, but purity is nullified at the exit of time by a flow concomitant with purity or existing after it, and if it does not exist then it is not nullified by exit of time.' Then he said: 'The summary of this speech is that the nullifier of the mustahadah's purity are two things: the flow of blood and the exit of time. Then if the flow of blood is isolated from exit of time, it is not a nullifier, and likewise if the exit of time is isolated from blood flow, because the ruling attached to a cause with two attributes is absent by the absence of one of the attributes.' Similarly in al-Nihaya and Mirqat al-Diraya. And with this the statement of Sheikh Ala al-Din al-Haskafi becomes clear. ... Then it only invalidates by its exit if they perform wudu while there is flow, or flow occurs after wudu. However, if it is while it is stopped and it continues until the exit of time, then it does not invalidate by the exit as long as no other hadath occurs or her blood does not flow. And it informs that if one performs wudu after sunrise even for Eid or Duha, according to the sound view it is not nullified except by the exit of Zuhr time, not by its entry, unlike Abu Yusuf; and that if he performs wudu before sunrise, it is nullified by sunrise by agreement, unlike Zufar; and that if he performs wudu in Zuhr time for Asr, it becomes invalid by the exit of Zuhr time according to the sound view. The conclusion is that it is nullified by exit, not by entry, according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad); according to Abu Yusuf, by whichever occurs; according to Zufar, by entry only. His statement: (And this is when no obligatory time has passed upon them except that the hadath exists in it) i.e., the ruling of istihadah and excuse remains only if no prayer time passes upon its people without the hadath that they suffer from existing in it, even if little. So if it stops for a complete time, they exit from being excused. We restricted it to being a condition of continuity because the condition for its initial establishment is that it occupies a complete time. As in most books. In al-Nihaya, it is a condition initially that the flow continues from beginning to end of the time, analogously to istihada, for it is not complete unless it stops for the entire time. In the commentary of Shaykh Hamid al-Din al-Darrir, the condition initially is that the hadath be the entire time, even if it does not occupy the whole time, she is not a mustahadah; apparently if it stops for a short time, she is not a mustahadah. In al-Kafi, there is contrary to that, for it says that one becomes a person of excuse only if he does not find in a prayer time a period in which to perform wudu free from hadath. In al-Tabyin, the more apparent is contrary to al-Kafi. In Fath al-Qadir, what is in al-Kafi is suitable as an interpretation of what is in others, since it is rare that a complete time continues without stopping for a moment, leading to its negation except possibly, unlike the side of health, for its stopping can last a complete time. In Sharh al-Durar wa al-Ghurar of Manla Khasru: There is no contradiction between what is in most books and what is in al-Kafi, for the commentators of al-Jami al-Khalati said in explanation of his statement: 'Because the removal of excuse is established by occupying the time like its establishment, complete stoppage is considered in removing the concession for the excused person, and short stoppage is not considered by consensus, so a distinguishing limit was needed, so we estimated it by a prayer time just as we estimated by it the initial establishment of the excuse, for initially the flow must continue for the entire time.' In Sharh al-Tanwir: 'The excused person's purity remains during the time under two conditions: if he performs wudu for his excuse and no other hadath occurs. If he performs wudu for another hadath and his excuse is stopped then it flows, or performs wudu for his excuse then another hadath occurs, then his purity does not remain.' This is explicit that flow without exit of time is a nullifier, but it is not so as you have known from the explicit transmission, so beware. Then I saw in al-Qahistani what is explicit in that: 'If a woman has istihadah and the time of Asr enters while the blood is stopped, she performs wudu and prays Asr, then blood flows in this time, her wudu is not nullified.' Then after a while I saw what removes the confusion and clarifies the situation: that the author of al-Minya has...
Source pages p. 375

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, deals with the rulings of the person with a chronic excuse (صاحب عذر) such as mustahadah (one with irregular bleeding) regarding the validity of wudu and the continuation of the excuse status. The author begins by stating that the wudu of such a person becomes invalid only at the exit of the prayer time, not at the entry, and this is conditional upon the hadath (bleeding) being present during that time. He then discusses the reasoning from Fath al-Qadir, which suggests that the command for them to perform wudu at each time is one of recommendation (istihbab) rather than obligation, due to doubt about nullification. However, the author of al-Siraj al-Wahhaj considers it obligatory because the person is truly excused. The commentary then explains that attributing invalidation to the exit of time is metaphorical; the real nullifier is the occurrence of the hadath, not the mere passage of time. Hence, such a person cannot wipe over socks after the time if the excuse existed at wudu, nor can they build upon a previous prayer if the time exits while they are in prayer. The text also addresses the difference between an excused person and a menstruating woman: a menstruating woman cannot exit her state by blocking the blood, but an excused person can potentially lose the excuse if they can control the bleeding through binding. The passage then cites al-Jami' al-Kabir by al-Sarakhsi, explaining that the nullifier of the mustahadah's purity is the combination of blood flow and exit of time; neither alone is sufficient. This leads to a discussion of when the wudu actually becomes invalid: if the person performed wudu while bleeding was occurring, or if bleeding started after wudu, then at the exit of time it invalidates. But if the bleeding was stopped throughout the time and only after the exit does it start, then the wudu remains valid provided no other hadath occurs. The text then presents an intra-Hanafi disagreement: according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), nullification occurs only at the exit of time; according to Abu Yusuf, it occurs at either entry or exit; according to Zufar, only at entry. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the first. The second major topic is the condition for the excuse to persist: if a complete prayer time passes without any bleeding, the person ceases to be excused. The initial establishment of the excuse requires that bleeding occupy an entire prayer time, but for its continuation, it suffices that bleeding occurs at least once within each prayer time, even if for a short duration. The text notes differences among scholars regarding the strictness of the initial condition, with some requiring continuous bleeding throughout the first time, while others allow gaps small enough to prevent performing wudu without bleeding. The author sides with the view that the excuse is established if the person cannot find a period within the prayer time to perform wudu free from hadath. Practical examples: if a person performs wudu before sunrise for Duha prayer, the wudu remains valid until the exit of Zuhr time, not at its entry. If they perform wudu in Zuhr time for Asr prayer, it becomes invalid only at the exit of Zuhr time. The commentary concludes with a note from Sharh al-Tanwir that the excused person's purity remains only if they perform wudu for the excuse and no new hadath occurs; if they perform wudu for another reason or another hadath occurs, the purity does not remain. However, the author warns that a statement in Sharh al-Tanwir might be misunderstood to imply that flow alone (without exit of time) is a nullifier, whereas the correct position is that both are required.

Key Terms
صاحب عذر (sahib 'udhr): A person who suffers from a chronic or persistent hadath (such as istihadah, a wound that constantly oozes, or a dripping urine) that prevents them from maintaining purity for an entire prayer time.
ثبوت (thubut): Establishment; the initial qualification as a person of excuse.
بقاء (baqa'): Continuation or persistence of the excuse status.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does a person cease to be excused (i.e., lose the status of sahib 'udhr)?
A) When bleeding stops for any length of time.
B) When a complete prayer time passes without any bleeding.
C) When bleeding stops for half a prayer time.
D) When the person recovers completely from the cause.

Key Takeaway
The excuse is established by the hadath occupying the entire first prayer time and persists as long as no complete prayer time passes without it.

intermediate

When does the Wudu of a Mustahadah Break? The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Time Entry vs Exit
Explains when wudu of a mustahadah breaks with respect to prayer time entry/exit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on when the wudu of a mustahadah breaks, distinguish the views of Abu Yusuf and Zufar, and apply the mufta bihi view to given scenarios.

Core Idea
For the mustahadah, wudu breaks only with the exit of prayer time, not its entry — the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq presents the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the time at which the wudu of a mustahadah (a woman with chronic non-menstrual bleeding) becomes invalid. The central question: does the wudu break upon the entry of a new prayer time, upon its exit, or both? The text settles on the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani that it breaks only upon exit, which is the relied-upon position for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the question and the mufta bihi position
Recognize that the ruling concerns the invalidation of wudu for a mustahadah. The mufta bihi Hanafi view (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that wudu breaks only when the prayer time exits, not upon entry.
This is the position that the text calls 'as-sahih' (the correct view).
2
Map the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf holds that wudu breaks by either entry or exit (whichever occurs first). Zufar holds that it breaks only by entry. Both differ from the mufta bihi view.
No explicit dalil is given in this passage, but the ikhtilaf is clear.
3
Analyse the practical scenarios
Apply each view to the three cases mentioned: wudu after sunrise, wudu before sunrise, and wudu within Zuhr time for Asr prayer.
For each scenario, determine when wudu breaks under each opinion.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The practical difference in rulings: a mustahadah who performs wudu after sunrise may pray all day until Zuhr exits without renewing wudu according to the mufta bihi view, but according to Abu Yusuf and Zufar she would need to renew wudu at the entry of Zuhr time.
This difference has significant implications for daily worship.
5
Identify the tarjih mechanism
The commentator uses the phrase 'on the correct view' (على الصحيح) to indicate that the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad is chosen as the mufta bihi.
This is a common method of tarjih in Hanafi texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إنما يبطل بخروجه إذا توضؤوا على السيلان أو وجد السيلان بعد الوضوء، أما إذا كان على الانقطاع ودام إلى خروج الوقت فلا يبطل بالخروج ما لم يحدث حدثاً آخر أو يسيل دمها، وأفاد أنه لو توضأ بعد طلوع الشمس ولو لعيد أو ضحى على الصحيح فلا تنتقض إلا بخروج وقت الظهر لا بدخوله خلافاً لأبي يوسف وأنه لو توضأ قبل الطلوع انتقض بالطلوع اتفاقاً خلافاً لزفر، وأنه لو توضأ في وقت الظهر للعصر بطل بخروج وقت الظهر على الصحيح. فالحاصل أنه ينتقض بالخروج لا بالدخول عندهما، وعند أبي يوسف بأيهما وجد، وعند زفر بالدخول فقط.
Then it (wudu) is only invalidated by its (time) exit if they perform wudu while flowing or if flowing occurs after wudu. But if it (flow) is stopped and remains until the time exits, then it is not invalidated by the exit unless a hadath occurs or her blood flows. And it benefits that if she performs wudu after sunrise, even for Eid or Duha, according to the correct view, it is not invalidated except by the exit of Zuhr time, not by its entry, contra Abu Yusuf. And that if she performs wudu before sunrise, it is invalidated by sunrise by agreement, contra Zufar. And if she performs wudu in Zuhr time for Asr, it is invalidated by the exit of Zuhr time according to the correct view. In summary: it is invalidated by exit, not entry, according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), and according to Abu Yusuf by whichever occurs, and according to Zufar only by entry.
Source pages p. 376

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with intra-Hanafi dispute. The commentator explains when the wudu of a mustahadah (woman with chronic bleeding) is invalidated by the passage of time. The key principle: wudu performed while blood is flowing (on al-sayalan) breaks when the prayer time exits. If wudu was performed while blood had stopped (on al-inqita') and it remains stopped until the time exits, the wudu does not break unless another hadath occurs or bleeding resumes. The commentator then illustrates with cases: if wudu after sunrise, it remains valid until Zuhr time exits (not by its entry), contra Abu Yusuf who says it breaks by either entry or exit. If wudu before sunrise, it breaks at sunrise (agreed). If wudu within Zuhr time for Asr prayer, it breaks at exit of Zuhr. The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is that wudu breaks only with exit (the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani).

Key Terms
المستحاضة (al-mustahadah): Woman with chronic non-menstrual bleeding (istihadah)
الوقت (al-waqt): Prayer time, specifically the time for a fard prayer

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, when does the wudu of a mustahadah break if she performed wudu after sunrise?
A) At sunrise
B) At the entry of Zuhr time
C) At the exit of Zuhr time
D) At the entry of Asr time

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi Hanafi view is that a mustahadah's wudu breaks only with the exit of prayer time, not its entry.
